When the solution of the belly comes from cold and moisture, so that the retentive and digestive virtues which are in the stomach and intestines are debilitated, and cannot be cured by means of cures; and you see the patient suffering and having great virtue, then make one great cautery on the stomach according to what has been said before about the cauterization of the stomach, at the circulatory cautery; and three subtle cauterizations around the belly, each one as fine as a key, and two cauterizations on the haunches.
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et .i. cautere sus chaicun yle, et .ij. petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	And if you see the moistors abundant and the patient suffering, then make a cautery on the navel, and one on each vertebra, and two small cauterizations on the stomach near the great one, because the cure is beneficial when there is good aid.
de la cure des emorroydes	of the cure of hemorrhoids
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: .iij. sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et .i. cautere desoz la boude. ij. dois;	When the hemorrhoids are in the fundament, or one or more, and are ancient and are made up of cold and moist corrupted humors, and are cured as we have said in divisions, but it does not benefit, then make cauterizations: three on the spine of the back, that which is entirely behind below almecdate, and gradually tapering, and one cautery under the belly. Two are necessary;
et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on .i. grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et .i. autre sus le foie, et i. autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens. Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you think that the stomach is chilled, and the meat does not cook, and one sees the face swell, then make one great cautery on the stomach, as has been said before, and another on the liver, and another on the mouse, all the way to the end of the cautery; and let the cautery stay open for a long time. After that, cure the patient until he is healed.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	of the charnosity which is called "Thelul"
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou .ij., et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you cope with Thelul, heat the cautery which seems like a razor, and then place it all ablaze on that coped Thelul; and I leave your hand there until the cauterization reaches the birth of the vein, so that the blood does not flow. Do this once or twice, and if there is much Thelul, make each one as we have said; after which perform cures that are beneficial for a long time until they are healed; and if you cauterize with a great cautery on the Alchatim, it will have greater aid.
de plaie mal curee	of an uncured wound
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot endure cutting or opening, as we will tell in its place, then comes such a disease that cannot be healed except by cauterization.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont. Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou .ij. ou .iij., selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes. se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	When to someone comes a fistula, and it is inflamed and discharges corrupt matter and moisture, you should prove the entire tent subtlety, and take care that you know exactly how deep the tent has entered. After that, heat the cautery which seems like a razor, and put it in the fistula according to the quantity of the tent that has entered, and continue the cautery until the corrupted flesh is burned away, once, twice, or thrice, depending on the quantity of what is needed; and beware of burning the nerves that are nearby, and the great veins. If the fistula goes into the bladder and intestines, take care to avoid those places, and do not make a fire except in a charred place, and think that it is not perilous; after which cure the wound until it is healed, and if the wound is seared, and the matter has been removed for a long time, then know that the wound is entirely healed; and if the matter is not removed, know that the wound is torn, and corrupts the bone at its root; and thus as one of those who we will tell about in their place.
de la maladie des reins	From the disease of the kidneys
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra .iij. cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	When pain of cold comes to the kidneys, and great windy-ness, and it does not take the shape of a woman, then it is necessary that you make a fire cautery on the kidneys from one side and the other at the cauterizing key that we have mentioned before; and if we were to cauterize in medium, there would be .iii. cauteries in line, and they will make more great help.
de la vessie	Of the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et .i. a destre et .i. a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais .i. cautere defuers le dos, ou .ij. se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the bladder is soft and weak from cold and moisture, so that the patient retains urine, then make a fire cautery on the part outside of the bladder, where the hairs begin to grow at the point of the finger, and one on the right and one on the left, each being as long as a nose's width; and make one cautery behind the back, or two if you need them; and let the cauterizing key be according to the form mentioned before.
de la marris	Of the uterus
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice .iij. cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et .ij. cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	When the uterus is cold and moist, and does not permit conception, and the flowers are corrupted and their terms late; and when they come, one feels great pain: then it is necessary that three cauterizations be made around the belly, as we have said in the cautery of the bladder, and two cauterizations behind the back; and let the cauterizing key be, as we have said.
de la hainche	Of the groin
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a .i. cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When the viscous moisture descends to the groin of the haunch, and because of this it moves out of its place, and the sign is that the hip is longer than the other when measured together; and one finds the signs of departure visible, then it is necessary that you cauterize the patient on the groin of the haunch at one cautery similar to a circle, and sign before the line around the groin as it turns, so that the groin is inside the circle; and let the cauterizations be such as those for which we have cauterized the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai .iij. cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if these cauterizations are not present, then make three large cauterizations of the olive-like ones, and let the cauterizations be as deep as all the keys; and heal until it is sound.
de la dolor de la hainche	Of the pain of the groin
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain comes to the groin of the haunch, and it is from coldness and moisture, and the patient is treated as we have said in the division, but the cure does not hold, and the disease is old: then it is necessary that you purge the patient of thick humors with fetid pills or other good-smelling pills similar.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc .ij. manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu. Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche .iij. cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a .iiij. selonc ceste forme:	Then you make a cautery; and the manner of the cautery is according to two manners: that is to say, together medicines burning and fire cautery. Fire cautery is according to many manners, one of which is: that you cauterize on the groin of the haunch three triangular cauterizations in this form, and make good profundity and great, and have between each cauterization a space as wide as an egg, and let the cauterizations be olive-like; sometimes one makes a cautery in medium on the head of the haunch, because of which there are four according to this form:
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you see, then cauterize at the cautery of the circle that we have mentioned before in the dislocation of the haunch; but make it in this manner so that the circles contain all the haunch, and all the spikes of the key are burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe. Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai .ij. cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et .i. cautere desus la cheville .iiij. dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor .iij. poins ou .iiij. au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And this is the manner in which one operates in sciatica, when the pain stays in the haunch and does not reach as far as the hip or leg. And if it comes to the hip and leg, then make two cauterizations there where the patient says that the pain lies, and one cauterization above the ankle four finger-breadths on the left side; and let the cauterizations be cutellate, and let the spikes of the key be burned; and if the patient feels that the pain extends as far as two fingers of the foot or almost there, then cauterize where they feel the pain three or four points at the cautery which is called "points".
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if it is necessary, make more; and if it seems that the pain is under the knee towards the hip, then make a cautery at the cutellate or circular cautery, and take good care in all your cauterizations that you do not leave the cautery so long that you burn the nerves and great arteries, and that you do not cause more great nuisance and contraction to the patient.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez. Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	And I myself have seen many who have made a cautery on the ankle of the foot, and left it so long that the leg was all swollen, and the feet also, and were pierced and corrupted all over the feet. After a purging of the belly which led to his death.
Et se li dolors est en .ij. parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere. // Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai .i. tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de .ij. pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait .i. mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	And if the pains are in two parts together, make a cautery on one and on the other, according to this manner.
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois .i. cautere reont et lou laisse .iij. jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let it be scalded until it is completely red and gives off an odor; then place it on the withered flesh of the afflicted person, and turn it around to the healthy side; and cauterize once a fire cauterization, and leave it three days; then make an embalming with butter, and leave the wound open for a long time; after the ointment cure until it is healed.
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	Albucasim says that we use this cauterization for the fear of his gaze, and if we see none who uses it; and yet it is good cauterizations, which can endure it, and where it applies.
de la dolor dou dos	of the pain of the back
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, whether from falling or striking or excessive evacuation or similar signs of cold matter spreading, none of these similarities is worth cauterization, except for that which comes from the infusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne .v. cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary after this that the patient be voided of fetid pills or similar things, and then one makes marks on the back, where the pain holds, three lines marked in ink, and in each line five cauterizations or more according to the virtue and quantity that the patient can endure; and the cauterization is done according to the "point" cauterization; and if you see, make three cauterizations or four at the cauterized middle point according to this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	This disease often comes to small children, and the signs of its beginning are that they have a thin line when they arise, and fear; and you find in the last vertebra of the back and in us the appearance which comes on the other vertebrae.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and you see it cured, then cauterize it with the "celcle" cauterization according to this form.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument. Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant .ij. lignes ou .iij., et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre. Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	And so the cauterization should prick each part of the vertebra equally. And if you see, then cauterize around the vertebra with the piercing cauterization two lines or three, and let the points be near one another. After the cure is complete until it is healed according to what we have said, and beware that you do not apply a cauterization in gibbosity which is in spasms of nerve.
de la dolor des jointes	of the pain of the joints
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When the pain of joints is from moistors that are spread to each member of the body, and when the pain comes in the feet, which the doctors properly call "podagre", and when it is from a cold cause and medicines do not cure it, then it is cured by cauterizations in this manner: make a great number of cauterizations around the joint of the foot, and let the cauterizations be olive-like according to this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point». Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if it is necessary that you prick on the face of the foot, then make a cauterization for all the "point" cauterization. And if the pains come up to the knees and at other joints, and this often happens, then make a cauterization on each knee three or four times, with all the olive-like cauterization; and if you need more, then make more, but do not keep your hand there longer than until the sparks of the fire are burned.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre. Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile .ij. lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines. Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	And if the pains descend to the knees and back, administer the cauterization that we have said in its chapter. And if the pains are at the hands, then make points around the wrist two lines; and if there remains some pain at the shoulders, then make points on each joint and on the hair of the hand; and if the pains come to the ribs or to the shoulders, then cauterize each part, and make good governance with the patient and take medicines. For if you make good governance and purge phlegm, it will be healed by the aid of God.
de la routure dou syfac	of the running of the itch
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When itch running comes to the armpits, and the boils descend to the groin and this is new, it is necessary that when you see it cured, it does not annoy him on that day; and that he uses things which loosen his bowels, so that the worms descend from his belly; after make him sit on his back between your hands, and command him to hold his arm straight until the boils are repaired, and then reattach them to your fingers, and sign with ink below the itch running on the bone of the pointing finger, and make a sign like the half of a circle above the body; then scald the cauterization in this form:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles. Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui .i. cussin et .i. serjant sus les cuisses, et .i. autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	until it is white and gives off an odor. Then reattach the boils to their place; and let the minister hold his hand on so that they do not return backward; and work well on the patient's hips, and put under him one cushion and one servant on the hips, and another on the chest which holds his hands; then put the cauterization on the sign with your entire hand, and hold it straight and hold until you reach the bone, and if you do not reach it at first, start again once more until you reach the bone; and take care subtly that the boil does not burst when you make the cauterization; that you do not burn him; and that through this the patient does not die or suffer another evil.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien. Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés .iij. jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides .xl. jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And know that when you do not reach the bone with the cauterization, your efforts are worth nothing. And it is necessary that the cauterizations of children be subtle according to their measure, and of great people also as great according to their measure; after three days, cure the wound of butter until the scabbing is removed; after use other ointments until he is healed, and let the patient lie on his back for 40 days until the wound is well closed; and it is necessary that his nourishments be given long enough so that the boil does not burst when he gets up to go to chambers.
Et aprés .xl. jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse .xl. autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement. Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And after 40 days, when he wants to get up, give him a bandage well made, and wear it for 40 other days; and have good rest, so that he does not trouble himself much and beware of too great excess in drinking and eating, and too high shouting; and when he has learned this lesson, then is healed entirely. And I will say hereafter the cure of cutting in its chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	of the running of the belly
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai .j. cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a .iij. angles selonc ceste forme:	When runs come to other bellies and are known, and you see that they no longer grow, then make one cauterization of the same quantity as before, and let the third spark of fire be burned; after cure according to what we have said; and some of the ancients have said that it should be cauterized at three angles according to this form:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile. Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	but sign the first one on the joint and make two lines above and below the running, and place your hand in the middle of all the cauterization to clamp it tight. But the first cauterizations are lighter and more subtle.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of ancient pain in any member
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor. s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence .i. autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	When pain comes to any member, whether from falling or striking, and that pain lasts long times, and the cure of medicine is not worth it, then it is necessary to be cauterized with the fire that is called "points", and the cauteries should be according to the length of the member, its thinness, weakness, virtue, and location of twists and pain. If one is healed from the first cautery, it is good; if not, begin another cautery on top of that one, because such a case is that it must change in the member that is nearest, so you should do the cauteries until the patient is healed.
de meselerie	of menstruation
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie. Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai .v. cauteres sus lou chief: .i. emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et .ij. sus les .ij. cornes, et .i. derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	The menstruations are helped sometimes by cautery with great aid, and even the disease that comes from the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy. When you see it being cauterized, take care if the disease is at its beginning, and if it is cured according to what we have said in the division, and does not descend or remain, and you doubt that the corruption will spread throughout the patient, then do 5 cauteries on the head: 1 inside the head by the nose, and another towards the forehead to the end of the eyebrows; and 2 on the 2 horns, and 1 behind on the forehead; and leave your hand there until the cautery comes up to the bone, and so that the scabs come out if the vapors of thick humors can escape; and cauterize on the mouse according to what it is beforehand.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.	And if the menstruations are everywhere scattered and manifestly failing, then it is necessary that you cauterize on the head with those cauteries we have said, and 1 on the neck, and 2 on the spine of the back, and 6 on the spine of the back, and 1 great one on the scapula and another below, and 2 on the shoulders; and 2 on the sides, and 2 on the tendons of the chest, and 1 on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the hollows of the hands; and beware of the nerves that are on the back part of the scalp, lest you burn them. And sometimes make a cautery on the bone of the elbow, and another on the bone of the stomach, and another on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus. Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers. Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	And know that the more I make of cautery, the more it brings aid and moves the profit; and know that the patient does not feel pain from the cautery as healthy people do, because the body is already quite corrupted. And it is necessary that the cauteries be great and small according to the members and joints, according to what you will find in manners of iron. After the cure, let the place be covered with flour and honey and other cures until it is healed.
de enfleure	of swelling
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez. Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	When swelling comes to any member and is cured by medicines and oils and plasters, and it is not yet healed, then one does cauteries on the member according to the size and smallness of the member; and let the cauteries be a little bit entering into the space of the joint. Then treat with ointments until it is healed. And sometimes make a cautery at the hand and foot and back, at the end of the nerve that moves the member, and thus the swelling is removed; but nevertheless no one should meddle in this unless they are knowledgeable about the members and the issues of the nerves moving the body.
de albaras	of ulcers
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease that is called "ulcers" is advanced, and the skill of medicine is worth nothing, then one cauterizes with a cautery a little bit deep, according to the quantity of the space of the joint, until the pus is removed, and its color is changed; then treat with flour of vetches and lentils with rose oil and plantain leaves, and blood of colander and of alder, each part separately; and mix everything together, and bind it with a cloth, and apply it to the wound until it is healed.
li cure de chancre par cautere	the treatment of chance by cauterization
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble .i. cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.  Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	When chance comes at the beginning and you see it stopping, then cauterize around the chancre with a circle-shaped cautery, all around the edge of the chancre. And although wise men say that one should make a cautery also in the middle of the chancre; and although this does not seem to me good, for I fear that it will be ulcerated and corrupted, and I have seen it happen once or twice; and more rightly is that it be cauterized around, with the circle-shaped cautery, as we have said in many cases.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the swelling that cannot be killed
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi. Car elle se hastera de meureir.	When someone has a disease that is called "adubelati", and it will not die or because of the superfluity it makes or because of the age of the patient when he is decrepit (that is, too old) and he has little blood, or because of the time; and you see it hastening to die: then cauterize around with many small cauteries that are painful; afterwards leave it so. For it will hasten to die.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see it piercing through the whole cautery, then heat the cautery with what is called "the form":
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis. Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And put your hand in the middle of that disease which is called "adubelati" until the cauteries have pierced the joint, and be such cauteries that the patient feels them outside in this way that the flow of pus is blocked. Afterwards treat until it is healed perfectly.
li cure dou feu par fer	the treatment by fire with iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches. Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit. Et puis le laisse .iij. jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption. Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.  Et se tu vois aprés .iij. jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus. Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	Another way of disease is called "corrodens", and it's nothing but a consumption of member, for it consumes members just like fire dries up dry leaves. If you see this disease in a place that can suffer both cautery and fire, then heat the cauteries with a small and large hammer, according to what is needed at the place where the disease is; afterwards cauterize all around until you remove all corruption, and nothing remains except what is corrupted. And then leave it for 3 days, and put on top of the burned areas soothing ointment with oil until the scorched areas are removed, and all corruption gone. Afterwards treat with ointments engendering flesh. And if after 3 days you see no healthy flesh growing, that's good; but if not, then start again the cautery on what remains of the corrupted areas. And this consumption has sometimes been cured by medicine in place of cauterization with fire; but nonetheless, cauterization with fire is of greater help, and I have already said the treatment of medicine in division: take it when you need it.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	of boils that come to the feet
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet. Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc .ij. manieres. C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude. Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe .i. cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi .iij. jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines. Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Mout de fois avient que as piez par defeurs naist une maladie qui est apelee "clos" selonc nostre entencion, and est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines. Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	Et s'il sont convertit par défauts lo cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d'eau chaude;
li cure dou trembler	The cure of the trembling
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres ou .iv. sus l’espinee dou dos, .i. cautere entre chescune espinee; et .i. cautere ou pez, et .i. sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When some people tremble from cold or numbness, or quartan fever or another, it is necessary that you do four cauterizations or five on the spine of the back, one cauterization between each spine; and one cauterization on the hip, and one on the stomach at the olive-cauterization; if the trembling ceases, and the patient's health will hasten from the cold disease.
des pustules puans	of foul pustules
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues. si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire. Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	Sometimes boils or foul pustules appear on the bathed body, coming from gross corrupted matters. If it is necessary when they appear to make a cauterization on each head of the pustule: one subtle cauterization made of myrtle wood, so that the point be seized by fire, or of long aristologe root, or at the lenticular cauterization. And sometimes we cauterize them at the beginning when they appear, in this manner, and they cannot grow any further forward, but are broken up the superfluitous matter from which they come, and are healed; but it is necessary that this be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	when the artery is cut off
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Many times there is great bleeding of blood from the artery that is cut off at the wound that comes before, or at the incision of an abscess, or at the cauterization of a limb, and similar things; and it is very grievous to stanch.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren .i., ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And whenever this happens to someone, if you hurry and put your two fingers on the wound of the vein, and hold them very tightly until the blood is calmed below your fingers, and no more drips out; then put some small and large olive cauterizations in the fire, so that they are all red; then take one, either large or small according to the wound and its location where the artery is severed, and place it on the vein or on what you are holding with your fingers, and hold the cauterization until the blood is staunched.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it bursts forth when you lift your fingers from the vein, and the cauterization has cooled, then take quickly one other of the cauterizations that are in the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not cease to do this one after the other until the blood is staunched; and beware that you do not burn the nerve that is nearby, nor let any other evil come upon the patient; and know that when blood pours from an artery, it cannot be well staunched unless by one of the three manners we have said: or by cauterization, or by extraction when it has not been treated, or by strong bandaging with thread, or by medicines applied which have power to stanch blood; and let it be bound and restrained accordingly.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Whoever thinks to stanch blood by binding tightly with cloths or putting hot things on it, or other similar things, will not profit unless the cauterization is not good.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to someone and he has no mirror or medicine present, then he should put his two fingers on the wound of the vein just as we have said, and press tightly until it is staunched above the wound and the vein; and do not move unless he moistens with cold water frequently when it is very cold so that the blood may congeal and thicken and be staunched; and make a note ahead of time of what cauterizations and medicines will be needed.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here begins the second book of surgical cures
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have told you in the first chapter about every disease in which it is necessary to cauterize with fire or hot medicine, and the causes and the forms of the cauteries; and I have placed that chapter at the beginning up to here, and I will proceed with this chapter by the same way so that what one wants to find may be found more easily.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And therefore as I begin this, dear friend, you should know that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first of the cauteries, and for that reason it is necessary to take greater caution.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	See previous translation.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie. Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures. si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	And I warn you not to embark on folly. For many kinds of people come to cures. Some come with such a grave illness that they will die quickly because of the severity of their disease and the great evil of their malady; and one should have fear of these.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse. Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	And of these there are some who give you their sense and say: "Wait, I am healed"; but the disease is spiteful. It is not necessary that you consent to those who come to you with this manner, but put greater caution in your honor than in your covetousness, and do not act foolishly but wisely about what you are certain of and can grasp; and use prognostication and indication in the cures of your patients so that salvation may be converted; and this will help you to acquire good reputation, glory, and memory of praise.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Very dear son, May Our Lord give you good understanding and straightness, and if you wish to be filled with the holy inspiration of His hand, Amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Now I have finished this chapter by dividing it into chapters, according to what is before the chapter of cauterizations, which I have divided from the beginning up to here, so that you may find more easily what you will need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	from the full head with water
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	Know that this disease often afflicts children during childbirth, and when the midwife holds too tightly the head of the child; and sometimes it comes from an unknown cause.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen this disease occur except in children, and all those that I have seen it affect soon died; and therefore it seems to me that it is not worth my while to continue working on such cures.
Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw one child whose head was full of water, and the skull was swelling every day until it could no longer be supported; and believed so much moisture that he would die, and this moisture is gathered under the bone above the spine, between the brain and the bone; and the operation is such that if the moisture is between the brain and the bone, and the abscesses are small, you cut open a large incision in the head; and it should be as long as two measures, until the moisture runs; and behold here the form of the skull:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is more swollen and the abscesses are larger, then make two incisions in the shape of a cross, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief .iij. fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is below the bone, and you see signs that each part's corners of the head are opened, and the liquid jumps far when you press it with your hand from inside, and this is not responding to you: then you must cut into the head three cuts in this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers. Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	And after the incision, extract all the moisture. After that, bind up the cuts with cloths and powders, and put wine and oil in, and leave it like this until the fifth day; then loosen it, and treat the wound with tents and anointings, and let the head be drained equally, and then feed the patient dried meat without moisture as long as the member is comforted and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another way of incision is that you look at where the aposteme opens up and the liquid assembles; for sometimes it is in front, sometimes behind, sometimes to the right, and sometimes to the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Cut then where the aposteme opens up and the liquid assembles, and cut according to what you have the power to do; and beware that you don't hit the artery; and if there is a flow of blood, so that the patient dies from the lack of blood and the evacuation of moisture.
de reume	of the joint
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les .ij. arteres.	When it happens to someone with a disease called "catarre" in the eyes or at the liver, and the disease is ancient, and medical treatment does not help, then the last resort is fire cauterization, by cutting off the two arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout .i. drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de .ij. pars. tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	Then it is necessary that when you see the arteries cut, the patient makes their head go back; after that, they rub the area with a rough cloth until the arteries appear, then pull the patient's neck back as far as one cloth; then look where the vein bites, and the paths of one and the other are afterward the ears, and they are not responsive; then mark the paths with an incision, then cut both with a sharp instrument that is two fingers wide, until the knife comes to the bone, and this should be done by the width of the head.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com .ij. dois au traver.	And if you see, push the spatula under the artery and cut above it, cutting just like two fingers across.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut, blood will spring forth continuously upwards.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de .iij. dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est .vj. c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins. selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And if the artery does not open up to feeling, it is necessary that you measure the width of the space with three fingers, then mark an incision and cut to the bone; and what needs to be done about the blood is to let it flow out for six cells, and by chance a little more or less, according to how much the patient can endure, and the filling of the artery; then look at the wound: if there is still a point of syphac on the bone, cut off that which prevents apostemes from coming, then drain the wound and bind it, and apply ointment until it is healed.
de emigrainne	of migration
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When ancient migration comes, and acute catarre, due to excessive moisture of tears and heat in the temples and old-fashioned foreskin and similar things, and all medical treatments by various methods of medicine do not help him, then we extract the arteries from the temples and cauterize them, as we have counted.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of extracting them is that the patient makes their temple hairs stand back, and listens to the artery which opens in the temple, for it opens well by its pulsation, and is not responsive except in some men who are too cold; and if it is responsive, then extract the patient's neck with some cloths, then rub the area with a rough cloth, and rise the liquid of hot water until the artery appears manifestly; then take the spatula which has this shape:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des .ij. chiés. Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	Then scrape the skin lightly until you reach the artery, then pull it upwards with forceps, and separate well from the threads that are below each part; and if the artery is fine, then turn it to the point of the needle, then cut off that part according to the width of two fingers. For if it is not cut, the blood will not flow out entirely.
Et trai dou sanc des .vj. c/, jusc’a .iij.; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en .ij. leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les .ij. liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And extract the blood from six cells to three; and if the artery is large, then it is necessary that you tie it with two strong silk threads in two places, so that no bleeding comes before the wound is closed and bleeding ceases; then cut off the superfluous part that is between the two ties at the same hour, and then, if you see fit, cauterize the cautery knife to the bone until the fingers are cut; and this is the chief work, if the patient has no fever and is of hot complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For fire cauterization is a help to finish off excess moisture; that's why it is of greater aid against excess moisture.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de .ij. pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	Or it is necessary for the extraction of arteries that one fills the area with old cotton and puts on well-made tents; and when they are loosened, be careful with dry medicines that make flesh grow, and with tents, until he is healed; and if without delay from the artery as much as you work, hasten to cauterize by fire, or fill the area with vitriol and strain it in your hand until the blood is stanched; and if you don't have what's needed, put your finger on the area so that the blood congeals, and rise the area with cold water until the bleeding ceases, and be strained as much as necessary; and what is more important and lighter in the extraction of the artery is to cauterize the vein of this fire knife cutting into two parts, but the cutting should be well spaced to ward off their heat for a longer time.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the cuts are too dense, they retain less heat.
Et doit avoir entre les .ij. coutelz .i. doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les .ij. leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en .ij. leus; et soient esloigniet entre les .ij. chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it should have between the two knives one finger's width of space, and then when you have marked with an incision the two places, and take the burning iron on top until it comes to the bone, and cut the vein in two places; and they should be separated by a distance equal to the width of two fingers because it is not sewn with this cautery from end to end; and that's the form of the cautery:
des larmes	of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears of the eyes are flowing from the veins that are above the forehead bone, and medical treatment done there does not help, and you see the patient's face redden, and feel the front heat and tremble as if in a fever; and the oil is abundant and moist so that the hairs on the paper are fallen, and the papers are scorched by the heat of the tears, then it is necessary to use this cure.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai .iij. fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com .ij. doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres .ij. as .ij. costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as .ij. costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des .ij. mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de .iij. dois au traver joins;	Et l'apelerent li ancien "cure contuse"; and it is that you do for the patient who has this disease the hairs on his forehead; then make three incisions on his forehead equally according to the length of his forehead; and one of the incisions be as two lines right down the middle of the forehead, going just up to the nose, and the other two be two lines on either side of the papery skin, and take care not to cut into the arteries that are on either side of the papery skin; and keep your hand away from the continuation of the jawbone, and let each wound be the size of three fingers across the joints.
et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de .ij. pars de coi ci est li forme:	and have prepared a piece of sponge and much cloth to absorb the blood, then apply the spittle thoroughly from two parts where the shape is.
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les .ij. fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	from the incision that is below the temple just up to the second incision; and scrape out all the keratin that is between the two incisions as far as the suture that is on the bone, then make another cut from the middle incision just up to the other second one, and then extract this spittle.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	and insert into the first incision the instrument which is called "culterelle", and it is very well cutting on one side, and not cutting at all on the other side, and that's its shape.
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure. Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place the sharp side towards the fatty tissue and the dull side towards the bone, and push it until it reaches the middle incision. And cut all the vessels that descend from the head to the eyes as long as the incision is continuous down to where the keratin appears; then make another cut in the middle incision up to the other edge; and then extract the blood evenly, and press the place where the blood has been taken; then put a poultice of old cotton in each incision, and wrap it with wet cloths soaked in wine, oil, and vinegar, and take care that abscesses do not form; and on the third day, loosen the bandage, and administer great abundance of lukewarm water, then apply the basilicon ointment with rose oil, and other treatments for wounds, until they are healed.
dou reume des eulz	of the eyes.
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When someone comes to you with a cataract that is accustomed to be, and you see the eyes tense and small, and weakening the sight, and the papery skin burned; and the hair falls out, and the head in front has great pain, and the patient is exhausted; then know by these accidents that those matters and the cataract do not come from just one vein, but from many veins, and the true cure that is here is this.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large. i. poc. Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les .ij. levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And it is that you instruct the patient to lift his forehead, then make a large incision in the middle of the forehead and another one of equal size. Start from the left temple to the right temple, and let the incision be until the bone; and keep your hand away from the nerves of the temples that move at mealtime; and when the bone is exposed, then pour out all the blood onto a sponge, and then extract between the two lips of the incision and put in old cotton and linen; then wrap it with wet cloths soaked in wine and oil, and take care not to form an abscess; when it is healed, then it is necessary that you rub the bone until flesh begins to grow, then apply ointments that make flesh grow.
En teil maniere: pren .ij. parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine .iiij. parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In the same manner: take two parts of wheat flour and three parts of colophony, and make a poultice; and administer it to these wounds in order to promote flesh growth throughout.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the earplugs.
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des .iiij. choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	Everything that falls into the ears is one of three things: or grains, or beasts, or pieces of flint or similar things like iron; or seeds, such as oats, beans, peas; or flowing things like water and vinegar and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel. Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus. Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	When something like flint or another thing that doesn't belong in the ear falls into the ear and doesn't grow there, place the ear in the sun. If you see the flint, then distill a small amount of violet oil or sesame oil, then administer extraction; and make the person sneeze with condiments, and stop their nostrils when the sneezing comes, and put pieces of cloth or wool around the ear; and keep the ear above. Many times it has come out through this treatment; and if it doesn't come out, then administer extraction using fine tweezers, as follows:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it doesn't come out with the tweezers, that's good; if not, then administer extraction using a fine thread of small double loop; and if it doesn't come out through this, then make a wire chain and insert the head of the chain or the ear canal strongly, and stop what is around the chain with soft wax so that the blood cannot enter with the chain; then take it out forcibly, for many times it has come out as we have said; and if it doesn't come out in this way, then takes glue from which birds take their feathers, and puts into some instrument that is pointed to do this, and puts a small amount of cotton around; then press the glue on the flint or whatever it is, and take it out.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it doesn't come out through all these things that we have said, then you must hasten to cut the ear so that an abscess does not form and cause spasms; and the manner of cutting is that you first make the patient's head bleed, and extract the blood according to its virtue, then sit the patient between your hands and turn his ear upwards, and make a small incision at the root of the ear at the fat or dependent part; and let the incision be like a moon, as long as you come to the flint, then remove it according to your power, and suck it hastily into your mouth; and care for it until it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre .i. spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it's grains that are inside and it swells, then administer extraction; and if it cannot come out, then apply a thin, subtle spittle according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain. Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	and administer an incision on that grain. But don't do this when you think the grains are moist due to the moisture of the ear, until you have cut many pieces; then extract it with fine tweezers and suction, as we have said, so that the extraction is smooth.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton. Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est. s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin. se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent .i. jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	In the water that falls into the ear, it is necessary for the patient to use sneezing with condiments first, and fill the ear with old cotton. And let it be placed on top of that same ear where the water is. If it comes out through this, that's good. If not, then take many pieces according to the length of your fingers, thin and light, and heat them slightly over the fire; and have the patient put one or a small hole in their ear, and pull from the other side with another piece, and strike another piece on top of the piece that is in the ear; and do not stop doing this until all the water comes out, and thus it will come out altogether. And if you see, then take one reed, and insert one end into the ear, and the other end burn over fire until the middle part of the reed is burned; then make another part with other reeds until all the water comes out, as we have said earlier.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	En the extraction of the beast, if it is of small body, such as a puce and similar things, cure it as we have said in the division; but if it is of great body that one can feel it, thus make an extraction with tweezers; and it is the thing more easily removed that is in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the extraction of earwigs from the ears, when you have cured as we have said in the division and the treatment of distillations, and the cure does not benefit, then it is necessary that you look at the ear to the sun: if there are no worms visible, then treat them with fine tweezers; and if there are none, take the thread that is the shape thereof.
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.
