Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent. Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And make it narrow below and wide above. And put the most subtle head in the ear according to the quantity of the suffering of the patient, then succeed well to the end of the thread; do this often until all the worms come out. And if they do not obey to come out, then stop around the thread with cotton as I said in the stone; and if they do not emerge forth as we have said, then administer distillations that the ancients have proven in the removal of worms, and you will find them in the treatment of distillations; and if you distill your oils and medicines in the ear with all this instrument, according to the form that you see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a .i. petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a .i. estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren .i. raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations .i. poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And make it of silver or lead narrow below and a little small openings, and above over to distill; and to press inside the distillation with one instrument of well-made lead for this purpose, and if you see take a scraper and envelop it around the point pleasantly with cotton; then throw your oil or juice into it, and all that you see of your medicines in the thread, and the thread be in the ear; then put it into the scraper to the end of the cotton, and press your hand temperately until the oil is distilled or extracted from the ear; and the patient feels inside, and the distillations are one pot heated over the fire so that one can distill in the ear; and take care that it not be too cold, for the medicine would not be so good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of the stopping up of the ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without some perforation in the ears; and this same thing happens to men by stopping up a wound, or a piece of wax growing inside the ear, and these stoppings come sometimes deep into the ear, so that one cannot see it; and sometimes there occurs a small pot to block the perforation, and one can see well.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	That which comes deep into the ear, if one cannot see it, is of grievous inflammation in many dispositions, and in that which one can see, it is necessary that you put the ear of the patient to the sun; and look inside: if you see the whitening apparent, then work with all this spatula according to the form.
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And be gentle and cutting in front and behind all at once, so that it does not hurt the ear; if the whitening is of wax or flesh of the ear, then hold it with fine tweezers and cut it lightly, until all that wax is entirely removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren .i. raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille. Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	And if the whitening is deep in the ear, then take a subtle and light scraper and heat it slightly over the fire, then put it on the flesh of the ear. If you feel the whitening that the patient feels grief at hearing, cut lightly, and take care not to harm the nerves of the ear; then put into the ear a tent according to the width of the perforation, and moisten with Egyptian mummy.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this every day until the wound is healed, or you take a tent and moisten it in rose water, and powder on vitriol boil; and if you see the ear swelling, then it is necessary that you remove the tent and put another moist tent made of rose oil and wax, until the swelling is removed; then cure it until it is healthy.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if the discharges of blood come forth, then dip a sponge and wring it in cold water, and put it on the ear, and use other cures that remove the discharge of blood which are found in the treatment of distillations.
de la char des papieres	Of the flesh of paperwax
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This kind of wax that comes from the eyes when they are moist and dry, it is necessary that you stretch them with tenacula and tweezers, and cut them with a spatula from their roots; then put on the ear vitriol boil.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if the wax is scraped away, then cauterize it with a fine lenticular cautery, and after the incision is made, it swells; and many times it repairs itself, until nothing remains of their roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and do not come back.
de la gresle	Of the Hellebore
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope. se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	Many times come forth from the eyes of the patient certain things that resemble hellebore in its shape and hardness, and because of this, this disease is called "grandine", and it is an assembly of thick moisture on the paper above and below; the work is such: take heed if the grandine moves to one side and the other, and it is a light thing to know; then make the incision of the width, then scrape off each part lightly, then take with tweezers, and cut. If you cannot cut without piercing the paper slightly, do not hurt the patient; and if the wound is large, assemble it with a seam, and cure it until it is healed; and if it is small, do nothing strong, for the ointment will restore it soon and extract the flesh.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the grandine is descending into the ear towards the upper part, then turn the paper over, and extract the grandine with tweezers, and cut and press from one side to the other; and if the paper is removed by the incision, it does not hurt anything; and when the grandine is cut away, lift out the oil of salted water, and cure the place where flesh is extracted until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	Of the fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil. Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	Exinach is a fat that is extracted from the papery membranes above, and this happens more often in children than in adults, and it hurts a lot to their eyes; and they come with catarrh in the mornings, and cannot look at the light of the sun because the tears rush to their eyes; and therefore they lie down on their faces, and sleep on top, and their papery membranes below are moistened by the swelling and appearance that cover the exinach which appears in the eye. And when you press the place with your fingers and feel the exinach inside.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren .i. drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the manner of work is that the patient puts his head on thy side; and then takes one linen cloth, and prepares a tent in the shape of a circle according to the quantity contained within each part, then places it upon him; and presses with both hands from one side and the other so that the exirnach is assembled within the circle; then cuts in the middle of the moisture at the spatula trenching a notch of small size, not more than the wound one makes on the vein; and cuts the skin deeply until you come to the exirnach; and in many dispositions comes out from the notch according to the shape of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Then take out the whole piece of cloth wrapped between your hands to the outside, and turn your hand right and left until it is spread; and be sure not to push into the notch, lest you bruise all the spatula just to the edge, lest you bleed.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the exirnach does not open at the beginning of the notch, then widen the notch slightly until it opens; then pull it out as we have said, then soak cloth in oil and water, and place it on the skin, and tie with bandages.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree. Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez. Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there are such men who burst and put on poultice to corrupt the moisture that remains; then cure it until he is healed. And if the abscess comes hot to the boil, then treat it with emplasters soothing until he is healed.
des poilz des papieres	of hairs of paper
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When hairs of paper grow, they become grafted onto something other than the natural one, and are inflamed, so they harm the eyes, and bring on manners of diseases such as accustomed tears and softenings of the papers and albugine, until it is a cause of the destruction of the eyes; and the cure is according to three manners: or by fire cautery together, or by medicine water according to what is written in this chapter of cautery, and it is done or by incision and stitching or by cauterization, according as I shall say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai .i. fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai .i. fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	It is necessary that you put the patient's head on thy side; then turn the paper of oil in thine left hand; if it is converted, that is good; if not, then take an awl and pierce all one thread above; and let this be below the margin of the paper or where the hairs grow, and lead one thread above all the paper, and turn it to the razor; then make in the part below the paper, below the grafted hairs, up to the great tear just to the small; then pull out one thread, and put beneath the paper a small tent of cotton and cloth; then sign on the paper a figure of anointing, such as the balm of myrtle, and yet it is necessary that the figure be according to the quantity that thou seest increase the paper which is divided to all.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les .ij. lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des .ij. angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout .i. fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les .ij. sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a .iij. jors ou .iiij.; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor;	And if there is one who needs to cut off a great quantity of the paper according to what the paper is softened; then make up to all the spatula above two lines that you have signed, and start from the great tear just to the small; and let it be one of the notches near the natural hairs in the thickness of a root, then insert the onyx into one of the two corners of the key, then skin it entirely; then assemble the two lips with a stitch of an awl and all one thread of fine wool, and stop the blood, and make the excess threads adhere to the two crescents for any things sticking, if you see this done; and if not, then do not care, and leave the stitches and threads just for three or four days; then cure the wound without stitching or constraining things, for the paper revives at the healing of the wound and its assembly, but the stitch is corrupting (as the ancients said), and this is work without fear.
et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a .iij. oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	and if there is another way: and it is that you sign the paper with a figure that is like the balm of myrtle, as we have recounted, with three onyx stones separated according to the form that is here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	then cut off what rises above the small forces equally according to the form that is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait .i. fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute .i. autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans;	And if you are unable to hold the forceps and things are not equal, then take an awl with one thread, and insert it into the figure; and insert another thread below the great tear, and the second thread below the small, and assemble between your hands the threads equally; then lift your hand equally, and lift all the skin above where you have signed, as we have recounted, then assemble the two lips of the wound by stitching, and cure it until it is healed; and if an abscess comes to thy incision, then soothe it with cerote and similar ointments soothing.
et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	and sometimes it happens that the hairs of the paper are converted: then it is necessary to use what we have said about incision; but the stitching in one and the other is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The cure of cauterization is according to this form: and it is that you convert the paper and cut it within according to what I have said, and then make two cauterizations by art, and two fine threads as long as the paper and the breadth of the spatula are; and cut at the two heads of the two parts or where you hold the threads; then assemble one and the other subtly on what rises from the paper of oil, and strain the two cauterizations from the two parts formally; and let it be thus for some days, and the skin that is strained will die and necrotize and fall off, until it falls by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope aunes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des .ij. cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it takes too long, then cut off the remaining forces, and cure it until it is healed; and when the wound is sewn, and the paper is lifted, and they will no longer hold the hairs; and this is the form of the two cauterizations that you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute .i. fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse .i. autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The work is such that you take a fine awl, and insert one thread of silk soft and subtle; then assemble the threads and bind one and the other subtly, and let the length of the threads be a palm's width long; then order in the chase another fine thread of silk briefly, and bind the head of the thread; then put the patient's head on your shoulder; and let it be beneath the sun so that the work is disclosed, for this is a subtle and delicate work; then insert the awl into the entire chase at the root of the hair joined, and make it pierce in the paper hastenly as long as you lead it above the natural hair; then pull out the hair up to the chase, and bind that hair in the chase if there is one, two, three, or more; then pull out your hand until the hairs come forth from all the chase in the paper with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne .i. poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the hare is treated and the hairs do not come forth with it, then draw the hare down below to all the thread that you have ordered, until the hare comes forth from above the pertus and you see it by the vision of the eye; then draw the hare and the thread, and close the eye and let it be two or three days, so that the hairs grow in their place and the flesh subsides; and if the hairs are small, accompany one long hair with the natural ones of the hives, and be raised with that which you leave it, until it is elongated and then lift it.
de la porriture de l’oil	Of the dimness of the eye.
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de .ij. manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.  Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	When this illness called "aleacrati" comes to the eye, there are two kinds of it: one natural, and the other unnatural. And it happens suddenly from a wound, or a cut, or a burning, and from similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent. Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	And the manner of treatment for it is that you cut open the wound, and separate the lips of it, and put a linen cloth inside, and bind it until it is healed; and it does not need to use in its care things that dry and constrict. For if you do this, the illness will return worse than the first one; but work with things that soften, such as fenugreek; and rose of water or althea and flaxseed cooked, and dayaquilon ointment melted in some oil, and envelop it in a cloth, and treat it thus.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasure of your treatment is that you take care that it does not harden again in the same form as before; and these works that we have said are nothing other than remedies for this illness, so that it does not return in the same form as before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	Of the flesh that comes to the eye.
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens. Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait .i. fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en .ij. chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a .i. spatumile large.	This illness that is beneath and is truly called "axacrati", and is natural and accidental. The accident comes from a wound, or a cut, or a burning, and similar things; and the way of treatment for it is that you take a needle, which has one double thread, and push it into the flesh, and make it pierce all the way to the right eyebrow, so that the threads come out in two places on the flesh; then lift the flesh up over the entire needle, and cut at one spatula wide.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren .i. raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent .ij. fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des .ij. fendures des .ij. angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «.j. griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les .ij. parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the figure of the paper comes back according to what is needed, that's good; if not, take a razor and put it in the incision, and turn the paper, and make two incisions or on the side inside the paper; and be the holes of the two incisions at the two angles of the incision that you have cut, so that when they are assembled, the figure will be like the figure of a letter which has the name "one Greek"; then remove that flesh, according to the quantity that its edges is worn away below, from what follows the paper; then join the two separated parts and sew them with a wool thread; then do the treatment as we have said with soothing medicines, and cloths, until it is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les .ij. leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the illness comes from an incision or a cut or a burning, it is necessary that you make a plain incision below the hairs of the paper, and according to what has been said before; then separate between the two lips of a cloth, as I have said; and one must do the treatment according to the form of the illness, for it is very diverse in form, and wise masters prepare an engine of all their power so that it may return to its natural form; and the patient himself, according to what is needed for treatment and instruments in various dispositions.
dou soudement de la papiere	from the sudden movement of the paper.
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this swelling occurs in many people in the same way that the paper above is swollen with the white of the eye, and cannot move or perform its natural functions, then it is necessary to put the point of a razor under the paper and lift it up; and let it be as pincers, until you cut what is suitable for the subtle spatula, which is not too worn down nor too cut, so that the patient cannot endure having the spatula too worn down or blinding the eye; and make your incision, from which you scrape away the assembled flesh, slightly, so that the paper returns to its natural form; and let all that assembly be healed, and sometimes in the eye a salty water forms, and lifts up with sweet water and vinegar; then put between the paper and the eye a cloth of linen, and put woolen cloth soaked in egg white on top of the eye; and after three days use cologne and soothing things until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the ulcers of the eye.
Saiches que li ungle est selonc .ij. manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a .i. dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	Know that the ulcer is according to two manners: it is nervous and resembles a hard scab, and another which is not nervous but resembles white moisture congealed, which when you touch it with iron and cut it with pincers, it cannot be moved; and one and the other resemblance begins towards the great eyebrow, and grows little by little until it covers all the sight and all the light and the movement of the eye.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met .i. poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et .i. fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of incision is that the patient places his head in your lap, then opens his eyes; and lifts the paper with your hand, then coils the ulcer with pincers of small double thread, and lifts it up; then takes a needle, and puts one hair of horse, or ox, or cow, and a strong thread on it; and doubles the point of the needle a little and inserts it into the ulcer, and pierces all the way to the end of the needle, and binds the ulcer with one thread and lifts it up, and scrapes away all the hair from the side of the ulcer that follows the prune and silk to the hair just to the head; then cuts off what remains in the root of the eyebrow at all the subtle spatula and small forces, and leaves the natural skin or eyebrow so that by incision the body does not bring forth tears as usual; and sometimes sets the ulcer on a cotton cloth, and on thread, as we have said; then scrapes away everything soft from what is here the form.
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And take care that the spatula does not touch the fleshy skin and break it, and that the prune is not pierced; and after the incision pours a little bit of silk broth into the eye, and makes a cologne from litargire, and leaves it until the next day; then treats with what is needed so that it may be healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the ulcer is not nervous and you cannot put the needle in, and the compresses cannot enter, many times this resemblance of ulcer is treated with medicines; and it arises as I have told in the division, and if you see it copulating, then do the oil treatment for the patient, and take a spatula slightly worn out according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And gently remove the pus above, and if you see it does not decrease and reason approaches, then distill from your mouth into the eye a potion made of lettuce and red hot chili pepper to stop the eye just until the next day; then continue the other work according to this same work, until all is removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing is contrary to you in the eye, as it is inflamed with apostema, then apply a poultice and cure the hot abscess until it is healed; then continue the work as before, until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh of the eyelid hurts the eye with great harm, then suspend it from the eyebrow and cut off a part but not all, so that the flow of tears does not come; then distill into the eye red hot chili pepper potion made of lettuce.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh that grows on the conjunctiva
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tune bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre;	There are some men whose skin grows red, and covers the conjunctiva, and restrains above the papillae and turns to the outside, and seems like a rose of baluster; and the work is such that the patient puts their head in your hand, then you open the eyes, and coil all that flesh around suitable strings, and sustain it with force; then cut off the first skin, and go all cutting to the scraper just until the end, and take care not to stain the eye during the work; and be the incision of the spatulum as we have said in the incision of the pus and small forces, by which one removes the shell, as the form shows after this chapter.
et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	and when the incision is complete and all the flesh is removed, then apply oil with red chili pepper or similar corrosive medicines to the eye, and place a cotton cloth with egg yolk on top of the eye so that it is assuredly free from hot abscess; and if there is nothing left, and the blood flows forth, and you suspect hot abscess, then leave the eye and cure the hot abscess with soothing things; then return to your work until it is healed, and thus make all the flesh that has been removed in the eye by this similar method.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	But it is also necessary that you lighten the treatment of each weak eye in the natural way and in the accidental way with iron work; and do not put your hand on any of these works until you see that these members are suffering from this treatment.
des voines des eulz	of the veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors. Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	The sebel are red veins that are covered on the eye, and tolerate its work and weaken the eye forever. It is necessary then to first examine whether the eye, in which this sebel is, is sound, and there is no other disease except for the sebel; then coil it in this manner: instruct the patient to put their head in your hand, then suspend those veins on all the eyebrow according to your wisdom, and be the eyebrow subtle double according to this form:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en .i. cors selonc ceste forme:	And be two eyebrows by degree in one flesh according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then coil those veins with gentle forces, and inspect the blood hour after hour, until you see removing those veins from the eye; and take care that you do not stain the eye with the points of spatula, and make this work at noon before the sun, and be very fervent in your work so that you do not cut away more than those veins; and when you have done this, then distill into the eye green and red chili pepper potion to corrupt what is remaining of the sebel.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you have no power to coil all that in one hour, then make a poultice on the eye with soothing things to ease the pain of the eyes, and leave it for some days until the pains are eased and be assured of hot abscess; then resume according to this manner which is before until it is healed; and this is the form of forces:
de la fistule de l’oil	of the pus of the eye
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The doctor is called "arissati" fistula: when you cure it with cauterization and hot medicine as I have said before, and it is not healed, then there is a reason in him that you cut into the abscess where it should heal, and drain out all the moisture that is there, until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a .i. chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is exposed, and you see the corruption and blackness, then take it away with all the instrument of which this form is; and it is called "aspre chief", and be made of iron indented to one point, and be pointed like a razor as it is in the present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And place it on the surface of the corrupted bone, then turn it between your hands, and press your hand a little until you know that that corruption is removed; and do this some time, then restore the surface with caustic medicines.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi xl. jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent .i. foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a .iij. angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the bone is sound, and flesh grows, and the bowels of the body are sound, and remain so for 40 days, and it does not heal and is not apostemated, and bad things do not happen, you know that it is healed; if not, then there is no other reason than to return the fistula to its original shape according to this form: and it is that you uncover the bone a second time with iron and hot medicines, and when it is uncovered, take one force according to this form, and be the iron key at three angles, and the wire be thinned down to the head as you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil .i. poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	Then place it on the bone near the eyelid, and remove your hand from the eye for a little while, then turn the whole force until it pierces the bone and the patient feels it through the vein if he holds his hand on his navel; and then restore the surface with dry medicines as I have taught you, and when the flesh grows and hardens the surface, the matter will go to the navel; this is a lighter thing for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	of the discharge of the eye
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil .i. liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en .iiij., et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eyes open completely and there is no obstruction or decrease in the navel, then it is necessary that you bind the patient; then heal him, then apply poultices or haters made to bleed with iron to suck out; then place on the eye a lien made of aloe, acacia, and incense, and then strain the eye, and apply a poultice on top of a bandage; and the manner of the bandages is that you take soft cloths, double each one four times, and then put one on top of another according to the quantity that the eyes need; then strain it with a strong bandage for a long time, and reapply the poultices to bleed without hurting; then remove the poultices and let the eye be strained day and night, and if the lien becomes worn out, you should bind it tightly; then remove the lien after the day and night, and if you see the eye repairing itself, that is good; if not, then reapply the poultice and bandages and lien and poultices until it is healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	the bursting of the eye's skin
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com .i. grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait .i. fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When a discharge comes into the eye's skin, then it opens, and there come forth papers like grains of resin, and it is unbelievable to see; then if you cover it, the works are such that you bore an awl into the root of the part below up to the point above, then bore another awl where there is a double thread from the eyelid; and make it pierce, and leave the first awl according to its position; then cut off the end of the double thread and tie one part of the eye around, and hold it tightly, then extract the awl and put on the oil linseed moist in abundance of yolk; and let it stay until the child's skin is stuck with the eye, then cure the eye with things that give comfort until the wound is healed; and sometimes the wound is restrained by the eye each part of a circle of cloth, until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eyes show great appearance, then pierce them with a fine spatula that comes from within the eye, and correct the moisture of the albuginea and descend the eyes, and enter inside shortly afterwards; then extract it until they are healthy.
de la bowe de l’oil	of the bottom of the eye
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de .ij. pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit. si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee .i. poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	This disease which is called "alcunnati" is nothing but the bottom part that is gathered in the eye, resembling descending water, and it is not actually water; and the manner of its appearance in the work is such that you make the patient sit on a prepared and straight seat, then take their head between your hands from two parts, and move it so that you see the bottom part come up to your eyes; then let it be fixed, and do not descend and discombobulate the light, and let the patient see things as they used to; and if it does not descend below, know that it is actual water, and if the descent of the bottom part is not prepared as we have said. Then make the patient sit between your hands, then take a fine spatula and put it on the corneal tissue one drop at a time by the continuation of the conjunctiva with the corneal tissue and the crown, until the bottom part comes out; and when it is out, let it distill into the eye hot honey mixed with water or fenugreek boiled with honey, then be cured with another cure until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	of the waters of the eye
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit. Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre. se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	We have the likenesses of the waters in the division, and what is needed to pierce; then work according to health. It is necessary that you make the patient sit between your crossed hands, away from the light by the sun, and have the healthy eye sutured tightly; then place the paper on the eye on your left hand if the eyes are left, or on your right hand if the eyes are right; then take in your right hand, if the eyes are left, the instrument called "almagda", or in your left hand, if the eyes are right; then place the point of the instrument beneath the crown by the thickness of a finger in that blepharitis of the eye at the part of the lesser eyelid, then bore the instrument called "almagda" vigorously, and turn your hand so that it pierces into the blepharitis of the eye, and feel that almagda comes to the empty thing; and it is necessary that the measure of almagda's path be at the bottom of the measure of the space which is from the prune to the end of the night; and this is the crown of the eye; then you will see the bone on that paper by the brightness of the corneal tissue, and place the instrument just above or where the water is; then express it below one way after another. If the water descends now, then the patient will see before him and the instrument in his eye.
Aprés repose .i. petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens. Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.  Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	After a little pause, and if the water rises again on the second path, place the force with the instrument, and when it is fixed and does not rise, gently extract almagda by turning your hand slowly; then put in the eye a drop of gemstone oil, and leave what's inside the eye. Then place on top of the eye estropes or linseed moist in rose oil and an abundance of yolk, and tie with the healthy eye. We, and those who are of our time, put on a common broth with an abundance of yolk.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if almagda cannot enter the eye because of its hardness, for there are some men whose eyes are too hard, it is necessary that you take the instrument called "alberit", which has this shape:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai .i. leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide .i. dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en .j. leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And then pierce the conjunctiva alone, and do not go too far in, but make a fine point, and then insert almagda as we have said; and at the completion of the work, prepare for the patient an attendant who is skilled, so that he sleeps on his back in a dark room; and be free from all movements, and take light foods, and do not move your head to the right or left, and be tied according to his disposition until the third day; then release him in the same dark house, and test his sight, and make him see some things, and then put the tie back on up to the seventh day; and it is not necessary that you do this during the cure or after the incision now, but it is necessary that you hasten this, because the water rises quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice .i. orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse. Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	If an abscess forms and comes, you should release the eye before the seventh day, and direct it to what soothes the abscess; and when it is appeased, then release the sight and put on its face a small ointment to cover for some days, and be still in that dark house. And then go out of the house little by little, and turn back to his case; and know that no disciples should interfere with this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us from the land of Irach, who told us that in his country almagda was pierced, through which water flowed, but I never saw anyone do this in our land, nor did I ever read about it in books of the ancients; and by chance it's a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the likenesses of the forms of almagda, because those who do not know them see it; and let them be properly of silver.
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	And let their heads be of the same subtlety, and their ends in three angled aqueducts.
de la char sor le neis	of the flesh on the skin
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color. En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; puis cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	There are some times when flesh on the skin is born or grows different, of which there are some that seem like scorpions with many points; and if there are such that it has flesh enchanted with a mixed color, and if it has soft flesh of bone color. In one of these flesh types which is soft, and not enchanted, you must make the patient sit between your hands facing the sun; and work on his nostrils, and pour the oil onto those flesh parts, and treat them with force; then do what you can to support at the fine subtle edge of a part, until you know that that flesh is entirely loosened.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	Et s'il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne pued coper, si l'ovrez à tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu'il n'i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c'est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, acoi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes .i. fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice .i. doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil. Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu .iij. jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Se the nail does not work, and moisture comes just to the palace, know that it is healed; and if moisture does not penetrate as it should, know that there is new flesh in the bone above, so the instruments do not come to cut: then you must put .i. thread of linen a little thick, and moisten with hands now, and have between each night .i. dot or less; and put the patient's head on the thread in his sleep at some power, and pull it slowly as he comes by the thread down through the mouth; and many times do thus the children in schools, and it is a light thing for him who wants to do it; then hold the chief that comes by the thread with one hand, and the other chief that comes by the mouth with the other hand, and know one after the other as we are on the thread. Do this until you know that the night has corrupted that flesh, then pull out the filament, wipe away the blood, and moisten the thread in Egyptian ointment, and put it back in the nail as before; do this .iii. days or more, until the ointments corrode all that remains of flesh; and then put on the nail a cord of cloth after some days until he is healed, and if he needs medicines such as these, use them; and this is the form of the instrument for purging the chief, to which one distills oils and medicines in the nail:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And let it be of silver or of brass, resembling an open lamp, like a cord, and lead it thus; and if you see, make a closed cord, and the instruments be full to purge the chief; and have one handle on the chief to hold it when one heats the oil or some liquid.
de la char sor le neis	of the flesh from the nail
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times a disease called "telul" arises on the head of the nail, and grows and becomes great in size, so that it is visible to behold; and therefore it is necessary that you cut off the tip at first, and remove all roughness, then put the cautery or burning medicine on top; and if one delays cutting it until it is great, beware if it turns hard, of a foul color, of poor sensation: do not touch it with iron because it is an enchanted aposteme, for when you cut it once, great evil comes to the patient; and if the aposteme is of soft touching, not of foul color, and you see that one can cut it all away, then empty the patient and the coping of fear, and care for the head with things soothing and restraining.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the nail is cut off and cleansed
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes. Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les .ij. levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Know that when solutions of continuation come to one of these worked cartilages, it profits little, more than in some men. It is necessary then to do as with anyone, if you look and see if the wound is fresh with all its blood; and then attach the two lips together with a seam, and care for it until it is healed; and if the lips are already separated on one side and the other, it is necessary that you scrape away all the parts of their flesh until they are clean, then attach the two lips together with a seam, and bind it tight, and powder on top powder of dragon's blood, and incense broiled; and put on top of the powders a piece of plaster or another plaster fitting, and let it be until it heals by itself, then care for it with ointment until it is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The manner of the seam is that you assemble the solution: either by needles, as we have said in the seam of the belly; or by thread, as I have told you.
des apostemes des levres	of the apostemes of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many men have within their lips an aposteme hard, resembling grains of peas, and smaller and larger; therefore it is necessary that you turn the lips inside out, and cut each night, and take as pincers and cut in each part; then apply a poultice to the wound after the vitriol incision, until the blood is stopped; and then leave the wound open, and care for the wound with dry things until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	of the flesh of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times there arises on the gums flesh congealed, which the ancients call "albulus"; therefore it is necessary that you hold it with forceps, and cut at its root, and let the flow of blood or pus; then put on the wound vitriol broiled, or other restraining and drying powders; and if that flesh returns after the incision, and many times occurs, then cut it a second time, and cauterize it: if it does not return after the cautery; and these are the forms of the instruments for cutting.
des sordens	of the abscesses
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes they are assembled at the head of the teeth, within the mouth between the gums, ulcers which are ugly and rough; and sometimes the teeth become black and yellow and green, as corruption comes to the gum, and the teeth stink; therefore it is necessary that you make the patient sit in your hands, and his face be in thy sight, and remove the teeth or ulcers that appear, until nothing remains; and thus do with the blackness and the yellowness, and the jaundice and other spots, until they are cleansed; and if one removes what is at first reason, it is good; but if not, then continue to repeat the second day and the third, until you have all removed; and know that the teeth have need of diverse forms of instruments to remove, according to what the work shows, because the scraper which one uses to clean the teeth between them has other forms than the one used to scrape away at the teeth; and these forms and others be with thee prepared.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you care for the tooth's pain that you wait until you can pull it out as much as possible, because it should not be done hastily; for it is a very high substance so that one has no excuse to regret.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant. Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Then when the patient is constrained to pull out, it is necessary that you be certain of the tooth's vitality. Many times the pain was the patient's guide, and believed that the tooth was sacred, and had the good tooth pulled out; and yet the pain did not depart because of this, until the bad tooth was extracted, for we have already intended to do so with these saints; and when you are well certain of the tooth's vitality, it is necessary that you scrape all around the tooth with a strong spatula to protect the gum from all sides; then move it to your hands or as fine forceps at first pace and pace, until it is well extracted, then firmly secure the forceps; and be the patient's hand in thy sight between thy knees, and hold it well so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier. Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	After extracting the tooth correctly without breaking, and if it does not jump away, take one of these instruments and insert it on each side slightly, and then move it as you did first. And if the teeth are pierced and mangled, it is necessary that you fill them with drapels, where the perforations are; and if you extract subtilly with forceps, so that it does not break when extracted; and it is necessary to work very carefully around the gum to dislodge the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere. Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	Here is the translation:
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the instruments, to which one should mold the teeth first, are long-pointed and thick-gripped, so they do not double back when you pull the tooth; and these are the shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And be of thick handles so they do not bend when pulled, and be well made of iron, and have teeth to hold in place.
de la racine des dens	of the roots of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre .i. jor ou ij., tant que li leus soit amolis, puis i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	When the root remains while pulling, it is necessary that you put a moistened cotton ball or butter on the joint for one or two days until the joint becomes soft, then insert the forceps called "algefri", by which the head seems to be like a fine comb; and are made inside as a file, and this is the shape:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all these forceps, it is necessary that you uncover the flesh entirely around the root, and put in the instrument called "althali", which is a scraper, by which this is the shape:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And be strong and thick so it does not break, and if the root jumps through this, that is good; if not, then help with all instruments, by which these shapes come next:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one uses this instrument having two handles, by which this is the shape:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other instruments that are before in proportion to the teeth, and of this instrument which resembles great forceps, by which this is the shape:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And be these instruments such that they cannot break, and know that many instruments for teeth are; and also other instruments which are not counted; and wise and subtle masters find their own instrument by themselves, according to what their works and the disease show them, for there are some diseases where the old ones did not teach any instrument due to the diversity of cases; or if it breaks a bone or another bone, or wherever, so it searches for instruments that it needs, which I have told you, and helps with gestures, by which this is the shape:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And be large and well-holding to hold the bone, so it does not escape, but can hold and remove; and then restore the joint with medicines fitting for this, and if there is in the bone some decay, and it is small, then repair all this instrument:
