Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not according to its natural place in the body, and its shape is ugly, especially in young girls, it is necessary that you know if the tooth is newly grown after the gum, and is not in its right place, and cannot be filed or sharpened: then scrape; and if it is stuck with the gum, take this instrument which has this shape, and is similar to a small beak, and be made of iron very sharp on top:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the file files and files a little by day because of the hardness of the tooth, and for that you do not move the others, and if it appears to be able to be filed, then file with a similar file which has this shape:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and is also like the file with which one makes needles; and in filing the tooth a little by day gradually, so that it does not move until it is even; then smooth out the end to all roughness, and if the tooth is too sharp and hurts the tongue, then file off the sharpness so that it is even, so that it does not hurt the tongue nor corrupt speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the teeth loosen
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les .ij. dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a .i. ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper. Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des .ij. dens sains, et des .ij. meus, si com tu vois:	When the teeth in front loosen by percussion or falling, and the patient cannot press down on what they are eating without spitting it out, and you have treated them with restricting medicines, and this does not work; then one must restrain them with a golden thread, for silver threads become green and decay, but gold never changes; and be the thread neither too thin nor too thick, according to the size of the space between the teeth; and if you see that the teeth are directed, take the thread and push it double between two healthy teeth, then put the ligaments between the other teeth, if there is one or more, so that they come up to the healthy tooth on the other side; then re-cover the part where you started, and strain your hand subtly and smoothly, until it does not move anymore; and be your finger at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape. Then file the ligaments with forceps, and assemble them, and re-point between the healthy tooth and the other tooth, and put it in such a way that it does not hurt the tongue; then leave it thus tight as long as it can remain, and if it comes loose or the thread breaks, then restrain it with another thread; so it will remain and serve thus for all its time, and this is the shape of the teeth and the figure of the direction of the two healthy teeth, and the two others, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth falls out, then put it back in its place, bit by bit, as we have said; and do not meddle with it if one is not wise and careful, and sometimes make the shape of a whalebone tooth, and put it in the place where the deficiency is, and restrain it as we have said, and remain and serve thus for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	of removing the ligament from the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder. Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	Sometimes this ligament comes from under the tongue by nature, or as one is born with it; or by accident of a wound that has healed; and the operation is such that you work on the mouth of the patient, and have their head in your healthy hand, and lift up the tongue; then remove the nervous ligament from its width, until the tongue is dislodged from its dwelling, and if there is hardness or knot, and it is due to a sudden wound, then insert an unguent and file that ligament; and be careful that the cut is not too deep, lest the artery below be injured; and when you have done this, then lift up the wet poultice of rose water and vinegar, or cold water, and put it under the tongue; and let the patient rest each night, so that the wound does not sicken. And if bleeding comes forth, then place a piece of vitriol broth on the wound; and if the blood flows, then cauterize with the slow fire cautery, which is good for this; then cure it with another treatment until it is sound.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if you see that it is dull-colored or black or hard, and the patient does not feel it, then do not touch it, for it is a chancre; and if it is declining towards a blenchor, and there is moisture, then pour on the unguent, and make a subtle poultice with spatumile, and deliver it from one side and the other; and if the blood flows at your operation, then apply vitriol broth until it is stopped, then return to your operation until you have completed all your work; then lift up the wet poultice of vinegar and oil, and cure it with other treatments until it is sound.
des apostemes de la gorge	Abscesses of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les .ij. amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer. Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez. Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Abscesses of the throat which are called "godath" and properly named ".ij. amandres", and when you cure them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, take heed: if it is a hard abscess with little sense and dull color, do not touch it with iron. And if it is red and the root is thick, do not touch it with iron, also for fear of bleeding; but leave it until it dies, and then you will part it, or it would break apart by itself; and if it is white-colored and the root is subtle, prepare the instrument to cover it, but look first if the abscess is calm and appeased. Then make the patient sit before the sun, with his head in your hand, and have him open his mouth and take the servants between his hands, and press the tongue underneath all the instrument, which is the form; and it should be of silver or refined lead, just like small knives:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	Can't you press the tongue all over this instrument, and then see the abscess, take a needle and stick it into the abscess, and let it go on top as much as you can; and do not touch anything with cloth, then cut at the instrument, which is the form, that seems like a force; and yet the head are curved, one side to the other, and are very sharp, and is made of iron or steel:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument present, then cut with pincers, which is the form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And be cutting on one side and the other; and when you have cut one of the abscesses, then cut the other in the same manner, and after incision, gargle the patient with hot water, and cold and easy, and if bleeding occurs, gargle the patient with hot water, or cooked apple skins, or myrtle leaves, and similar things, until the blood is stopped; then cure it until it is healed; and sometimes other abscesses are born in the throat than the two amandres, so cut them then like the two amandres similarly.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir .i. aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi .i. jor ou .ij. Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis .ij. rains par les .ij. pertuis dou neis. Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un .i. oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	And I healed a woman from an abscess that was born inside her throat, that is to say one abscess of little sense; and I had well closed the entire throat, so that the woman could not breathe through the conduit which was blocked, and could neither eat nor drink, and would have been dead if she had remained like this for a day or two. The abscess was so high that it had pushed out two streams through two openings of the birth canal. I hastened then, and stuck in one place a needle, then drew forth blood; and drew out a large portion of pus; then refilled the other opening with the birth canal, and opened the mouth and pressed the tongue; after which I inserted the needle into this abscess, and cut part of it away, and only a little blood flowed out; and thus the conduit of the throat was unblocked for the woman, and she began to drink water and then wine, and did not cease cutting at that abscess for a long time; and the abscess recrossed again, and filled up the space that I had emptied, until it became very large; then I tied it off and cauterized it inside the throat: thus it remained growing; and I left those parts, and only God did what happened after me.
de l’uve	of the vein
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve». Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li. Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide. Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a .i. des .ij. estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres. Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee. Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor. Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague. Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	When the swelling goes down to the vein, and it is inflamed and long, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is under a thick and rounded one, it is called "vein". When it is cured as we have said in the division, and the cure does not benefit, and you see that the abscess is appeased, and it is subtle, then it is necessary to cut it; and the one that is rounded and not long; and it is sanguine or dull-colored or black, then it is necessary to avoid the incision. For there is great peril on the patient. It is necessary, when you see it, according to the manner that I have said, to make the patient sit before the sun, and press the tongue against the instrument which we have made a remembrance of herebefore; then stick the needle into the vein, and pull it down, and cut at one of the two instruments that I have said in the incision of the two amandres. And it is necessary not to cut more than the superfluity that is outside the natural term; for if you cut more, it will harm the voice, and the speech; and after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the two amandres, and cure it until it is healed. And if the patient has fear of cutting, then it is necessary to use a trick at the cauterization so that there is no more fear. The manner of the cautery is hot water. And it is that the patient puts his head in your hand, and then presses the tongue against the instrument which we have said or chapter of cautery, and confesses with living water, so that it is not too thick nor too clear; and in using the handle of this instrument, which is the form:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And have the patient put their head in a hairnet or on a comb, just like the hairs of a comb, and place the instrument all over the medicine on the vein; and the patient should be lying on their side with their chest against your hand, so that saliva and mucus flow from their mouth into the medicine, but do not go down to the throat and wound. Then hold your hand on the medicine and press it on the vein for half an hour, until you see it numb and the medicine's irritation be appeased; and if you see anything, take a cotton cloth and wrap it around some instrument, and soak the cotton in the medicine, then insert the instrument into all the cotton wrapped around it on top of the cane, so that the cotton gets on the vein; and do this often until the cautery is complete, then let it dry, and wait for three or five days. And if you need to start again with the medicine's cautery, then start again, and after the cautery, apply a poultice around the vein, wrapped in cloth soaked in butter, and cleanse everything that is around the medicine; and be treated with gargling until it is healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer than incision or cautery; if it is cured by fumigation according to this manner, take calament and ysope and origanum and rue and camomille and avronne and similar herbs, and assemble all or some of them in one pot, and add a little water, and make it boil; and the pot should be well glazed with strong earth, and inside the pot have an instrument shaped like this:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut. Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	Et soit d'argent ou d'arain, and let it be of silver or lead, and whichever one you insert into the patient's mouth so that the vapor rises to the eye through the tube, until the eye is mortified; afterwards it often starts again, until the eye dries, and take care not to do this at the beginning of the abscess's heat, for many things happen then; and don't do this at all unless at the decline of the abscess's heat. And if this instrument isn't present, then take a tube and put a quill inside it so that the patient's mouth doesn't get too hot; because the quill doesn't allow the vapor to weigh down the mouth, and it is good care for both health and salvation.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times it is applied to the throat or spine of a fish, or to nothing; therefore you should try what you can see, and press the tongue against the sun with all the instrument, so that you see the thing move; and what does not appear and is returned to the throat, it is necessary that you make the patient vomit as soon as the meat is cooked in the stomach; perhaps then the thing will be expelled through vomiting; or the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of nautilus shell, or a lettuce root, or one small piece of dry bread; and tie the sponge to a thread, and then make it pass through; and when it comes out, it will stay, and then you can pull further; and if it does not come out as we have said, then take an instrument of pumice according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the instruments be curved at the head so that it can enter the throat more easily, and have the head raised high; and take care not to touch the epiglottis, lest all come together, nor insert the bone inside; and make sure that the patient puts the instrument in, because it may move or the thing is expelled; then put it down, or pull it out slowly with the instrument equally, until it is out.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the discharge from the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit. Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout .i. petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu. Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine .i. fer chaut, et fai ce sovent. Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor. puis pren plein .i. voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	No time is medicine for the discharge, as I said in the division, by the treatment of medicines; and when this does not help, then look into the throat of the patient at the sun, since you press the tongue against the instrument that I told you. And if you see the discharge, pull it out slowly with a small hook or fine forceps suitable for this purpose. And if this is not effective, take a hair-like tube and insert it into the patient's throat, then put the hot iron on the end of the tube and do this often. And if the patient is troubled by water all day, then take a full view of cold water, open their mouth, and spit it out without swallowing, and move it around with your hand often; and as soon as the discharge feels the water, it will fall.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier. Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes .i. pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And if it does not fall as we said, then suffumigate the patient with asafoetida at the instrument that I told you in the fumigation of the eye; do this many times, for it will fall without effort. And the manner of the fumigation is that you take a pot with hot coals, and let it be covered with a perforated cloth, and in the hole put the head of the instrument; then pour your fumigation, and the patient puts the end of the tube into their mouth, and closes their mouth, so that the smoke does not come out, but comes just to the discharge; and the discharge will now fall, and if it does not fall, then repeat the fumigation many times; and let the patient suffer thirst, and eat salty and bitter things, and do not drink water; and then there will be need for it to come out through this governance.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the form of the instrument with which you treat the discharge is such that when it can be seen, it resembles curved forceps for moving into the throat; and it has a resemblance to a doctor's beak, and it has roughness like lime, so that whatever it takes, it cannot let go; and see this form:
li chapistres des apostemes	the chapters on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en .ij. manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor. Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors. car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	Many kinds of abscesses are, according to what is remembered hereafter in this book, and they differ in perforation and size; and there are two ways in which one is similar to the other, and that it holds moisture. And the second manner is for those that are on the bone or at the body. For abscesses of the head are different from those of the foundation, and abscesses of the bone that char is different from those that come together with joints, and each has its own judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures. Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre. Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	And if there are abscesses that one should not pierce until the swelling is gone according to its accomplishment; and some are such that it is necessary to pierce when they are ripe, and do not die according to their accomplishment, as abscesses that are near joints. For when abscesses come near joints, and one leaves them so long that they become gangrenous around, by chance the ligaments and nerves of the joint are corrupted, which is a cause of contraction in that member. Or if the abscess is on the principal member, and you delay perforation until it is gone, it will harm the principal member; or if it is near the foundation, then one should pierce it as soon as it is ripe; and it is not necessary to pierce a ripe abscess without digestion being complete, except for that which is near the foundation, lest it become a fistula and be prolonged inside, and come to be a great affliction.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And it is necessary that you know the hour of the perforation of the abscess which is ripe according to its accomplishment, and this is when the pain has subsided, and the departures of fever have ceased, and the reduction of pain and redness, and the cessation of throbbing and the soothing of the head of the abscess, and other signs; and it is necessary that you perform the perforation or more depending on the location of the abscess, and where it appears to be moving; and the perforation should be from the long part of the body, and if the abscess is at the hands or feet, or in joints and nerves and arteries, and in all equal places where there is no pleurisy.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre. Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit. Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui. Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.  Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com .i. drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en .iij. angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	In those that are pleuritic, according to the affected member. And when abscesses are in the charnut location, it is best to wait until they are confirmed in complete digestion, as we have said. For if you pierce them before then, the body of the venom will be prolonged and full of many impurities; and by chance, the lips and deeper parts will become hardened. And there are some abscesses that are pierced according to the width of the body, according to what the member needs. And it is necessary that you make small incisions for small abscesses, and large incisions for large abscesses, and many slits according to the appearance of the size of the abscess; and there are some such that need to have the wound closed, and covered when it has become as a piece of cloth, and is no longer inflamed, then one must do as with infants: and there are some such that are cut in three angles, and some that are cut like the foliage of myrtle, like abscesses of the groin; and some such that require a round incision, and other incisions and shapes of covering.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites. Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois. Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Cil who have not a chief, such as a superficial aposteme, it is necessary that you make a incision quickly; and it is necessary when the apostemes are great, and they have gathered a large amount of pus, and you make an incision, so do not draw out all the pus at once, but only a part; then stop the aposteme just until the next day, then take nothing further; do this gradually over time, until all the pus is gone; likewise if the patient has weak vitality, or women bearing children, or small children, or old men decrepit. For the hopes sometimes tremble with the issue of the pus, so that by chance the patient dies, and you are not aware. Therefore, use this chapter with great caution, and when you have incised your aposteme, if the wound is plain, then try to stitch it together with linen or old cotton; and if it is a large aposteme, and there are many pustules, then it is necessary that you make a tent in each one so that they come together against each other; and if you have cut out from the aposteme a part of leather, and you have sewn it around, then it is necessary that you fill it with old cotton or flax cloth without moisture, and tie it just until the third day; then remove it, and treat it with ointment until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille .i. drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.  Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if hemorrhaging occurs at your work, then apply cold and easy water, and wet cloth, and place it on the bleeding site repeatedly. And if the hemorrhaging persists, then administer governance and care, and the powders that I have said to use in this book, and if it is winter, and the site or aposteme is very nervous, then it is necessary that you put up tents and wet cloths soaked in wine and hot oil; and if it is summer, and the site is fleshy, then it is necessary that you put up wet cloths soaked in water and oil, or in cold wine and oil, until the third day, as we have said; and then release the aposteme and treat it, so that it may be healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And it is necessary to know universally in treatments of apostemes: now I have said how one should proceed before treating apostemes, and see this chapter.
des soros	of blisters
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances. Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire. Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout .i. estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient. Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc. Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit. Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se li apostemes tient .i. nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés. Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	Where blisters on the head come small apostemes, and they are ways for us that are in toils, like the weaver of a spider's web, and there are many similarities. There are some which are fat and similar to those that have moisture as pustules; and there are others which are hard and stony to cut, and there is no doubt if the artery does not make it contrary. And the work of cutting is such that you test each one by a tool called "entromissoire", from which the form comes after, whatever thing it contains. For if it contains moisture, then wash it above the long; and when the moisture is empty, then scrape off without leaving any of the peel which contains that moisture, for it returns again if you leave anything; then plunge cotton in Egyptian ointment, if it is present; if not, in water and oil, and fill the wound, and let it be just until the next day; and this will cure those who remain from the night. And then begin again with the cotton, as before, on the second day, and the third, until you know well that it does not remain from the night; then treat the wound with ointment as necessary, until it is healed. And if the aposteme holds a fat night, then cut it according to this form, above the long; and throw away your needles, and scrape off all around, and put all your care in drawing out of the coat where it lies; and if the artery makes it contrary, do what I told you after. And similarly do with the aposteme if it is stony, and cut and cure as I told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc. Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut .i. apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere. En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	And the cutting above the stony and moist aposteme is easier, because they are full of blood. And if there are some of these apostemes on the head where there is no moisture, and one of these apostemes that I cut off from a old woman's head; and I found the aposteme to be like a hard, rough, and white stone, and could not break it; and if anyone had done anything with it, they would have made a wound as if from a stone. In other apostemes coming on the head, more than those that come on children's heads and at the roots of ears, the opening should always be to the most dependent place, in order for the pus to issue; and treat them as necessary.
des scrophules	of scrofulas
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre. Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes. Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit. en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les .ij. levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	Many times these apostemes occur at the neck, and below the armpits, and in the groin, and sometimes they come elsewhere on the body, and are many, and are intertwined one with another. And each scrofula is properly within its own coat, as the night and the aposteme of the head, as we have said; and the likenesses of these scrofulas are many. There are some that contain moisture, and there are others that are malignant and will not obey health. Therefore, when you see a good disposition to touch, and it resembles the color of the body, and is mute on each side, and is not harsh against the nerves of the neck or the artery or the conduit, and is not swollen; then it is necessary that you cut it above, and scrape off each part, and are careful that you do not cut the nerve or the vein, and that the hands escape, and do not see too far ahead, lest you cut what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir. Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde. Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if you cut the vein or artery, and it does not let you work, then put vitriol broth or some powders that remain blood in the wound, and hold the wound; and leave it until the aposteme is pacified, and the wound is softened, and begins to rot. And when the blood is stanchied, then return to your work, until you have completed it; then look at your indication if there are any small scrofulas left, cut them off and scrape them clean. And if there is a great vein in the root of the scrofula, then do not need to cut that scrofula at its root, but tie it with a double strong thread, and let it fall down without harm; then fill the wound with old cotton steeped in Egyptian ointment, and cure it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les .ij. levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule. si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit. Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you cut the entire scrofula, it is necessary that you bring together the two lips of the wound and sew them up now, so that there is no remaining superfluity due to the size of the scrofula. It is necessary that you understand how to cut at its root and draw out the excess, and sew it as we have said. Those scrofulas that hold superfluity, burst forth where it is most abundant; and burst forth in this way as the one previously mentioned, depending on, then administer tentatives with ointment and similar things, so that it corrupts what remains of corruption; and when the wound is well cleaned, cure it with ointment flowing with flesh, until it is healed.
de squinance	From shrinking
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The old ones said and spoke of the cutting of the throat; but I never saw anyone in our land who did it, and this is the writing of their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	To those who have shrinking, it is necessary that the incision of the throat called "epiglote" be removed; and one does not help by doing so, because all the veins and the body parts of the patient are hot in the mouth, or in the throat, or in both sides.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the channel of the body, it is necessary to cut off the epiglote to avoid the destruction that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz .iij. cercles ou .iiij. une petite fendure dou travers, entre les .ij. cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;	It is necessary then, when we want to cut the epiglote, that we cut it under three circles or four a small incision across, between the two circles or by the quantity of the incision of the siphac, not in the cartilage.
et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	and that one is suitable for the cutting of the epiglote so that there is no flesh, and the vessels are long in length.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit;	And if the master is fearful, it is necessary that he stretches the skin of the throat to all its length, then cuts the leather so that it comes to the channel; and stop the vessels of blood, if you see anything, and then cut the siphac, as we have said.
et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix;	and it is demonstrated by the cutting of the phlegm from the channel which leaps forth through the torn place and by the failure of the voice.
et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	and leave the wound open for a while.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour is passed about which one doubts strangulation, bring together the two lips of the wound of the leather, and sew it all alone without the cartilage; then administer medications that cause flesh to grow, until he is healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Abacus says one does not do this just yet until the throat is entirely stopped up, and the patient is judged to be dying, and the default leads to failure.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort;	Then cut off the epiglote because the patient cannot breathe, and he is breathing through the wound, and thus is preserved from death.
et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en .iij. jors ou en .iiij.	and for this the ancients command to leave the wound open until the evil of the disease has passed, and it passes in three days or four.
Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee;	And then they commanded to sew up the wound and heal, until it was healed.
et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist .i. coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon;	I saw a maiden take one knife and stick it in her throat, and cut off part of the channels of the body;
et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	and I was called to cure her, and I found her just as dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound and found the blood that had issued from it, and knew well that she had not cut the vein nor led forth but the throat, and the veins were flowing out through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee;	I hastened, and sewed up the wound, and healed her until she was whole.
et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition;	and nothing happened to the maiden except that she was restored to her voice, and returned afterwards to her condition.
por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	therefore I say that in the cutting of the epiglote there should be no fear.
de la grosse gorge	of the thick throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes;	This abscess is called "hernia of the throat", and it is a great abscess in the color of greenish-yellow, and it is very common in women.
et est selonc .ij. manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	and it occurs according to two manners: natural, and accidental; or the natural one has no fault.
Et li accidens est selonc .ij. manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere;	And the accidental is according to two manners, one of which resembles fat, and the other manner resembles an abscess that comes from an artery.
et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire:	and there is fear, and one should not dare to do anything but in that which is small, and prove and search everywhere.
se tu le trueves ausi com .i. nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point;	if you find it like one fat lump, and it cannot be brought to any vein, then cut it off, just as one cuts fat, and treat the rest of the body, if there is any.
et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	and search well throughout, and heal it as needed, until it is perfectly healed.
des nous	of fat
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances;	Many kinds of fat are, which I will tell all the likenesses;
et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	and it is necessary that I say the whole difference that is between fat and issue.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that issue is heat and fever sustained, until the ebullition has passed, and the putrefaction is complete; then the fever and heat subside.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient .i. syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros;	With the fat there is no heat or fever or pain, and contains one siphac, which is its own sack and is according to the color of the body, and begins like a greenish-yellow color, and becomes big.
et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	and they are according to two likenesses, either greasy or moist, and much of color are as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to the cure of fat, that you examine and inquire first about all the instruments which are called "entromissoires", according to what its form comes or chapter that follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme;	And the manner of inquiring about abscesses of fat is that you take or the moistest part that you find in the abscess, and turn your two points and points, until you know that the instruments have pierced the leather, then according to the size of the abscess.
puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	then extract the entromissoire, and take care in that which jumps forth.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes;	If moist corruption runs clear, no matter what its color may be, then do as I have said with other abscesses.
et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;	and if after the entromissoire no moisture comes, know that it is fat, so then cut it in crosswise, and take it up with pincers, and scrape off lightly from each part and ward off the coat where it lies that you may lead out the fat.
et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	and if you cannot pull it out whole, then cut it into pieces so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois;	For if anything remains, the fat will return many times.
et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if a little bit remains, and the wound troubles you, then fill the wound with some corrosive powders and close the wound, and put on soothing things for hot abscesses, and heal it with other remedies until it is healed.
et se li nous est grans, si cout les .ij. levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	and if the fat is large, then sew up the two lips of the wound, and heal it with those things that cause flesh to grow.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	and if the vein is opposed to you or another such thing that hinders and employs the leech of vitriol, let it stay for two or three days, until the wound purrs, and rest the ebullition of the blood; then return to cutting what remains of the fat.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de .iij. manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a .iij. quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et .i. qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de .iij. manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule;	Here is the translation of the first sentence:
et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule;	and they are like the needles used to sew sorceries, and they are made of citrine earth, or iron, or silver, and those that are yellow are more valuable, and they are more tried for black pitch to surround the sores of fistula;
et sont de .iij. manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	and they are of three kinds: great, middle-sized, and small, according to the quantity of the breadth of the holes.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures de .iij. manieres ausi;	The shapes of the warts are of many likenesses, as you see here: great, middle-sized, and small; and there are also warts that have two sores of three kinds.
et si a oncines qui ont .iij. corbeures, et sont ausi de .iij. manieres; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de .iij. manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	and there are also warts that have three sores and are of three kinds; and there are also warts that have two sores, and single warts with one sore, and they are all necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf;	The heads of these ones are cutting, and there are some that do not cut more than one side, from which we strip the nerves, because that's why we don't cut the vein or the nerve.
et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes;	and these introgressors are the leeches wrapped in cloth, so that the patient does not feel them during the opening of abscesses.
et sont de .iij. manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois;	and they are of three kinds: great, small, and middle-sized, as you see;
et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus;	and one does not use them at all except in a warm place, such as thighs, and arms, and armpits, and in similar places.
et aucune fois fait on .i. autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	and sometimes one makes another small instrument, resembling a scorpion's stinger, according to this form, with which one stops blood.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and one puts it sometimes in the place that bleeds at the puncture of veins and arteries, and sometimes returns according to this great form.
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme;	Sometimes the armpits of some men swell when they begin to be corrupted, so much that they seem like a woman's armpits.
et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne b. jusques a .g.:	and remain ugly and swollen, and whoever wishes to cure them, it is necessary to be made according to this form of the line b up to 7.
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then strip the fat, and fill the wound with medicinal ointment wrapping it in cloth, then bring together the two lips of the wound by sewing them shut, and care for it until it is healed.
et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en .ij. costelz desus, par .ij. semblans fendures;	and if the armpit bends downward, and is moistened by its size as it is in women, then make a cut above it in two folds, through two similar openings;
de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.;	so that one is joined to the other at the end of each and makes a single line, where the larger line contains the smaller according to this form, from line b up to line g.
puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les .ij. levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then strip the skin that is between the two lips, and remove the fat, and apply what we have said about stitching and powders, and all that is necessary for the care, until it is healed.
et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif;	and if it is not healed or the incision is not fully made because the patient does not rest or due to the corruption of blood, then it is necessary that you fill the wound with moist cotton in corrosive oil.
et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	and leave it like that until it dissolves the remaining and fat, then care for it until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	of abscesses in the buttocks
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come from under the buttocks are types of hard scrofulas or boils, and some contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those that contain moisture then need to be cut according to this form, from line b up to line g:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus that is in the abscess has been emptied, then fill the wound with old cotton and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton and care for it with ointment suitable for this purpose until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess is like a scrofula, then make it as we have said in scrofulous cuts, and if the wound bleeds pus, then apply fire cautery as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	of the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme;	When the artery is ruptured and the skin above it is sewn up, then abscesses often occur, and also it happens that the vein swells and becomes an abscess.
et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont;	and if one knows how to do so when it is due to the artery, then the abscesses are long and deep.
et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens .i. estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans;	and when you feel it in your sides, you feel one strangeness; and when it is due to the vein, then it appears as if it were going away from you.
et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	and it is foolish to cut this abscess, and especially when it is under the buttocks and armpits and at the neck and in many other places, and is very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc;	It is therefore necessary to avoid the treatment of fire, and the one who is at the head should also avoid it, and in the one who has swelling from an artery make a cut above the skin long.
puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte;	then work the incision on warts and part the artery from its sheath so that it is uncovered.
puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en .ij. leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des .ij. arteres qui sont en temples;	then insert a needle underneath one and make it pierce through to the other side, and bind the artery with a doubled thread in two places, according to what I have taught you in the extraction of the two arteries that are in the temples.
puis point le leu qui est entre les .ij. liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme;	then prick the place that is between the two ligatures with an introgressor until the blood comes out which is there, and loosen the abscess.
puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient;	then apply the treatment that brings pus, until the ligature falls.
puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then care for it with ointment suitable for this purpose, until it is healed.
et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir,	and if the abscess is due to the swelling of the vein, then it is necessary that you daub with your hand whatever you can of the abscess onto all the skin.
puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait .i. fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit;	then insert the needle underneath the place that you hold in your hand, and make it pierce through, and have one doubled thread, so that you pull it from the other side.
puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de .ij. pars as .ij. chiés dou fil;	then bind the abscess, as I have told you, or tie one end of the doubled thread to the two jaws of the other end.
et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout .i. fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en .iiij. leus;	and if you doubt that the thread will not come out too far, then rebend another needle along all of the thread underneath all the abscess to the incision of the first needle, and bind the threads in three places.
puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez;	then cut the abscess until the excess comes out, then cut the excess of skin and leave what is bound.
puis met sus .i. drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then put a moist cloth soaked in wine and oil on it, then apply treatments of tents and ointments until it is healed.
des apostemes des ners	Abscesses of the nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Just like abscesses come in an artery and a vein, abscesses of the nerves come when they are wounded or from excessive hard work, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est .i. grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor;	And these things happen more often at the shoulders and elbows, and in all places where there are joints, and it is a great abscess, and its color seems like the color of flesh, and it is accompanied by many dispositions without pain.
et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur;	and when one is strained strongly, then the patient feels pain, and it is not in the deepest part of the body, but just below the skin.
et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction;	and it can be felt on all sides, and does not go forward or backward, nor above or below, and the one who is in joints should not be struck by iron: by chance there may be contraction.
et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	and he who is in the head or forehead, feels the skin on the forehead.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine;	If the abscess is small, one should hold it with forceps and cut its root;
et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if it is great, one should suspend it with a ligature, and scrape it, then cut it out and close the wound by sewing, and care for it until it is healed.
des grosses boces pendans	of large hanging boils
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans;	Sometimes it happens in bellies and not elsewhere on the body, and it is a disease called "fungus" by its resemblance to those things, and is the root subtle, and the head large; and there are some small and very great ones.
et je vis .i. home qui en avoit .ij. ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	and I saw one man who had two in his belly which were more like fungi than anything else, and there was no difference between them, and they were white, and had a small root, and were split open, and were rotting with moisture.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un .xviij. onces pesant, et en l’autre .vj. З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine;	I cut them and found in one 18 ounces, and in the other 6, and the works of incision are such that you look to see if the patient is moist, and the color of the artemisia is white and moist and of subtle root;
si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu. Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer;	so cut at the forehead, and have fire cauterization present with you; for when cutting, there often comes a great abundance of blood, and if it overflows, then hasten with the cauterizer.
et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent .i. fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse .ij. jors;	and if you see the patient panting and fearful of the incision with iron, take one well-made linen thread, and tie the artemisia as we have said, and leave it for two days;
et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet,	and then restrain it, and do not cease to strain the linen thread until it cuts the artemisia, and choose by it the least labor; and if the roots are large, be afraid to cut yourself with the same knife for the belly, but you can well cut half of it.
puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	then cauterize it so that it does not relapse; then care for the wound, and take care that you do not cut the artemisia which is of bad color, poor sense, and little regard.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For it is an enchanted abscess, and I will come to the care of ulcers later.
quant li boude ist fuer	when the bread is burned
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit;	If the appearance of bread comes from a cautery of wound or opening of syphilis, and is on the belly and in some of the bowels, just as it happens in other wounds, or from blood which flows from veins or arteries according to what has been said before, or from windiness;
et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	and if it is from the wound of syphilis and from the opening of the bowels, then the color of the abscess is similar to the color of flesh, and it is a light thing without pain, and appears with various openings.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is because of the opening of the intestine, then it is even more diverse, and when one presses it at its sides it swells up, and then returns, and by chance it becomes hardened, and greatly enlarges at the entrance to the bath and from excessive labor.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit;	And if it is because of moisture, it is a light thing, and appears clearly when you press it with your hand, nor does it constrain; and if it is because of blood, then it appears by these signs as a large and hard abscess, and is fixed according to a quantity.
et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	and if it is because of windiness, then it is tender to the toucher, and the works are such that you look to see if the appearance is from blood of the artery, or vein, or windiness.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure. Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	It is necessary that you leave the cure alone. For there is doubt and fear, as I have said in the chapter on abscesses, concerning the artery and vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude;	And if the appearance is from the intestine or the bowels, it is necessary that you command the patient to hold his breath, and be stretched out straight, then sign by pointing all around the bread.
puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains,	then command him to sit quietly between your hands,
puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile,	then go around the place that you have signed at all the forehead.
puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine;	then lift half of the abscess above to the great ligature;
puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz;	then tie it around with a strong thread or a cord of firm silk tightly, and let the ends of the ligature be secured.
puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine;	then work on the half of the abscess that is extended above the ligature, and thrust your finger index into it, and probe the intestine.
se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre;	if you find it caught by the ligature, then loosen it, and thrust the intestine to the back of the belly.
et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit;	and if you find the bowels, then take hold of them with a ligature, and cut off the superfluity.
et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren .ij. aguilles, et i boute .ij. fors filz, et boute les .ij. aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier;	and if the artery or vein gives you resistance, go around it well, then come back to your work and take two needles, and put two strong threads on them, and put the two needles around what you have done in a cross shape as if you were piercing.
puis estrain l’aposteme en .iiij. leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi;	then strain the abscess in four places above the needles, and if you see, remove the needles, and leave the place until it purrs, and choose the dead flesh by itself.
