ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit;	or you cut it when it is subtle and purrs, then care for what needs to be done, and heal the abscess as we have said.
et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	and extract the blood or moisture that you find, then care for the place as it needs to be done, and bind the place.
dou chancre	of the ulcer
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have said in the division the signs of ulcers, and how one should work by medicines, and how one should avoid the cure of iron. And we say that an ulcer is born in the marrow, and great caution must be taken in its care. The ancients said that when ulcers are on a place or can be removed like those on the breasts, and in the armpits, and in similar places, and it should be entirely removed at the beginning; and when they are old and large, one must not approach them, for I never saw anyone heal from it; nor did anyone before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide .i. boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Et the operations, when they are in place or can be removed, as we said, is that you purge the patient with black bile at times; then make him healthy if he has manifest repletion; then prepare the patient a good location to perform the operation; then throw out your needles or chancre, and remove the hair from all parts, and the bone from all parts without leaving anything behind; and let the blood run freely and press well on the area with your hand or something, and if the bleeding is contrary to the incision of the artery or vein, then cauterize until the bleeding stops; then cure another cure until he is healed.
de ydropisie	De ydropisie.
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces .ij. semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer:	We have already said in the division the similarities of dropsy, and how the assembly of water is made, and the signs of each similarity, and the cure that is done by medicines, and that which is cured by iron: it is all said; and one should not touch iron on these two similarities: that is to say, tympanites and yposarche, for it is a deadly thing; therefore when you medicate this similarity of dropsy which is called "ecclites" of medicines, and the cure does not benefit, then look if the patient is weak, or if he has another disease besides dropsy, such as indigestion and similar things; do not touch iron then, for there is doubt; and if you see the patient of strong virtue, and he has no other disease than dropsy alone, and he is neither too old nor too young, then you should work thus:
lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme: Et soit trenchans de .ij. pars. a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier;	Hold the patient straight upon your hands, and the attendants press the belly out to the lowest part of the stomach, then take the spine needle according to this form: And let it be cut off at two parts, to a point; and yet not so far that it can come just to the intestine when you put it in, and do not let it hurt.
puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude .iij. dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude .iij. dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu;	Then look if the dropsy is flowing towards the intestines: if so, it is necessary that you cut into the stomach three fingers' breadth below the nipple; and if the dropsy is due to liver disease, then make your incision on the left side of the stomach three fingers' breadth; and if it is due to wind, then make it on the right side, and it is not necessary for the patient to lie on the incision so that the superfluities do not flow towards that weak place.
puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme: Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz .i. petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, .iij. pertus; et .ij. d’autre part, et .i. d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	Then pierce the whole skin with the instrument, and plug it, and lift your hand to all the spine between the skin and the sac as when shearing to the length of a fingernail or thereabout; then pierce the sac until the spine comes to the seventh rib, and that is the place of water; then treat the instrument thus, and plug this instrument which is the form: And it resembles a subtle silver chain, and is made of iron or light archaic metal, and has in the lower part one small perforation; and on one side three perforations; and two on the other side, and one on the other; and the handles are cut like a feather, and that is the form of the incision from which the writers shape the feather.
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort;	At the top is the alembic, so that when the instrument comes to water, it then pours down on the instrument; empty it therefore by half or a third part, for if you empty more than it is necessary in this hour, perchance the patient will die from the resolution of his spirit from the arm, or he will faint, or he approaches death.
mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit;	But empty it according to the quantity of his virtue, and according to what the dispositions of the patient's virtue signify, and his pulses; then treat the instrument and retain the water, and it is retained now for the reason that blocks the perforation which is on the sac, as I have spoken, so that you pierce in this manner; then recommence the instrument the next day, if you see the patient suffering thus, and draw out a small quantity of water.
fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue. Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	Do this day by day, and take care not to pour out too much water at once. And if you doubt about the patient, and you leave too much water, then the cure of sepulture or sand will heat up, and through excessive sweating or bathing and sunlight, and if it becomes black; and the cure of drying medicines until he is healed, and cauterize on the stomach and on the liver and on the spleen after the extraction of water, as I said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	of the stopping of the flow
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu. Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout .i. spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme: puis met ou pertus .i. clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi .iij. jors ou iiij. et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	Never are children born who do not have holes in the penis, or the holes are small, or it is not in its place. If this is so, then it is necessary that each spout is pierced very subtly according to this form: then put a subtle plug of cloth into the hole, and tie it and hold it thus for three days or four; and when he wants to urinate, then take out the plug, and let him urinate, and then put it back; and perchance there will be no need, for the urine that comes forth does not leave the plug closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera. Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those whose holes are small need the medicine of cloth plugs, as we have said, and it will expand. Those who do not have their hole in its place are hurt, for no one is born with a hole at the head of the penis, so they cannot urinate unless they lift their penis up; and they cannot flow because the matter cannot come to the opening, and that is a bad disease.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the way of working is that the patient lies on his back, and then place the head of the penis and cut it off like the shape of a feather, so that the hole opens in the middle, as it should; and take care not to let blood come out which comes many times, and if it does, then stop it with what stops bleeding, and cure the wound until he is healed.
des pustules de la verge	of the pimples of the penis
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a .i. oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times these pustules come on the penis, and it is an ugly appearance of flesh; and there are malignant and non-malignant ones; so it is necessary that you take them to a subtle poultice, and cut and clean all of them, then put a wet cotton cloth in Egyptian ointment; then treat with divine ointment until he is healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere. Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer. Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the pustule is malignant, with a bad color and smell, it is necessary that you apply fire cautery. When you have cut it open, and if the pustule is on the penis, and has part inside the skin and part outside, it is necessary that you remove the pustule that is inside first; and when it is closed, then cure what is outside. For when you cure them together, it is not assured that the head of the penis will not be pierced, and blackness and corruption will come into its place and on the scrotum; so it is necessary to remove everything that is black and corrupted, then smear with an ointment made from the rind of pomegranates and vetches, and then cure with other cures until he is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme: Li cauteres si aide as .ij. dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a .i. estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars;	And if bleeding occurs, then apply the lunar cautery according to this form: The cautery is helpful for two dispositions together: that is to say, for the bleeding of blood and for corruption; and if the head of the penis is corrupted and retracted, it is necessary that you tie or guide the penis with a cloth cord, and make the patient urinate through it; and when the skin is worn out at the head of the penis which has not been circumcised, or if there is a wound or aposteme, then it is necessary to cut off with a sharp instrument, as much as the ligaments are loosened, and free the head of the penis from all sides.
et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a .i. spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre .ij., et i met .i. subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	et se c'est grief chose de deviser ceu, if it is a grievous thing to discuss this;
de la circoncision	of the circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not the cutting off of continuity like other wounds; however when we do this work of our own will, and properly on children, it is necessary that we make the best work, and the most gentle for salvation.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancient ones did not speak of circumcising their children, because they do not use it in their law, and we have only what we have acquired through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor .i. dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a .ij. toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I have seen the greatest part of masters and sages who performed circumcision around one inch, with force, and with all a new novaculum; thus it was done because there are two skins, and by chance if you cut above and leave that below.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Then it recovers, and the pain is doubled, and the point of the member at the circumcision is not assured; and the purification of the wound by chance escapes the iron, and hinders the work, and many times so that they do not need purification and I have seen this.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	Of the purification which is done with force to all the thread I have found the goodness of the experiment, for the forces cut equally well above and below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en .i. tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	For when you press your hand, it cuts equally well in one stroke through the entire thickness of the skin; but let the thread be well stretched around the leather; and the manner of the first work is that you make the child think, if he understands, that you are not doing anything to him except tying the thread around the penis just so, and then you will leave it in all ways that you can.
puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz .i. poc a .i. autre liien; et la tien as .ij. dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les .ij. liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge;	then make it stand between your hands straight and point the forces between your hands or below your feet so that the child does not see them nor any of the instruments; then put your hand on the penis and blow or cut, and pull it up as high as the head of the penis is; then cleanse it well from the dirt that is gathered there, then tie a double thread to the signet and tie below one piece to another string; and hold it with two thumbs by the second ligature at the pouch and the right index, and cut between the two strings, then lift the edge above hastily and pull the head of the penis.
puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre .i. drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then let the blood flow little by little, for it is the mothers; and put powder on top and top, one layer glued with a yolk of egg cooked without water, mixed with rose oil, good and fresh, and leave it there until the next day, and cure it with another cure until it is healed.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The shape of the forces for purification is this: both heads should be held and cut off, and they should be equal in size like the fingers.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	the error of purification is when the knife bleeds within the incision; therefore it is necessary that you stretch it to your finger, so that the ligaments make an abscess; and cut equally, and if you cannot hold it with your finger, then hold it with forceps, and then cut.
Et s’il trespassent .iij. jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if it lasts three days and the part below the penis is swollen, then leave it so that the abscess becomes appeased, and lightly scrape off; then cut as you can move, and take care not to harm the part of the penis, for nothing will be hurt by this.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cure the ligament with sudden wound powder that we have said to treat about powders, and if you cut with the knife beyond measure and it goes above, then it will not harm; cure it then as we have said, until it is healed.
dou retenement de l’urine	of the retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division;	The retention of urine is due to obstruction of the kidney, or frozen blood, or bowel, or new flesh, or similar things that we have said in the division;
et se li urine n’est desliie, et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e;	and if the urine is not released and you see that the retention is due to the kidney which is in front or at the back of the bladder, it is necessary that the patient be bent over his knees; and have his feet placed on the back, and stretch out his belly from the part above the back, and strain the patient's abdomen as much as he can; and then constrains the necks of the bladder to express itself into the kidney above, so that the urine is released.
et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	and if it does not come as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then it is necessary that you administer extraction with all the instruments called "siringue", which is this form: and be made of subtle silver wire, like a bird's feather; and have a cane of one palm and a half long, and be subtle at the tip.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren .i. fil double, et lie au chief .i. poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus .i. siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede;	And the manner of the issue of urine is that you take a double thread, and tie it at the top to a piece of wool or cotton, and put the top of the thread into the syringe; and cut off the excess thread and put it up to the top of the syringe, then anoint the syringe with oil or butter and yolk of egg, and make the patient sit on a seat, and raise the bladder and penis with moist oil and olive oil and dry water.
puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine;	then gently put the syringe into the penis, until it reaches the root of the penis, then double the penis upwards towards the belly; then put the syringe forward just to the bladder, and let the patient feel that it is coming up to the empty thing, and this is not done in accordance with this order unless the guide or conductor is twisted; then pull out the thread all along the wool piece by piece, and the urine will follow the wool, then pull it out, and make the urine flow.
et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	and repeat the syringe until the bladder is emptied, and the patient is alleviated.
des maladies de la vessie	of the diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When bleeding or blood comes into the bladder, or corruption is gathered there, and you see it distilling waters and medicines, then make all the instrument that is called "clepsedre", and this is its form:
Elle est close, et si a .iij. pertus: .ij. d’une part, et .i. d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est;	She is closed and has three perforations: two on one side, and one on the other, as you see; and the threads are shaped so that the medicine can be poured in such a way that it stops up well the penis without addition, and then one can draw out the moisture, and pour when needed.
et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira;	and when you see pouring your medicines into the bladder, put the head of the syringe into the moisture, and draw out what is inside; then pull back strongly on the syringe; then the moisture will enter and come to the bladder now, so that the patient will feel it.
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	and this is the form of the subtle syringe with which one catheterizes the bladder: thus:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a .i. sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les .ij. seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe .i. poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie;	And it is of silver or archaic, and the head is higher; and below one side or the head lies; then take a sheep's bladder and put in the moisture that you see to be able to close the bladder, then tie between two breasts with a good double thread, and warm one part of that moisture over the fire; then pour the head of the closed container into the vein, then strain your hand on the bladder all the moisture having come, until the patient feels that that moisture has reached the bladder.
et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai .i. cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute .i. fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble .i. dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	And if you do not have a bladder, then take a piece of parchment and make one circle, and pierce it roundly around; then put a strong thread in these holes, then assemble the circle as one assembles a tile, and put inside what you see of oil and moisture and water, and tie it to the instrument; and do so as you did with the bladder, by pressing your hand until the moisture reaches the bladder.
de la piere	Of stone.
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have already said in the division the ways of stone, and also extraction together with medicines; and I have said the difference between the stone that is pierced by rain, and all the signs, and which stone one must operate on in size; and in the bladder, and in the vein; and I will tell you plainly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone that is pierced in the bladder happens more often to children, and it is a sign that water bursts forth from the bladder like water in its subtlety; and it appears hairy, and grates the patient's vein, and makes many sounds, and then renews itself; and many of these pierce the foundations; and is lighter the recovery of children until they are three years old, and is very grievous in old men, and is to those who are between young and old; and is the cure more light for those who have a large stone than for those who have a small one.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines. Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	And when we come to the cure, it is necessary first to purge the patient with a clyster, in order to draw out all the phlegm that is in the intestines. For it sometimes hinders seeking out the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche ded ens;	Then take the patient by the feet, and lift and move him downwards, so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder, and sometimes comes out from above; then make him sit between your hands prepared, and his hands be below his buttocks, so that the bladder is entirely declining downward; then search for it and touch it inside.
se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere. Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	If you feel the stone in its place, then hasten now to cut on the stone. And if it does not fall when touched all over, then wet your thumb and index finger with oil from your left hand, if the patient is a child, or your middle fingers, if the patient is young and complete; and put it into its foundation, and search for the stone, and when you feel it on your thumb, then bring it to the neck of the bladder; then press on top of your thumb, and push it forward where you see cutting.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And command the attendant to press the bladder with his hand, and tell him to stretch his right hand upwards towards the kidneys, and with his left hand, remove the skin that is below the kidneys in the part where you are making the incision; then push the spatula copiously, so as it forms.
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans;	And make it between what is between the kidneys and the foundation, not in the middle but beside the left flank; and be straight on top of the stone, and your thumbs be at the foundation, and make the incision so that it is wide behind and narrow inside, according to the quantity of the stone, not too large.
par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	By chance, the pressure may be so great that the stone jumps far away from your work; and know that there are some stones that have angles and margins: it is hard to get out; and there are others that are soft, like a gnat, and rounded, through which the issue is light.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li .i. estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge .i. poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole;	To that stone which has angles and margins, make the incision larger; and if it does not jump, then it is necessary to strain on the pincers that are like a file at the head, in order to grasp the stone so that it does not escape; or you put below one part of the instrument with a subtle curved point; and if you cannot manage it thus, then enlarge one part of the hole, and if the stone decorticates, then grip it with vitriol.
et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors. Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie. Car .ij. choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces;	And if there is more than one stone, then extract the largest one from the neck of the bladder, then cut above it, then draw it out, and the small ones afterwards if there are several. And if it is very large, then it must be split, and make a larger wound. For two things happen to the patient: either he dies, or his urine comes out soon on one side where the flesh cannot heal; but nevertheless you strive to extract, or to break off with pincers, until you draw it out in pieces.
et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus .i. drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	And when you have completed your work, then anoint the wound with incense, aloe, and dragon's blood, and apply it, and put on top one damp cloth soaked in oil and wine, or in oil and rose water and cold water, to soothe the hot aposteme; then revive the patient over his neck, and do not loosen the bandage until the third day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you loosen it, then arise the flesh with oil and water very well; then care for him with diaphrenic ointment and basilicon ointment, until he is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit;	And if apostemes, boils, and congealments of blood in the bladder occur, and it is retained by that urine, which flows in such a way that it does not jump with the urine: then put your thumb into the wound, and draw out that blood, for if it remains, it will corrupt the bladder and ruin it.
puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les .ij. cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	Then lift the wound with water and ice and silk, and help him in all ways that you know, until he is healed; and it is necessary that all the works you do to cure him, that you bind his two buttocks together, and assemble the medicines on the flesh.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure. Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	And if the stone is small, and it is in the urethra of the penis, and stuck inside, and urine cannot come out; then cure him as I say before, by cutting into the stone many times, or excuse yourself from cutting because of this cure. I have already proven it thus.
Pren .i. foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a .iij. angles fichiees en .i. tison:	Take one iron rod in the shape and form, with three angled tips fitted into one socket:
puis pren .i. fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge. Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides;	Then take a thread and tie it around the penis below the stone, so that it cannot come out into the bladder; then insert the rod gently into the penis until it reaches the stone; and turn the rod back and forth in the stone, bit by bit, until you can pierce the stone from the other side. And soon the urine will come, then press your hand on what remains of the stone that is inside the penis. It is then broken and jumps out with the urine, and the patient is healed.
et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie .i. fil desoz la piere et .i. autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les .ij. liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	et if you cannot do this for any reason that prevents it, then take one thread under the stone and another above, then make the rod next to the stone between the two strings, then pull it tight and untie the string and clean the congealed blood that is in the wound; and cure him until he is healed.
de la piere des femmes	of the stone of women
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por .iij. choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	Often it happens that the stone is lodged in women, and if it does happen, then the cure is grievous, and it is defended against three things: one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a well-informed woman who will reveal herself to midwives, especially when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a.	And the third manner is that perhaps one cannot find a well-informed woman in this art of medicine; and the fourth manner is that the stone of the woman is more deeply seated than that of man, which is why it is necessary to make a deeper incision, and there is great fear.
Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier .i. caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere;	And if necessity demands this of you, then it is necessary that you take a well-informed midwife, and find one who knows the truth, and if you cannot find one, then take one chaste and subtle midwife; and present to her a wise old woman in the life of women, or a woman who knows part of the art, and command her to do what you command regarding the examination of the stone.
et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	and look very closely to see if the woman is a virgin: then it is necessary that she push her uterus or foundation and seek out the stone; and if she finds it, then constrain it under her uterus, and command her to push her uterus or the patient's uterus, and grasp her left hand firmly on the bladder.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite;	If she finds it, then it is necessary that she move it gradually from the entrance of the bladder to below, until it comes to the root of the thigh; then strike on the stone at the root of the thigh against the middle of the womb, where it is most apparent, and feel the stone in that part; and do not move her uterus above or below the stone, and make the incision at the first small one.
puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains. si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	then push the right in the incision, if you feel the stone so far back in the wound that the stone can come out freely, and know that many kinds of stones are: namely, small and great and rough and smooth, long and rounded, and those with ridges; and know their likenesses to know the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre;	And if the blood overflows, then put vitriol broth at the place, and hold it there for an hour until the blood is stopped; then return to your work, until the stone is out, and have the instruments that I told you in the extraction of the stone from men to aid you in your work.
et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	and if the blood overflows, and it is from the artery that has been cut, then put powder on the place and the strain of tents and bandages, and do not start again with these things, and leave the stone alone and do not pull it out except by chance the patient would die; then cure the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood is appeased and the swelling subsides, then return to your work until the stone is out.
de hernie carnouse	of fleshly hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit .i. autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	The white sac is nothing else than an accumulation of moisture or whitish fluid, which is located under the key of the womb, that contains the egg; and it is called "syfac", and sometimes it properly belongs to the membrane of the egg, if one thinks that it is another egg; and it is the skin of the womb between the white sac that we have said; and this does not happen unless there is no way.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this ramification is from weakness that comes to the womb, and it spreads out that matter.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus;	And sometimes it comes from percussion on the womb, and this moisture has many colors: or it is declining towards yellow, or it is without red, or black, or whitish water, and it happens more often;
et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, .i. poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	and these are the signs to know this assembly, for if it is the white sac that we have said, then there is an abscess near, a long one like the figure of an egg, and does not open the womb, because it has moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef;	And if there is moisture in the proper membrane, then it is an abscess near with a part of the egg, and because of this one thinks that it is another egg;
et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	and if the moisture is between the skin of the womb and the white sac, then one can sense it well; therefore when you wish to know the color of the moisture, test all the surrounding quadrants, so that the shape appears as before.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	Accordingly, what comes after the quadrants, judge what is inside.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz;	And when we cure it with fire, then it is necessary that the patient be healed according to our power and the replenishment of their body; then apply oil on their back, on something a little high, and place many cloths underneath.
puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des .ij. costelz dou keur des coions;	then sit on their left side, and command the attendant to sit at the right, and extend the rod to one of the two sides of the womb.
puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir;	then take the spatula left, and cut through the skin of the womb from one end to the other, and be your incision straight and level with the white sac, and scrape it subtly according to our power.
puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a .i. large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue;	then pierce the white sac with water to a small opening, and extract all the water, and then place your fingers and stretch the white sac upwards; and do not touch the womb, but only the white sac itself; cut it into pieces or as needed, in a subtle manner, so that if you do not cut it well, the water will return.
et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les .ij. leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if the egg bursts forth from your work, then put it back in its place when you have completed the work of the white sac; then assemble the two leaves of the womb to a seam, and then cure it as with other wounds, until he is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the egg corrupted by another disease, then it is necessary that you tie off the vessels that are suspended, doubting the dislodging of blood; then cut the womb at all the suspensory parts, and extract the egg, and cure it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en .ij. parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont .ij. ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset;	And if the water is assembled in two parts together, know that these are two stones; then cut the other part equally as you did the first one, and dry out the blood, and put a moist linen cloth soaked in rose oil into the wound.
et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les .ij. coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	and put another moist linen cloth soaked in wine and oil, and place it on the two wombs, and place double cloths above them, and tie it with all the thread that is according to this form.
Puis pren .ij. drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les .ij. angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier;	Then take two cloths and use them to wrap around the woolly yarn in this shape and have them sewn together at the waistband of the braies, and one of the straps will lie on the foundation up to the back, and the other on the part of the finger; and another strap will be placed on top of the two armpits, and all assembled with the restraint in the loop of the braier.
et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes .i. cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers;	And sometimes medicine is made with this wick of a fire cauterization in place of iron surgery, and it is that you take one subtle cautery knife, and cut the skin of the testicles, and be heated as we have said, so that the white gallstone that contains water becomes uncovered.
si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	Take the cauterization according to this form, and pierce that gallstone with fine needles, and scrape it off with a hot subtle cauterization.
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille;	And cut it in all ways that you can, until you have removed everything; and be sure that the fire does not touch the egg; and know that this work is more safe; and beware of disfiguring blood, and take care as much with the works of surgery.
et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	And if nothing contradicts you, or abscess forms or disfigurement of blood or anything else, then care for what contradicts you, according to what has been said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai,	And if the patient is fearful and does not wish to endure this work because of its horribleness, then administer a perforation, as I tell you, and know that when you are well certain by the signs that we have said, the wick is burnt out.
si fai seoir le malaide sus .i. siege leveit; puis perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer;	So seat the patient on a light stool; then pierce the abscess in the lower part of the spatula-like space, and put the perforation through the length of the body; and make the holes wide so that all the water can flow freely.
puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee;	Then put cotton on the place and tie it, and let the remaining water run off, then care for it until the wound is healed.
et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge .i. poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés .vj. mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	And if the white cloth does not let the water come out of the mouth of the wound, then it is necessary that you put a pin or an instrument with which one treats the water of those suffering from dropsy, as described before; and enlarge the wound a little, and know that the water returns, and is assembled after six months or so, and when it is assembled as before, and thus the patient will pass their days.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the testicles
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse;	Know that in the cutting of this wick there are many dispositions to fear, therefore it seems to me that it is better to leave it alone.
et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	and I will tell you the work and the likenesses of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I say then that many abscesses come to the body, and indeed to the testicles; and this is by many cases.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion;	It is known by excessive bitterness and ague, which spreads to the testicles, or from striking;
et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief;	and it is the color of the abscess according to the color of the body; and there is no pain found, and it is a grievous abscess.
et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	and by chance some grievous abscesses are fearful and piteous, of a foul color, and sometimes come from a rupture or an inflammation of the vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois;	When it is by a rupture of an artery, then it is known by the hot abscesses when you press them with your fingers.
et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	and it does not seem good to touch it.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois,	He who is afflicted with an inflammation of the vein is known by his appearance when touched by the fingers.
et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars;	and can do well to make a cut on this shape, and on other joints.
et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	and it is that you cut the skin of the testicles, then lift the egg upwards and pull out the white gallstone, and deliver the suspensory ligament from all parts of the egg.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope;	If the egg is already softened with these joints, then it is necessary to pull out the egg and the skin.
et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	and if it is hard in the gallstone or in what is inside the vessels, then it is necessary to deliver all that tension and cut again afterwards.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the birth of the joint is at the back, then it is necessary to cut all of it and extract the egg, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your work is completed, then apply the wound with wool soaked in rose oil and wine, and care for it with other remedies until it is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the testicles
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a .i. borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions,	This is an abscess wrapped in a wrapping similar to a bunch, with the softening of the testicles,
et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait;	and if the patient groans grievously when he walks.
et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant,	and the treatment of this disease is just as fearful as that which has been said before.
et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	and yet we will tell you the work of it, according to what the ancient ones did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois,	It is necessary that you seat the patient on a light stool, then tie the suspensory ligament of the testicles down to your fingers.
a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment;	to all the vessels that are near the penis, and tie them tightly, and stretch them forth.
puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert,	then cut in the spatula-like space, cutting wide across the traverse place between the vessels, until they are uncovered.
et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples;	and then scrape from each side, as we have said in the extraction of arteries that are in the temples;
puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait .i. fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief;	then insert a needle where there is a double thread, and tie it to the first place where the vein has come forth, and tie it again at the other end.
puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues;	then cut them in a straight direction, according to the length of the body, and pull out the corrupted moisture.
puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions;	then care for the wound as with others that are opened up, so that no vessel may bleed which nourishes one of the testicles.
car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz;	for if it does not come from evil, and all the vessels come forth with blood, then it is necessary to pull out the testicles from all the vessels.
si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	so that the testicles do not lose their nourishment due to the incision of the vessels, and dry up and cannot help themselves.
de la routure dou syfac	of the rupture of the gallstone
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions;	The outcome of this wick is by the section that comes out of the gallstone, or the extension above the belly in the part of the armpits, therefore the intestines descend from that rupture to one of the testicles.
et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces .ij. manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses;	and this rupture is either from the gallstone or from its extension, and comes in two ways due to many causes: either by striking, or by jumping, or by roaring, or by lifting a heavy burden, and by similar things.
et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement;	and the signs when it is of the extension of syphilis, so it has a little and a little, over a long time, and does not come suddenly;
et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	and the abscesses are equal down to the deepest part, because the syphilis presses on the intestine.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs are when it is of the section of syphilis, which brings sudden pain at the beginning, and there are diverse abscesses appearing underneath the skin close by, and this is because of the issue from the intestine and the body being drained of the syphilis.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And sometimes the abscesses burst with the intestine, and are retained there, and cause great pain to suffer in the patient, especially when it is pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these iron treatments, there is fear, for which one must take heed.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir;	And the manner of the work is that you instruct the patient to insert his hand into the wound as far as possible and into the intestine.
puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes;	then press down on his throat between your hands, and lift up the ribs;
puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc;	then straighten the back above, and cut away all the skin of the long intestines.
puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir;	then thrust your fingers into the intestines of the wound, according to what you need to open it up, and make them such that the pus can come out.
puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars;	then scrape away the syphilis that is underneath the skin of the intestines, until the white syphilitic discharge is uncovered on all sides.
puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac,	then press your two fingers into the intestine in the place where the white syphilis is underneath the skin of the egg, and between the second syphilitic discharge.
et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille;	and depart what is behind the egg, and between the second syphilitic discharge; then move your right hand into the intestine of the intestines, and straighten the white syphilis up to your left hand, and lift the egg away from all the syphilitic discharge towards the navel.
et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement;	and instruct the assistant to stretch the egg upwards, and loosen what is above behind the bond.
et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz;	and search with your hands if there is any part of the intestine or white syphilitic discharge that has been covered, and if you find anything, then push it into the belly underneath.
puis pren une aguille ou il ait .i. gros fil fait de .x. filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait .iiij. filz;	then take a needle with a thick thread made of ten threads, and insert it in the back part of the syphilitic discharge, which is after the skin of the intestines; after the navel, then cut the knots that appear from the threads, as long as there are four threads.
puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de .ij. pars;	then assemble them one on top of the other in the shape of a cross, and tie the syphilitic discharge, which we said is underneath the skin of the intestines, with a strong bond from two parts.
puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de .ij. pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne;	then envelop the knots of the threads and tie them together from two parts, so that no vessels that nourish them can enter in there, lest the abscess grow again.
et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc .ij. dois de celui, et aprés ces .ij. liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi;	and place the bond above according to the first long band of two fingers of that one, and after these two bonds leave the syphilitic discharge which is underneath the skin of the intestines a quarter of an inch.
et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant;	and after all the rest according to the rounded shape that the egg bears; then cut in the part which is underneath the skin of the intestines, as long as the healthy flesh appears, and the bowel comes out, as we have said before.
puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	then apply moistened wool in oil to the wounds, and put it on the abscess, and apply the bond that we have said.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And sometimes the white syphilitic discharge that we have said is cauterized after incision, out of fear of blood dismemberment.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece;	For this often happens, and leave the bond until it falls of its own accord; and if it tarries in falling, then be raised with hot water, and put on what we have said, until it falls.
puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	then treat the wound with another treatment, until it is perfectly healed.
de hernie carnouse	of a fleshly hernia
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this recipe I never saw anyone who dared to perform the treatment by fire.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz;	And the ancients say that it is done in such a way as the recipe which is together with life, in this manner that you tie the vessels, after the navel above lightly underneath.
puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then cut in the middle, and treat the abscess of those who work, until the vessels bleed; and cure it as we have said, until it is healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres;	Sometimes a rupture comes in the intestines, as we have said, and opens up the loops; and none of the intestines come out to the intestines, and if any do come out, it is small, and repair all hours.
et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent;	and even though it stays too long in this position, the wound or syphilitic discharge grows, until the intestines come out.
et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert;	and this happens because of the extension of the syphilis that is at the intestines, as we have said, for it is extended, then softened and inflated the loops and opens up.
et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere:	and the cure is by cauterization, as we have said before; and never is cured by fire in this way:
et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de .iij. dois;	and it is that the patient lies sovining on his back between your hands, then cut the loop of the rupture inflated from wide according to the quantity of three fingers.
et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac;	and then extract the syphilitic discharge that is underneath the skin which ensues, and take the cloth and place it on the loop appearing above the syphilitic discharge.
et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les .ij. leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre;	and press it to the depth of the belly, then cut the two loops appearing above the syphilitic discharge on top of the cloth, and cut one and the other.
puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines;	then take out the head of the cloth, and do not cut the syphilitic discharge nor extend the egg or any other thing, as I have made known to you in the treatment of the recipe for the intestines.
puis le cure par la cure des plaies. Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	then treat it with the treatment of wounds. And when you cut the threads, make sure to dress and treat the wound, until it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The syphilitic discharge is constricted and has no appearance in the rupture, and the cauterization is more useful in this place, and closer to salvation.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the skin of the intestines
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a .iij. costures ou .iiij. fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Many times the skin of the intestines becomes soft in some people because the contents inside are softened, and it can be seen; and it is necessary, when one wants to cure it, that one makes the patient lie on his back, and cuts the soft skin on top of the natural skin. Then assemble the two lips with a seam, and if you see, cut off the excess of the soft skin at three or four seams. Then cut between the seams, and treat it as other wounds, until it is healed, and the thread bleeds.
dou chastrement	The punishment
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes. Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc .ij. manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.  En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.  Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a .i. cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	The punishment. It is ordained in our law that it should be done thus, and I would rather not speak of it in this book at all; and it is only necessary for two reasons: one is that the apothecary will respond to questions and provide a cure when asked; and the other is because we often have need of punishing certain beasts to help us, such as oxen and sheep and goats and other beasts. I say then that punishment is done in two ways: or by attraction, or by division. In the way that we do it by attraction, we make the beast sit in hot water until the testicles are softened and pliable; then we take them in our hand until they are restored and no longer felt. On the subject of castration: one must first skin the beast, and press the hide of the testicles into your left hand; then tie a suspender and hit each ball with one blow, when you have well skinned it; and leave some of the soft and subtle sac which is above the vessels; and this manner of punishment is more severe than that which is done by attraction, because in the attraction something may remain of the testicles, for which the beast desires lust; then cure the wound until it is healed.
des hermofrodites	of hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc .ij. manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les .ij. coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.  Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et .ij. coions.  Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	Hermaphrodites are in two ways like men: one is when between the two testicles it appears as much as the figure of a woman's nature, or it has hair and at times urinates in court. And the other way is in women, who have on the finger as much as a penis and two testicles. And the cure for men and women is that you cut out the lumped-up parts and cure them like other wounds; in the second manner, of men whose urine jumps through the skin of the testicles, there is no cure.
de la tentigene	of the tenting
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure. Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee». Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Tenting is a lumped-up part on the natural part, as much as it is too ugly to see; and some women have it as big as a hand, and that is the cure.
