It is necessary that you remove the superfluity of the tenting with your hand or with forceps, and cut it lightly; and do not go too far in, lest blood does not come forth, then treat it with another treatment until it is healed; and there is another lump that is born at the mouth of the womb, and fills, and by chance jumps forward, and it is according to the likeness of a cow, and for that reason they called it the "cow disease" in ancient times. It is necessary that you cut it, as we have said the tenting, and treat it until it is healed.
de erratique	of the erratic one
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile. Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait. S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as .ij. leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes .ij. dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les .ij. leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder. Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte. Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.  Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez. Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	Erratic is when the natural part of a woman is not perceived, or if the opening is small; and it is caused by birth, or by accident due to disease that has occurred; or it is caused by a lumped-up part, or subtle or thick syphac, and it is made in front, back, or side, or wherever; and it hinders conception, childbirth, and perhaps the flowering of breasts; and knowledge of this is gained through the examination of the belly. If the swelling appears nearby, go to your knees or on your rump. If it is due to subtle syphac, and it is close to the two kidneys, hasten and do thus: put your two hands together, and have the woman sit on her back, spreading her legs; then the two kidneys will form, until the subtle syphac is drained, and the swelling will be gone. Then take flax, moisten it in oil, and apply it to the skin, and have the woman lie down each day, so that she cannot coagulate. And if the syphac is hard and thick, you must cut it off at the spatula-like shape of myrtle leaves. If the swelling is from a born part, suspend it with forceps and cut it; and use medicines that stop blood flow, such as aconite, dragon's blood, incense, together with many eggs; then administer a wide belt of cloth, so that the wound cannot coagulate; and thus it will be long-lasting. Then apply a linen tent; and cure it with other treatments until it is healed. And when a born part comes in the womb, you must cut it according to this method, unless it is enchanted apostemes. For at an enchanted aposteme that is in the womb, one should not touch it with fire.
des emorroides	of hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation. Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer. Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer. Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai .i. emplaustre sus son dos. Et se il estainche, c’est boin. Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.  Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a .i. chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Hemorrhoids are openings of veins that are not accustomed to being cut, and when they become old they become thickened; and we have said in the division what their likenesses and signs are, and I will say here those that receive a cure. I say that hemorrhoids and thickened flesh, when they are made in the womb, and do not appear to be felt, there is no cure by fire. Those that are at the mouth of the womb can be felt, are those that can be cured. It is necessary then that you put the woman in a cold house, then set the altar-thickened flesh with pincers, and cut it at its roots, then powder on medicines that restrain blood flow, such as aconite and dragon's blood and incense, and similar things; then bathe her feet for an hour, then put her in cold water; and if bleeding comes forth, make her sit in a decoction of sumac and pomace skin and galls and similar things, and then take barley flour, mix it with honey and oil, and apply .i. plaster to her back. And if it stays, that is good. If not, have her wear air-filled bladders on her back and at her breasts so as not to feel fire; then take flax, moisten it in plantain juice or elderberry juice with old wine, and apply it to the skin. And when the aposteme subsides, cure the skin of ointment until it is healed; and that which is called "albathir" is red, and is like a rough head, so it must be cut as I said for thickened flesh; and then cure it until it is healed.
des apostemes de la marris	of the womb apostemes
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division. Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.  Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege, et ait .ij. petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument. Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés .ij. jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.  Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	Various types of apostemes come into the womb, such as chancre and piercing aposteme, and herpes and estiomenes and fistules and hemorrhoids and hot aposteme, and many other diseases that I have said in the division. It is necessary then that I say about the hot aposteme that comes into the womb, which is not one of the apostemes that wraps around the bowels; and if you want to know how to work with fire, look first if the aposteme is inflamed at its beginning, and full of heat and fever, and if it becomes red when you can see it. Then do not hasten to cut, but let the pain subside until the discomfort is alleviated; and then make the patient sit on a stool, with two small stools or cushions that they lean on, and have them support their back and bring their legs together in front of the other leg; and spread their thighs apart, and put their arms under their knees, and tie them well with a good cord; then apply the bellows to the right side, and there place the instrument used to work on the mouth of the womb, from which the form will come forth; and it is necessary that when you apply this instrument, you place the first ring to know the depth of the womb, so that what enters through the instrument does not go deeper than it should, and does not harm the patient. And if the instrument is larger, it is necessary to cover the depth of the womb with drapes, so that the instrument does not cause discomfort; and it is necessary to place the bellows' horn above and hold the instrument.
de l’enfantement	of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment. Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	It is necessary for the midwife to first know the figure of natural childbirth, and the signs that are when you see the woman hastening downward, and desiring to give birth; then the child hastens to come forth; then know that this childbirth is according to the natural figure, and the issue is below its head, and the secondine with it; and when you see these signs, it is necessary to press lightly on her belly so that the child may come out soon; for when it descends above its head, the secondine comes with it, and the afterbirth of superfluities is purged by good purification; and this which comes otherwise does not come naturally. For sometimes it comes on its feet, or comes forth from the body or from the shoulders, or comes below the navel, and is converted by chance onto the neck, and by other bad figures; therefore it is necessary for the midwife to be wise and subtle in these things, and beware of error and deceit, and I will show you all the figures how one should help her.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child comes forth above its head in natural birth, and the woman gives birth grievously, and her strength is weak, then make her sit on a stool or hold her up by women; and have her nature bathed in oil or fenugreek cooked, and then give the midwife a small spatula-like instrument whose shape is as follows:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.Et se les .ij. mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus .i. siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	and cut the afterbirth, and scrape at its angle until the moisture that is inside it flows out; and take hold of the woman's belly as long as the child descends, and if it does not descend, then it is necessary to purge the woman with fenugreek with sesame oil; then make her press down and stretch with condiment, and keep her mouth and nose for an hour: now the child has come out. And if both hands come forth, then it is necessary that you gently guide them in and out; and if they cannot enter, then put the woman on a stool, and lift up her feet high; then put the stool back down on the ground, and hold onto the woman so she does not stumble; and if the hands cannot enter, and the child has died, then cut off the hands at the joint that is before mentioned, and extract the child, and guide it equally.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piez	of the issue of the child on its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut;	When the child comes out on its feet, then it is necessary to push it up.
et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz;	and then turn it slowly and carefully until it is even.
puis preigne .i. des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	then take one of its feet and stretch it slowly and carefully.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi;	Until it reaches the crotch, then instruct her to press down and stretch with condiment.
si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	If it jumps forth, may God will it.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it does not come forth as we have said, then turn it slowly and carefully until it is according to the natural figure.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it will be easy.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons dit, si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en .i. mortier;	And if it does not come forth as we have said, then take fenugreek juice, and sesame oil, and boiled gum, and grind all in one mortar;
et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement,	and put this unguent on the woman's nature within and without.
puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz;	then make her sit in lukewarm water down to below the ribcage;
et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai .i. coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre;	and when she is moistened underneath, then make a mirror-colored clyster and put it underneath, and let her be for an hour;
puis la fai seoir sus .i. siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	then make her sit on a stool, then make her stretch and hold her mouth and nose, and press lightly on her belly, for the child is now jumping.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	of the issue of the child from its knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc;	When the child comes out in this form, then put the midwife's hands slowly and carefully.
puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor .i. lit;	then it should be supported on its neck, and the feet should hang down below, and it should be laid on a bed.
et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval;	and bend its hands slowly and carefully, and then press the hands on the belly, and take out the cushions underneath, until she is prepared below.
et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains;	and if the child does not jump, then take its feet and shape them well, then shape the belly upwards, then put your hands in.
et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	and gently lift the child slowly and carefully; and instruct the woman to take hold of it until the child comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	of the issue of the child which comes out with one hand holding onto something.
I covient engignier a ramener la main:	It is necessary to contrive to bring back the hand.
s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler;	if one cannot bring it back, then make the woman stand up and walk.
s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus .i. lit, et li deboute les jambes forment;	if she cannot walk, then make her lie on a bed, and gently lift up her legs.
puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit;	then administer the fenugreek juice that I have told about.
et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus .i. siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main;	and if she does not give birth, then make her sit on a stool, and study how to bring back the hand.
et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	and gently lift out the child according to its natural shape, and make her stretch, and instruct her to take hold of it until the child comes out fully.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	of the issue of the child from its neck, and having spread its hands, and its face turned towards its mother's back.
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement;	It is necessary that the midwife holds onto its hand, then gently turns it slowly and carefully, and lifts it lightly.
et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc;	and when it is even, then put on the fenugreek juice and oil, as we have said, and instruct her to move slowly and carefully.
et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus .i. siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	and when you have done this, then make her sit on a stool, and instruct her to take hold of it; and make her stretch.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	of the same manner for all the afterbirth.
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie;	When it comes forth in this way to all the afterbirth, then cut the afterbirth at its joint until the moisture is emptied.
et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes;	and if the child falls on its face and neck, then cut it from below so that it is not retained, and let the child die.
puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois:	then put the child inside as you have placed it, and instruct the woman to take hold of it sometimes:
adonques si istra legierement.	Then it will be easy.
de l’issue des gemelz	of the issue of twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent .iij. ou .iiij.; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Know that twins are born many times, and sometimes three or four are born; and this is not an unusual thing, and it happens often.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom;	Two [twins] are a strange thing, and do not live if they are not named.
je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude;	I know that they are multiplied, and are devoured by the yolk which divides them, which is connected to the mouth.
et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	and sometimes come out naturally like one under, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait;	And if they should heal, then follow the cure as we have said, and be subtle in the application, and do quickly and lightly all that it does;
et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	and do so as it is of value for salvation.
de plusors enfans	of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou .iiij. ou .v. ou .vj. ou .vij., ou plusors jusc’a .xv., et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious,	Sometimes they are formed in the womb i.e. one, two, three, four, five, six, seven, or more up to fifteen, and are all shaped in the form of an infant by the measurement of wise and glorious providence,
et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient;	and it is fitting that the healer knows all this, for similar things may happen by chance;
si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	so do according to what is necessary.
de l’enfant mort	of a dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains;	When you are treating the woman with a dead child or in her womb, as I have said in the division, and it does not come forth, and you are compelled to operate by hand;
si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort;	so it is necessary that you know whether the woman has a healthy temperament and does not have an accident or fear of death;
si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees;	so it is necessary that the woman be positioned on her back, and have her hips inclined downwards, and her legs lifted;
et li ministre la teigne de .ij. pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant;	and the attendant holds a cloth of two parts, or she is tied to the bed so that she will not be moved in the delivery of the child;
puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges;	then wipe the mouth of the womb with moist oils mixed with alum, and fenugreek and flaxseed, then anoint your hands with these oils and these poultices;
puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere .i. leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu,	then pour them into the womb lightly, then take one or two of those poultices that are suitable for this purpose,
et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief;	and take care to see if the child is prepared to descend onto its head;
si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez,	if you place the poultices in his ears or on his neck or mouth or palate or under the beard or in the forehead or near the ribs,
et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes;	and if the descent is onto the feet, then place or pinch and make moeving at the sides;
et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide;	and it is necessary that he holds the poultice in his right hand, and places the cord between his two hands of the left hand, and pours it all over his hand lightly, and places the poultice in one of those places which we have said, until it comes to the empty thing;
et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	and that is the form of the poultice:
puis fiche encontre .i. autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz;	then place it against another poultice, or the third one if you need it, so that the extractions are equal;
et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	and then stretch it evenly by moving from one side to the other, in order for the poultices to emerge, and have the poultices toothed so as to hold them, as is the form;
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie;	And if there remains a part, then anoint the healer's fingers with oil, and pour it into that part, and treat the other part;
et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	and if there remains nothing, then place this poultice or one higher up, and do so until it all comes out forthrightly.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement,	And if one hand comes before the other, and he cannot return because of the constriction;
si covient que tu envoloupes sus .i. drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote;	so it is necessary that you envelop it on a cloth until it all emerges;
puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as .ij. piés.	then cut at the joint of the toe or at the cuticle, and thus it is necessary that you do the same in the other hand, and with two feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee,	And if the child's head is large and it is narrow in the exit, or it has an assembled aquiline nose;
si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue;	so it is necessary that you place the spatula-like spine between your fingers, and shape the head and extract the aquiline nose;
ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui;	or you use the instrument called "almidach", by which the form comes with instruments or chapter that follows this one;
et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment;	and thus make it so if the child has a large natural head;
et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles,	and then treat the bones with forceps;
et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer;	and if the head jumps forward and it is strained at the forehead, then be split, so that the moisture which is in the back part comes forth;
et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues;	and if it cannot come out, then cut it into pieces as much as you can;
et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	and if he is swollen in the belly or beneath the ribs, then it is necessary that you make a hole until the moisture flows;
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the child is on its feet, then the traction is light, and the direction towards the mouth of the womb is light.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a .i. drapeil envoloupeit sus la main;	And if he is narrow in the belly or back, then it is necessary that you extract him onto a cloth wrapped around your hand;
et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre;	and shape the belly or back until the moisture that is there flows;
et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure,	and if the other members are removed, and the head remains,
si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris;	so anoint your hand with oil to the very bottom of the womb, and treat it up to the mouth of the womb;
puis i boute .i. oncine ou ij., et le trai fuer;	then place one or two poultices on it, and treat it forthrightly;
et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier,	and if the mouth of the womb is constricted due to a hot abscess that has come forth, then it is not necessary to trouble oneself;
ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses;	instead it is fitting to administer moist and greasy things;
et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	and the administrator applies ointments, and uses them in softening and moistening liquid substances.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif;	And if the child is on its side, and you can place it evenly, then administer to the living child as we have said.
et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	and if one cannot do so, then treat it forthrightly in pieces, and leave nothing of the second stage.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris;	And when you have done this, then administer what we have said for hot abscesses that come forth in the womb;
et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	and if hemorrhaging comes from blood, then it should be stopped with water restraining, and the administrator should administer other remedies.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut .i. autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman whose womb had contained a dead child, then she consulted with another about that one, and rejected the dead one.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, an abscess came forth in her mouth, and swelled so much that it burst open, and began to cause great turmoil.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to the treatment, and I thought for a long time, and could not stop the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I applied a plaster with strong traction, and one bone came out, and after some days another.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was very surprised, because the womb has no bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	So I thought that it was the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em miglior point;	I cleaned the wound and extracted many bones, until the woman was in a better state.
et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu;	and the woman lived long thus, and at times a little bit of bowel came from there.
et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	and I have not remembered this chapter except that when the master finds a strange thing, he knows how to help it.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	of returning the marrow to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a .ij. tornans as .ij. chiés des .ij. liiens.	Then comes the form of pressure, for which one reads books; and at two turns to two joints of two ligaments.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux;	However, the corners should be more subtle than the restrainer, and made of ebony or boxwood;
et soit li bouche dou fust .i. doi de large, et li marge des arbres .i. doit, et de lonc une palme et demi;	and let the mouth of the wood be one and a half fingers wide, and the border of the trees one finger, and as long as half a palm.
et enmi les .ij. liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus;	and between the two ligaments should be two joinings of this same wood, which are tight in one and the other, as long as half a palm or a little more.
et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les .ij. cornes.	and these two joinings are fitted in the mouth of the marrow to open when one turns the two corners.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles;	Another form, more subtle and light in appearance, should be made of ebony or boxwood wood, according to the appearance of forceps;
et ait as .ij. chiés .ij. ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et .ij. dois de large;	and have two joints, two joinings, just as you see, one palm long and one finger wide;
et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor .i. lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes,	and when you see the marrow open with all the instrument, make the woman sit on one chair, her feet pendant and her legs outstretched;
puis boute les .ij. ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes;	then fit the two joinings joined together in the marrow, and hold the head of the instrument below between her thighs;
puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	then work your hand on all the instrument, just as you have done with forceps evenly, according to the size that you see open the mouth of the marrow, until the ball makes what it wants.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	These instruments are all mounted, and their forms are multiplied; and when the makers have prepared them, the work is then more hasty, and higher for men according to their quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	Do not despise the instrument that you have prepared, for its necessity is not excusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis;	When the secondine is retained at childbirth, it is necessary that you instruct the patient to retain her urine, and then make her void with condiments, and hold your hands on her mouth and navel;
et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	and if she sweats because of this, well it is.
Se ceu non, si prent .i. pot, et fai .i. pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire;	If not, take one pot, and make one perforation or cover, and put in herbs that can open the mouth of the marrow, such as chamomile, rue, anise, and centaury.
toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris,	all these herbs, or some of them, should be cooked or put in water above the fire; then place one end of the pot or perforation on the mouth of the marrow,
et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	and keep it so that the vapors come into the marrow; then make her void, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the secondine heats up quickly.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature,	And if she remains after this treatment and is not fully cured, instruct the nurse to moisten her left hand with sesame oil or mugwort oil of hawthorn, and then insert it into the natural opening.
et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction;	and takes hold of the secondine; and when she has found it, grasp it and stretch it out little by little straightly, so that the marrow does not resist the extraction.
mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	but it is necessary to move it slightly to the right and to the left, and then pull; so it will come out and become dislodged.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes;	And if the mouth of the marrow is congested, we have said the cure for voiding and for fumigating herbs;
et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire;	and if she is not helped by all that we have said, then beware that you do not force it.
mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon;	but it is necessary that what is at the mouth of the marrow you tie to the woman's thigh, then anoint her with ointment of fourfold medicine.
si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	so it will be poured and replaced, and come forth; but nonetheless, when she has purged in this way a foul odor comes to the stomach and head, and hurts the patient.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	So it is necessary to make suitable fumigations in this case: none of the ancients have proved that fumigation with cress and dried figs is not good.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The form of the instrument with which one fumigates the woman to retain the flowers and the secondine is this:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu;	And it resembles seeing a cord, and one places the head of the instrument in the natural opening, and the wide ends above the fire;
et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	and let the fumigation be above the coals, and keep it until it is exhausted, and then start another one.
de percier lou fondement	of piercing the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac:	Many children are born who do not have their foundation pierced, but rather it is stopped by a subtle membrane.
si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche;	So it is necessary for the nurse to pierce that subtle membrane at its tip, and not pierce it with a sharp instrument, and guard the location so she does not touch it.
puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	then put on a moist linen cloth with wine and oil, then apply the treatment of ointment until it is healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will not stop, put a cord of flax into the wound and let it stay for many days, and be removed when the child wants to go to chambers.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And whenever this stoppage comes from a sudden wound or abscess; it is necessary to close that stoppage: if it is cured, as we have said with the cord of flax.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula of the foundation
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des .ij. parties,	Fistulas that come from under the foundation are nodulation, and grow larger as they come from below the foundation or in the space between the two parts.
si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe,	and if there is one or more fistulas; and when that nodulation is old, it will work, and in the meantime put more moisture on white or subtle bread.
et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	and sometimes these fistulas are purged; and they are known by that which comes out or is voided through the mouth or windiness when the patient makes an evacuation, and by chance one jumps forward.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if there are fistulas that penetrate just to the bladder, and just to the middle of the penis; and they reach just to the joint of the thigh, and just to no point of the knee.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant:	And thus one knows the fistula is purging at the foundation, and not purging.
et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	and is that you insert your two fingers or foundation, and insert a fine needle of iron or steel into the fistula when there is no twisting.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou .i. poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit;	And if it has tortuosity, then put in a thin tent of cloth or one hair of a horse, until you feel the tent or hair at your own discretion.
et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit:	and if you do not feel it, and there is no passage of pus, windiness, or fever, as we have said:
saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	know that it does not break through; therefore hasten to cure.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula is pierced all the way to the bladder or the urethral canal, if it jumps with urine, and cannot be healed by medicines.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu;	If it is pierced all the way to the crotch joint, then the tent comes up to its place;
s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement;	if there is no tortuosity and the cause of pain around it, then it is that he goes away, and there is no remedy by medication nor by soothing with oil.
et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	and in these pierced fistulas there is no cure except labor, and the vanity of foolish doctors who meddle with them.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit,	In that which is not pierced and is not old, there is hope of healing by fire, as I have experienced.
et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre;	and it is that the patient lies between your hands on his back; and lifts his legs up to his crotch, and has his crotch inclined towards his belly.
puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	then put in a tent of iron or cloth if there is tortuosity, until you know where the tent comes to.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice,	If the patient feels it around the fundament, then it is necessary that you put in two fingers.
se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans;	then sense that the tent has pierced it; and be discovered where you feel between your skin or flesh, then know that it is pierced.
si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	if one does not work on it, one cannot heal it.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc;	One says that one can indeed heal some, but this happens rarely;
et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit;	and the aid that is done there is to cauterize the subtlety of the fire according to the width of the fistula, as was said before;
et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu .ij. fois ou .iij., tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil;	and put it all hot into the fistula, until it comes near the fundament; and do this two or three times, until you know that these burned flesh scraps are like a bird's feather.
et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	and then cure with moist tents in butter, until those flesh scraps are gone; and then cure with ointment anointing the wound and binding.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien. Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez;	If it is thus healed, that's good. If not, there is no other way to heal;
et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur;	and if the tent goes in and does not pierce all the way to the skin which is at the fundament, and between your two fingers and the tent there is a thick covering of flesh or skin, and you see the fistula at that point where the covering of fat ends.
si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente;	so cut from the beginning of the fistula, and put in advance of the tent, and then apply the cauter after, until it comes to the head of the tent.
et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	and the tent will be delivered and fall away; then remove those burned flesh scraps that resemble a bird's feather, and none of it will remain.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the blood increases, and cuts between you and the work, then cauterize with fire or medicine again.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble .ij. bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor;	For the cauteries of fire bring together two good things: namely, the burning away of these adhered flesh scraps, and the stopping of blood and the drying up of moisture.
puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe;	then cure with moist tents in butter or in crushed cheese, until the wound flows away, and the burned flesh scraps are gone from the flow.
puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	then cure the wound with binding ointments anointing hard flesh, and use dry medicines.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, then it is healed and does not come back.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if the fistula comes all the way to the bottom of the fundament, and is distant from the body, then insert your finger into the fundament and feel around.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre .ij. est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des .iii. manieres:	If you feel the tent and between two is the thread or skin or flesh, where it is near to piercing, then there are no remedies except by way of faith and hope, through the administration of one of the three methods:
ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier;	or you cauterize it as we have said, or cut it all the way to the bottom, or if you can, put in tents and cure it as before.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit;	and do not go too far down into the fundament, lest you cut the tent that holds the foundation, and come to an evacuation without intention.
puis le cure, si com nos avons dit;	then cure it as we have said;
par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé;	by chance if it will be healed, or you remove that covering and the mud when it is cut away from the fundament, by tent or by another instrument appointed.
puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues;	then remove the burned flesh scrap that is in the wound, as much as you can.
puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	then study to restore the wound and to keep the fistula in the part beyond the fundament: if it is a lighter thing for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus,	And sometimes are fistulas in this manner: and it is when you put the tent into the fistula, and it is on the edge of the fundament near the skin above.
si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	so take a pierced tent at the head according to this form:
Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And I put one twisted thread into two, and put the tent all along the thread in the fistula until it reaches the head.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement;	If it is pierced on the edge of the fundament inside, then pull out the thread from that opening, thus putting your finger or fundament.
et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les .ij. chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse .i. jor ou .ij.;	and pull the head of the thread, and bring together the two ends, and hold one to the other, and let it be for one day or two.
et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent;	and restrain it sometimes, until the thread cuts through those flesh scraps that are between two, and they fall away.
puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	then cure the wound until it is bound up and healed.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not pierce, then make it pierce in all ways that you can, except if it is too deep.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is not necessary to cut too far down and then cure, as we have said, until it is healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans;	The shape of the spine-like instrument used to make the fistula is quite rough and uneven, one side and the other.
et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	and the other side not, because of which you do not cut what you should not cut, as you see here:
des emorroydes	of hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc ij. manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc,	Hemorrhoids are according to two manners: or they are inside the fundament, like grains of resin, and there are small and great ones, and in short time blood flows.
et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor,	and if there is one or more, and they are farther away from the foundation and at the head of the foundation; but those that are farther away have little moisture,
et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors;	and then again or a little bit of yellow water or a little bit of blood, and they have the color of flesh;
et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz;	and the cure for those who have it inside the foundation is that you instruct the patient to stretch forth and move towards a room, until the foundations come forth, and then the sons appear;
si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines;	so hurry, and hold it with pincers, or you hold it to your finger, then cut into its roots;
et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a .i. drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot;	and if the ligament cannot hold them due to their moisture, then take them by a cloth, or a cotton cloth, or a piece of camlet;
et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere;	and extract them to your hands, then cut, and powder on some hot powders that are in place of cauterization;
ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, puis les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	or you cauterize them as it is said or written in the chapter on cauterization, then cure with other cures until they are healed;
et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement;	and if the foundations cannot come out, then purge the patient with a bitter and sharp laxative to cleanse what is in the foundation, so that it can come out openly;
cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere;	when the patients are pierced, and if the sons are gone from the foundation, then the cure is easy;
et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	and it is that you pierce them with your finger or pincers, and cut, then cure as we have said, until they are healed, and that he fears the incision by iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren .i. fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les .ij. chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille,	and it is necessary that you bring the suture in this manner: take one twisted thread, and put it into a needle, and then draw out the thread above and make the needle pierce from the other side, and turn the two ends of the thread below the needle,
et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse .i. por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc;	and if it is of the length; and hold the thread tightly, then knot the thread, and extract the needle, and do thus with all the others, and leave one for closing the excess blood;
puis met sus le fondement .i. drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose;	then put on the foundation a damp cloth moistened with rose oil or cerate, and put it on the foundation, and instruct the patient to rest;
et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then leave him until he is purged, and when they are purged, then cure with ointment and other cures, until he is healed.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	of the dryness of the fiend or foundation
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Many times it happens that dryness of the intestines occurs, and due to constriction of nature, and when the patient is old and medicine does not help.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir;	So it is necessary that you remove at the tip of a spatula or with your finger the outer layer above which does not allow it to be moistened;
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient;	then cure it until it is soothed as necessary;
et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez;	and if it cannot be soothed, then begin again the scraping more strongly than before, until it is healed and purged.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then cure it until it is healed.
dou fremit	of the shivering
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont;	Fomentation is a small appearance of boil on the body, and goes very deep;
et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	and sometimes it bursts open in cold weather, and one feels it just like death from shivering, and comes all over the body, and more so in the hands than elsewhere.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor;	And the cure is that you take a goose quill or a strong turkey feather, and put that quill on the shivering, until the circles become purple all around.
puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	then turn your hand to the whole quill until you cut all around the shivering, and put it deep in, and extract the shivering from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see, then do this with a file of iron or steel in this form, and be subtle below and drawing above.
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	but not pierce, to keep it at the joint, and press it And if you see, then cauterize the shivering, as written before or in the chapter on cauterization.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of a purgative
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Sometimes one makes a purge of silver or of archroot, or of melted iron or cloth; and sometimes one makes these instruments small and great, according to how they are brought together.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those then which are used in the care of children and those who are weak and painful are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of a purgative small and great is thus broad or the belly is bound in this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez .ij. pertus, et en l’autre .i.;	and it has an indentation or the belly is bound, as you see, and the edges are pierced inside; and has two holes on one side, and one on the other.
et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus,	and it is the belly or where one puts medicines from a beast's bladder or parchment, and is pierced all around with small holes.
et ait entre chescun pertus .i. doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus .i. fil fort de fil crut tort en .x. ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre;	and has between each hole one thread of esparto, then put in those holes one strong thread of twisted linen in ten or eleven turns around, and bind the belly as a goat.
et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and when the medicine is inside, tie it with a strong thread to the instrument beforehand, then purge; and that is the form of the circle.
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement;	And let the medicine not be too hot or too cold, and anoint the top of the purgative with oil or egg white or similar thing, then put it on lightly.
puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses .ij. mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit,	then instruct the attendants to lift it together with their two hands until it is completely visible, then extract the purgative, and raise the patient's legs to the parapet.
et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	and if the medicine wants to come out, then tighten it as much as it can; and if the patient sleeps a whole night through, that is more great help.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you purge in a disease of windiness of the belly, and the medicine hastens to come out, then repeat it until it is healed.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por .i. enfant;	And if hemorrhoids are in the foundation or abscess, then the purgative should be as subtle as for a child.
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	and that is the form of the subtle purgative when the skin is strained on this account.
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have said in the division the treatment of wounds; and now we will tell you the treatments of hands and medicine, according to completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to how they are made, and according to the places or the wounds are made, and of what they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses;	The things by which wounds are made are by cutting with a stone, or by the edge of a sword and knife, or by a spear or fist or seat, or similar things.
ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres;	where are made according to the places of the body, as a wound that falls on the neck, or on the head, or on the back, or on the belly, or on the liver, and similar members;
et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	and I will tell you the cure for each wound, and begin with simple wounds of the head, because the reminder will come in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans,	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head, and the bone is not broken, take care if it's from a blow of stone or similar things, and although the skin is torn and the wound is large,
et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree;	and you lightly doubt of aposteme hot: so do it soon to heal from the head itself if it comes forth with blood from the wound, and let the healing be contrary to the injured part;
et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	and instruct the patient to take in wine and big meats.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char;	And if he does not want to heal, so let his meat be weakened, and let him drink no wine, nor eat no flesh;
et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice;	and put on the wound if hot apostemes come, a moistened cotton cloth in rose oil alone, or in stiptic wine;
et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés;	and if there is no hot aposteme, so put on the wound, if it is fresh with all its blood, and it is not moved by air, powder, which I will say a little later;
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if the fire has moved it, so put on some ointments until he is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large like a sword cut and similar ones, and the lips cannot be brought together by stitches, so bring them together by suturing, as I will say about belly wounds, with suturing.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir,	If the wound is uncovered of bone and open, and does not hold but for a moment, then cut it; next, treat the wound with medicine, and restore hard flesh in place of skin.
et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	and instruct the patient to eat big meats, such as cooked brains and wheat, also like fowl, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure;	And if you find or skin rot, and it is not on the bone, then cut out all the rot and throw away what remains, then treat it.
et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil;	and if he has an artery in the wound or vein, without a cover, and it cannot be stopped by medicine, then bind the artery, and if you find it dislocated, bind it with a thread.
et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	and if this does not help, then cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, the cure is easy: and that you put on this powder which sets in motion as soon as the fire has moved it.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon .ij. parties; chalz vive .iij. parties, et le poudre subtilment,	And the manner of the powder is this: take one part of incense; two parts of dragon's blood; three parts of live coal, and the powder subtly mixed,
et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc;	and apply the wound, and bind it firmly, until it heals well and joins with all its blood.
et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	and then bind it well, and let it be without untying, unless it swells; for one does not remove the medicine until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And one does not do this with coal alone, except when one has no incense nor dragon's blood, but only when the fire has moved the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre;	And if the fire has moved the wound, even though it is set, do not put on this powder at all.
mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe;	but put on some digestive ointments, or thrush made from wheat flour, water, and honey, until it flows forth.
puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat with other treatments until he is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz;	And if the breaking of bone comes with the wound, and it is small, so extract it with subtle pincers.
et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	and I will tell you later about the fractures of the head.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound on the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If a wound comes to the neck and it is simple, there is no difference between it and one on the head, but if the nerves of the neck or an artery are cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire;	If it's the nerves, then there is no other remedy than to let the wound heal, and not put anything restrictive on it, for it harms the nerves and makes them retreat.
et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres;	and don't put anything cold on the wound, for the substance of the nerves is cold, and their continuity is with the brain, which is the highest member.
mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce,	but let the medicine be gentle, like coal washed in sweet water, and mixed with rose oil, and washed again in sweet water.
et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	and other stones of mines according to this manner, and moistened ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, then cut and bind with bandages, then treat until he is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu;	And if the wounds are deep and have become hollow and full of pus, then puncture or lower down.
et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est;	and if the artery is cut and blood comes flowing out, then stop it, tie it off, and cauterize it as needed.
et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va,	and if the spine of the throat is cut, or the gullet, and the conduit is guarded, by which the meat goes,
si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel;	so cut the gullet above the cane of the throat, and do not touch the throat but put it back according to its natural shape.
et puis l’estrain avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then bind him gently, and let him be for some days, then treat with drying ointments until he is healed.
et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier;	and if the wound has made an impression in the bone, then cut it.
et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse,	and if there are pieces of bone, so treat them all as you can, and those that you cannot have, then leave until the wound becomes rotten.
et soit desevree et aligie li issue;	and be dried and closed the opening.
et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	and if the wound is fresh, so powder with powder that I have said.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there are bones in the wound and a fistula, then treat it as I have said in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound from a spear or dagger
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz;	If it's a cut from a spear or dagger, and the wound is deep, then look to see if there are signs of inflammation coming from the wound that the patient will lose their life: know then that the wound is mortal.
et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont,	and if it's not deep, and it's fresh with all its blood, then don't put on the powder at the first hour, nor bind it for the blood that doesn't penetrate deeply.
et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide;	and reverts to the heart, and kills the patient.
mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie .ij. fois le jor;	but I put on an attractive ointment, and bind it twice a day.
et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor,	and if you do not have oil, put old cotton in the wound to absorb moisture.
et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie .iij. jors, ou .iiij., ou plusors;	and make the patient sleep on top of the wound three days, or four, or more.
si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’es traingnemens d’alainne;	if no convulsion comes, nor evil trembling of the heart, nor any perturbation.
et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	and when you see good conditions, then know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then cure it with tents and other treatments until he is healed.
et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	and if it cannot heal or do well, then know that there is a fistula; and treat it as one should.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant;	And if the wound is from a cut of sword or knife and it is simple, or deeper or on the back, then treat the part that is in front.
s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez;	if it is large, with sewing; and if it is small, with powder, and if it is pressed into the bone and has broken pieces, then cleanse the wound and remove any detached flesh.
et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions;	and if they are not detached, then let the wound suppurate, so that it will facilitate extractions.
et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	and for other wounds in other limbs, make judgments as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	of the rupture of the belly
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis;	The ruptures of the belly are great and medium and small;
de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus;	of the great wound sometimes an intestine or a part of the intestines is cut, by which there is no further passage for them;
et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans,	and the sewing is more difficult, and sometimes the small wound is worse than the great one,
por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut;	because therefore one puts the intestines back in slowly, if not put them back together piece by piece;
por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes,	because the intestines swell at once when they feel cold, so they enter more slowly,
et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres .ij.	and for this reason the middle wound is worse, because one must reinsert the intestine to its place as with the other two.
Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc .iiij. manieres:	And know that the rupture of the belly is according to three manners:
les .ij. costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre,	the two common sewings occur in the sewing of the belly,
et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et .ij. autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies;	and the sewing of other wounds of the body and two other proper sewings are common to other wounds;
et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	and yet they are more proper with the sewing of the belly, and I will say each one and declare.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer,	I say that when the wound is small and nothing has come out of the intestine,
et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des .ij. manieres:	and a little thing is required to put back, this is done by one of the two manners:
ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit,	or because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said,
ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	or because the intestine is swollen from cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere:	And when it is cold, warm it up in this way:
moillie une esponge ou .i. mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement,	soak a sponge or one piece of cloth in lukewarm water only,
ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique,	or you boil it in water with squinat and cypress and spike,
