et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	and apply the intestine until the swelling is removed.
et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	and sometimes make this wine restraining and is good to have alone to reduce swelling.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites,	And when you see the swelling departing, then moisten the intestine with water or boil it with marjoram and melissa.
car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose;	for through this it is facilitated the entry of a little thing;
et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes;	and if it cannot enter, then make a small incision in the wound with the instrument used to lance hemorrhoids;
et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille,	and the first treatment is better than the cut.
que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait;	that no one should cut without great necessity there be;
et c’est li estrumens por le fendre:	and that is the instrument for cutting:
si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	so cut inside in the curvature and do not cut too much, and see to it that the form remains.
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer,	And when the wound is enlarged and the intestine comes out,
si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre,	so put it back according to its natural shape in its proper place.
se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	if you have the power, because this is a great thing.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre,	When the wound is large and it is in the part below the belly,
si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos,	so it is necessary that you make the patient lie on his back.
et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief;	and place his legs higher than his head;
et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre,	and if it is in the part below the belly,
si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz,	so elevate the head and chest higher than the parts below.
et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des .ij. parties	and also if the rupture of the belly is in one of the two parts
si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre;	so make an effort to have the injured part higher than the other.
et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	and thus it is necessary to administer what I say about great and middle wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet,	For small wounds, use what appears best to you,
puis aies entre tes mains .i. ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main,	and then have in your hands one pitiful minister who holds all the rupture in his hand,
et assemble les levres;	and bring together the lips;
et c’est la maniere commune de costures,	and that is the common manner of sewings,
et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie,	and it is that you take a needle or several, according to the quantity of the width of the wound.
puis laisse des le chief de la plaie .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait .i. boin fil fort;	then leave from the head of the wound a good space, and insert a needle where there is a strong thread;
et perce les .ij. chiés dou cuir avec les .ij. chiés dou siphac,	and pierce the two joints of the skin with the two joints of the siphac.
qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie,	which is below the skin inside, as long as you make it pierce from that part,
et assemble les .ij. chief dou siphac les .iiij. ensamble;	and bring together the two heads of the siphac and tie them together.
puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de .ij. pars,	then strain it with a double thread around the needle from both sides,
puis assemble les .ij. chiés de la plaie avenanment,	and bring together the two edges of the wound in an even manner.
et puis laisse .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille;	and then leave a good space, and insert another needle;
puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille,	then tie the thread just as you did with the first needle.
et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles,	and do not stop doing this as long as you need to use needles.
tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte;	until all the wound is restrained.
et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses,	and are the needles middle-sized, between fine and thick.
car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer:	because fine needles cut through all the flesh, and those that are too thick cannot enter well:
por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes;	therefore it is necessary that they be middle-sized.
et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir,	and it is not necessary to push the needles too far into the flesh and skin,
k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;	so that they do not cut and open the wound before the suturing.
et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir,	and then cut off the heads of the needles, so that they do not harm the patient while sleeping.
et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir,	and I put tents or cloths on the heads of the needles to hold them in place.
et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee;	and leave them there until the wound is sutured.
et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies,	and this manner of stitching with needles is more suitable for small wounds,
car il i soffist une aguille ou .ij.	for it requires only one needle or two.
Li seconde costure si est commune,	The second stitching is common,
et est que tu assemble les .ij. chiés dou cuir et les .ij. chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait .i. fort fil moien;	and it's that you assemble the two pieces of leather and the two pieces of silk together with a needle where there is one strong middle thread;
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz .iiij. ensamble,	and when you have pierced all these pieces threefold,
si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;	then push the needle through to the part where you started, in the manner one sews clothes.
et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi;	and put a space between each stitching the thickness of a minor denier;
ceste costure sevent li home,	this stitching is suitable for men,
et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre,	and I sewed a wound that a man had in his belly,
qui estoit navrez d’un coutel,	who was wounded with a knife,
et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant,	and the wound was more than a palm's breadth wide,
et issoit des intestines bien .ij. palmes de grant,	and it had exposed the intestines two palms' breadth long,
et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	and the wound was in the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit .xxiiij. houres fuer,	I pulled back the intestine and then it had been out for twenty-four hours,
et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a .xv. jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	and the wound was healed just after fifteen days, and I cured him, and he was sound.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	And the doctors had judged that he would die, and it was a miracle;
et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en .i. leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;	and I did not cure him with ointment, for I was in one place where we could not find any, nor any medicine;
et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel .ij. fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	and I placed clean cotton on the wound twice a day, and washed it with honey water until he was healed.
Or vos dirai les .ij. propres manieres de cousture:	Now I will tell you the two proper ways of stitching:
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	take the needle and plunge it through from outside to inside.
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille,	when it has pierced the thickness in its right place, then put the tip of the silk or thread where you have inserted the needle.
et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;	and make it pierce from the other side of the inside to outside.
et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz,	and the intention of this stitching is that you sew as the furriers do the furs,
et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	and leave the silk on one side and take it up again on the other, until the stitching is completely done.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement,	The second manner of stitching, which Galen calls properly,
si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les .ij. parties ensamble naturelment,	is like that of some who assemble the two parts together naturally,
et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	and apply one end of the silk to the other end, in this manner:
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement,	insert a needle or close-fitting point nearby, and make it pierce only that place.
et laisse les .ij. chiés dou syfac;	and leave the two ends of the silk;
puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens,	then turn the needle and make it pierce from outside to inside.
as .ij. chiés dou syfac;	to the two ends of the silk;
puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en .ij. autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;	then make it pierce one and the other from outside to inside, in two other notches of the mirror that are on the other side.
et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	and this is the more common manner of stitching.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent,	Galens says this word, and some bear witness to it,
c’on doit coudre le ventre a .ij. aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;	one must sew the belly with two needles, where there is thread in each.
et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies;	and one must insert one needle from one side and the other from the other, in the manner of those who sew corsets.
et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre,	and knows that when the rupture is in the belly,
si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	it is the stitching more difficult than for other places of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	The judgment of the wound is such as the judgments of other wounds:
et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee,	and it's that when you find the fresh wound with all its blood, before the fire has changed it,
si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char,	then replace the intestine and the gut; then put on the powder enchanting charm,
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe;	and if the fire has changed it, then apply some ointment that is available, until the wound closes.
et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach;	and tie up the thread, and sew together the silk and mirror;
puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then cure the wound as with others, until it is healed.
et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel,	and if you don't have medicine, then put on, as soon as it begins to close, clean cotton,
et le remue .ij. fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	and move it twice a day until he is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;	For you don't need any other medicine in many cases where the wounds are simple;
et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz,	and if you doubt that the wound may cause community with principal members,
si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset,	so it is necessary that you anoint lightly with oil of temperate heat or oil of rose.
et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles;	and put it around the arms and below the shoulders;
et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient,	and if he feels pain or burning in his bowels, and this often happens,
si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine;	then cleanse with black wine vinegar, and likewise if the burning comes just to the intestine;
et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	and pierce inside, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez,	The intestine called "jun" cannot heal when it is wounded,
et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	and this is because of the putrefaction of the veins that are there, and due to the subtlety of all the body, and the approximation of its nature to that of the fish.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres;	And if the membrane jumps out of the wound, then put it back in the same way as the intestine, while it is fresh.
et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne,	and if it is old and has become yellow or black, then it is necessary that you cover the part that is black, so that no blood may come from there.
car il i a voinnes et arteres;	for there are veins and arteries;
puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien,	then bind what is between the ligament,
et met les .ij. chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	and put the two ends hanging from the part below the wound up to outside to facilitate extraction when the membrane falls off and the wound closes.
de la routure dou boueil	of the rupture of the belly
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite,	When the intestine is torn and the wound is small,
si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes,	it can be restored in some men,
por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance;	because I have seen a man wounded in the belly by a lance;
et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac,	and the wound was on the right side of the stomach,
et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez;	and it became inflamed and turned into a fistula, and there was evacuation and flatulence;
je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	I applied the cure as best I could, and did not cease to subtletize until he was healed, and the parts were joined together.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre;	And when I saw it heal, I doubted that the patient had not evil in his belly;
et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans;	and there was no harm, but he remained in better conditions, eating and drinking.
et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere:	and certain experimenters say that when there is a small wound in the intestine, it must be bound in such a way:
pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie,	take fresh from great tests, then bring together the lips of the wound,
et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les .ij. levres,	and when the fresh has opened the mouth, so put it on the two lips,
si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus;	so that it stretches its mouth thus;
et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier,	and then tie the head, and this stays so that he cannot untie,
puis met .i. autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise;	then put another fresh behind in the same way as before, until the wound is completely covered;
et cout la plaie.	and close the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide,	This treatment if done in the intestine, and does no harm to the patient,
et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste,	and one can tie the intestine with a thin thread which is taken from the intestine of a beast,
en teil maniere:	in such a way:
pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez,	take the end of this thread of intestine that is well separated,
et puis lie au chief de cest fil .i. fil de lin subtil tort,	and then tie to the end of this thread one thread of fine linen twisted,
puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure;	then pass the thread through the needle, and close the intestine, and tie it in the way;
et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance;	and this manner of stitching with fresh is not other than according to the way of faith and hope;
et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	and if the wound is great and wide, especially when it is in one of the intestines, then there is no remedy or health, except subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of fistula or whatever it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule»,	Know that any wound or abscess, when it becomes inflamed, is universally called "fistula",
et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	and even when it is opened and discharges pus.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor,	And fistula is according to the true nodation lacking a hard and white swelling, or where one does not feel pain,
et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	and it discharges pus like the feathers of a bird;
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	and sometimes in clear and abundant pus, and other times thick;
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	sometimes little, and other times sufficient;
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char,	and I have spoken of this in the division of wounds, that any wound which is not healed and has no flesh,
ce n’est fuers que par une des .viiij. causes:	is not other than through one of the eight causes:
c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	namely, through the smallness of blood or flesh;
ou por sa malice;	or through its wickedness;
ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;	or because there is hard flesh inside and on the lips that does not allow new flesh to grow;
ou il i a trop de bowe;	or there is too much pus;
ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;	or the humors are corrupted, and the matter is of bad quality;
ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;	or the medicine is not good in the treatment;
ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	or because the corruption is a manner of plague;
ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;	or because the property in the region is late with digestion and health, and flows naturally;
ou il i a voinnes ou os:	or there are veins or bones:
et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	and I have already shown all these causes, and their signs, and the remedies of medicine in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	or it is necessary that I should make you aware of the treatment for fistula which is done by manual work.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	Know that fistula occurs in all members of the body;
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners,	for there are fistulas that come from great veins, and arteries, and nerves,
ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes,	or the bladder, or intestine, or bladder, or some of the ribs,
ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	or to the spine of the back, or to any joint of the hands or feet;
et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	and if it comes to the property of the principal member, and to similar humors.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance;	And all the fistulas that are in this manner are of grievous sanitation, and there is nothing but labor, and ignorance;
et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure,	and if there is any fistula that does not come to the point I have said, and you have faith in the treatment,
et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	and if you see it, know it, take a tent of iron or earth, if the fistula is straight, then cut it;
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc,	and if the fistula is twisted, then search for a subtle tent of cloth,
car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	for cloth bends around the twistiness;
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes,	and if the fistula has many pores and you cannot well search it with tents,
si la clisterize par l’un des pertus,	then cleanse it by one of the pores,
car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	for the moisture is so short from one pore to another, and cleanses;
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont,	then cut the bleeding at your ability, as you know whether there is bone or nerve, and it discharges abundantly;
et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	and ask the patient well about the pain he feels when you press your hand on him, and where he feels it;
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine,	and when you know truly the place where it is, and if it is far from a jointure, or nerve, or artery, or vein;
ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit,	or in any of the places I have told you, then tie it according to what I have told you,
et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	and cut away the faulty and corrupted flesh that is inside;
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee,	and then treat it until it is healed,
et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues,	and if the fistula is well opened from the right place, then it is necessary that you cut away abundantly as much as you can,
puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule,	then put wet tents in medicinal aloe and tie them just at the head of the fistula,
tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	until the medicine corrodes the superfluity that remains at the bottom;
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then put anointings on healthy flesh, until it is healed.
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit,	and if it is not healed by this, then cauterize it as we have said,
et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	and if the bone is corrupted from the fistula, then cut it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	If veins or nerves do not trouble you or principal members, as we have said;
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee,	and if the bone is uncovered and there is corruption and blackness, then remove the corruption as much as it is necessary.
puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat with anointings on healthy flesh until it is healed;
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant,	and if it is not healed and discharges pus as before,
saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	know that you are not yet at the end:
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons,	then uncover and cut away until you reach the bottom,
et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	and remove all the corruption, then restore the place;
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	and if it is thus healed, that's well.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	if not, know that the corruption is too deep in front, that you cannot come to it;
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	so there is no other remedy but to wait for nature.
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles,	and if there is a small bone corrupted and you can pull it out with forceps,
si l’estrai a .i. estrument covenauble a ceu,	then pull it out with a suitable instrument for this;
et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	and if there are many of them, so treat all together, nor leave one.
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour,	and if moisture makes you contrary, and there is no mistake or fear,
si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	so cut and moisten and flesh, and deliver the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture,	And if you cannot remove them in an hour, then place on the wound something causing putridity.
et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os,	and let it stay until the flesh is rotten around the bones,
et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	and then if they will be more easily removed.
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse,	and if it is a great bone, such as one of the thigh or leg,
si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee,	so remove only the corruption until all the decay is removed.
puis restoure la plaie;	then restore the wound;
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	and if there is great part of the decay and comes just to the bone;
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	so clean and cut all the way to the decay, and then treat it until it is healed.
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint .i. home en sa jambe,	and I will tell you of a fistula that occurred in a man's leg,
si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	so that you may take it as an example and aid in your work.
Il fut .i. jovencelz entor .xxx. ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors,	He was a young man around 30 years old, who had a pain in his leg due to something that came from within the body,
tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	until the matter came to the leg, and was swollen with a great abscess, and there was no reason to stop from opening.
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri,	but the physician by their foolishness opened too high and the abscess burst open,
et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	and there flowed out a great deal of matter, and it became a fistula, and there came a great many pus-filled sores that all went down into the moist parts of the body.
et maint mire i mirent cure entor .ij. ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains,	and many physicians treated it for two years, and there was no gain in the art of healing,
tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit,	so long that I was called to it, and saw his leg and the remedies with which he was being treated.
et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	and what flowed out through the sores was great in quantity.
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	and the skin of the young man became red and had a yellowish color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus,	I placed a tent in one of those sores, and then searched all the sores.
et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	and I found that some were coming together from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os,	I hastened then, and cut into one of the sores until I uncovered a part of the bone,
et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	and it was decayed and perforated, and the decay came right down to the bone inside.
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	I cleaned out what appeared from the decayed bone, and thought that there was no other decay, except for what I had removed.
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	and began to restore the wound with soothing medicines over a long time, and could not heal.
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant,	and then I recommenced, and uncovered the bone just as before,
et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	and found the decay continued in the bone, and I cleaned it, and then removed it, and took care to heal the place.
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole,	but I couldn't until I cut around a palm's width of bone, and then cleaned it all the way to its entire base.
puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment,	then I restored it with medicines; and it was healed and sound quickly.
et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir,	and there was no longer need to restart the treatment except for the patient's weakness, who could not endure.
et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	and because of the fear of death that I had for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement,	For through the evacuation it often bled profusely, but he was healed entirely.
et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	and instead of the bone, a hard flesh grew, and he was of good disposition and had no harm or contrariness from anything at all, neither going nor coming.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	And if the bone is broken anywhere in the body, then it must be cleaned in this manner:
pren .i. liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert,	take one thread and strain it at the top of the exposed bone,
et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	and command someone to stretch it upwards.
et met .i. autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os,	and take another thread of linen slightly thicker than the first one, and tie it on top of the flesh that is above the bone.
et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz,	and stretch the top, so that you pull out the corrupt flesh below.
et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	and uncover the flesh above the place where you see it is to be cleaned, so that the cleaning does not cut into the flesh.
et met .i. tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	and put a hot iron or a heated table under the bone to move and cover the corrupt flesh.
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	and it is necessary to clean as much as can be seen and felt of the corruption, and then clean again another time.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie,	And if the bone is decayed, and does not open up, and the corruption is in the middle or in one part.
si descuevre la char toute; puis met .i. tison desoz,	so uncover all the flesh; then put a hot iron underneath.
et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption .i. poc, si com nos avons dit;	and then clean from one part to the other the corruption, and be sure of the length of the corruption by a foot, as we have said;
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	and if the corruption is in the joint, then cut out the decayed joint and clean the bone where it contains from the other side.
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des .ij. jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	and if the corruption is in the continuation of two joints, then there is no other remedy than to cut.
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose,	and if the corruption is in the finger or in the toe, it is very strong indeed.
mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	but still it is necessary that you inquire about this corrosion, how it opens up;
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	and purify it in all the ways you can, but let the vein or nerve not hinder you.
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous,	and know that the knife and the threads for cutting these bones are many, according to the shape of the bones and their appearance outside.
et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	and their thickness and subtlety, and their largeness and smallness, and their hardness.
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	and for this reason it is necessary to prepare each instrument according to the appearance of the work.
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art,	and know that the work will show you the instrument that you will need, according to the knowledge of this art.
et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	and the testimony of the methods of diseases;
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	so think about the instrument that you need according to what is necessary.
dou feu	of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The head of the shoulder may become dislocated due to a reason within, or due to a reason without.
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie,	and when you have tried medicine on this corruption through the treatment of medicines, and it does not help.
si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient,	so it is necessary to cut that member all the way down to the place where the corruption comes.
si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	so that the patient may escape either by death or by the evil which is greater, namely, the deficiency of the member.
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu,	and the signs are that the member becomes black, as if it were burned by fire.
et porrist aprés la noiror, puis va celle corrosions de membre em membre,	and afterwards the blackness appears, then goes on to corrode member by member,
et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper,	and takes hold of the entire body; if you hasten to cover.
et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans,	and if it is due to the percussion of some venomous beasts, such as sea scorpions and vipers and similar ones.
se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	if the corrosion is at the head of the joint, then it will spread and not give space for coming as far as the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it comes as far as the hand, then it will spread to the joint, so that the corruption does not come as far as the arm.
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors,	and if it comes to the arm, then it will spread to the shoulder; and if it passes the shoulder, it is death.
et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	and there is no remedy except for the quantity of his virtue;
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	and so it goes when the corruption comes to the foot: if it comes to the first joint, then it will spread to the other joint.
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	and if it comes to the foot, then it will spread all over the foot;
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	and if it goes up to the leg, then it will spread to the knee joint.
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	and if it comes above the knee, then there is no other remedy except for the physician to let the patient die.
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz,	and the manner of binding or covering the member is that you bind it above and below.
et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont,	and stretch one minister down from one band, and another minister up from the other band.
et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les .ij. liiens a .i. spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	and you uncover the flesh that is between the two bands with one wide spatula, until the bone is exposed.
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part .i. drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain,	then bind or cover it, and put one cloth of linen on each side, so that the binding does not touch the healthy skin.
et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	and another lesion and abscess occur in the patient.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment,	And if blood flows from the wound when you work, then cauterize the area at once.
ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie,	or you put some restraining powders on top; then return to your treatment until it is completed.
puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then bind the injured member with a suitable bandage, and treat it until it is healed.
et je te conterai k’il avint a .i. home en som piet:	and I will tell you what happened to one man on his bare foot:
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu,	he had a blackness that seemed like burning coal,
et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	and the corruption came first to his toe of the foot, until it spread all over the foot.
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	and when the man saw the corruption, he hastened to cover the foot and was healed.
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi,	and long afterwards the corruption came back to his hand, and he came to me.
et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	and I put some counteractive things on him after purifying the body, but could not stop the corruption.
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	and he wanted me to amputate his hand, and I did not consent, because I had hope of counteracting the material;
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist,	and I also doubted that if I cut off his hand, he would die.
car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre,	for the man's virtue was weak; and he became desperate in all respects, and returned to his land.
et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	and he hastened to cover his hand, and was healed.
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	and I have told this tale only for this reason: that if one is in need of it.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	Sometimes an abscess comes on the fatty part of the skin, and remains so long that it makes a great gathering of pus.
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	and then bursts and perforates, and the pus jumps out, and the skin remains empty, just like a vessel.
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com .i. drapelz deliiez,	and the skin on top is also as delicate as a piece of fine silk.
et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain»,	and does not spread as far as the bone, nor as far as the nerve, and such a disease is called "sain".
et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	and it is not called "fistula".
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	but if it is so long that it comes right to the bone in the middle, then it is called "fistula".
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	and the skin is such that you cover all around with skin, and similarly when it is delicate like a piece of silk.
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	and does not harden because of its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont,	And if you have faith that the skin will harden, and the corruption is not in the middle,
et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	and the skin is thick with flesh, then treat it with a poultice thus:
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor,	see if the breast is large, and the pus that issues from it has a foul smell,
adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	then treat it with Egyptian medicine made thus:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en .i. vassel au feu,	take equal parts of asafoetida, oil, and lye, and put them to boil in one vessel over the fire,
tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	until the medicine is red, and becomes equally thick as honey;
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel,	and then take from it according to your need, and mix it with water and honey.
et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	and use it to foment the breast, and stop the abscess.
et laisse la medicine ens par .ij. houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	and leave the medicine on for two hours, then remove it by pressing gently.
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	do this many times until the breast is made clean and the pus is removed.
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres,	and sometimes it is fomented with ash water,
quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus,	when this medicine is not present, and take ashes from grape vine, and pour water on top.
puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	then let it flow, and foment with it, as long as you know the breast is well cleansed.
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres,	and if the patient cannot tolerate it, nor the Egyptian medicine nor the ash water,
si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	then foment with water and honey, or add a little lye to it.
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver,	or foment with honey and mead, since the honey has the property of cleansing and washing.
et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	and the wine makes the skin tender.
et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez,	and when you have done this, and you have faith that the breast is well cleansed,
si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li,	then foment with what makes flesh grow in it.
et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin;	and take defined emplastern, and mix it with rose oil and wine.
ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;	or foment with various medicines and ointments, whose properties I have said or how to treat with ointments;
et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer,	and if the abscess of the breast is small and the poultice of the fomentation cannot enter it.
si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein,	then enlarge it slightly with a needle, and put in a tent made from Egyptian ointment.
ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez;	or balsam ointment, until it is enlarged.
et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement .i. leu ou li clistere puisse entrer,	and if the wound is too wide, then sew it up and leave just enough room for one end or the poultice to enter.
et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	and if the abscess that pours pus is above, then cut it lower than it is.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	Since
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	And if you cannot cover the chest below as you see
si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est,	so arrange it in such a way that the bowstring runs at its lowest position.
car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char	For when the bow is full, do not let it run bare
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	And if you cannot cover the chest below as you see
si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe;	so arrange it in such a way that the bow runs slightly downward, and do not leave anything of the bow.
et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sein,	and take consolidative medicines to put on the chest
et estent sus .i. drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sein;	and place a linen cloth over one and a half feet of the chest;
puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein .i. poc plus large dou premier,	then cover the weakened area on the chest, about a pace larger than the first one,
pues estent oignement souef sus .i. autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus,	and place soft ointment on another cloth according to the size of the weakened area,
et le met sus le pertus dou sein por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois;	and put it on the weakened area of the chest to ease the bow, and do not remove the large cloth until after about a day or once.
et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe,	and he who is on the weakened area of the chest, often removes it to remove the bow,
et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste;	and knows what comes from the bow, whether it is venom or pus or enough or undigested.
et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non,	and take heed if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not,
et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sein,	and when your medicine has been extended in this way and you see the nature that bursts forth on the weakened area of the chest,
si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez;	so know that the chests are already set right, and approach the healthy state;
et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie,	and then loosen it in the morning or third day, and when you loosen the wound,
si chainge .i. autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	so change another cloth, and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the chest ejects undigested bowels after many days, know that the chest is not healed.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit,	And if subtle poisons come out after long time, do not despair of health at all.
car li santez aproche. Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;	for the healthy state approaches. For there are men who slowly putrefy in their wounds, and those who do the opposite;
et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie;	and if undigested bowels burst forth from the chest after many days, know that the chest is not healed.
et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut,	and if the chest takes a long time to heal, and is distant, then add medicines that are moist in substance and dry in virtue,
si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine;	as defined ointment, for it has a great part of vitriol, and this is the last medicine;
pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance;	take defined ointment, and mix it with rose oil, and add equal parts of old wine in substance.
puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez,	then cook it and use it; and the same thing makes cooked honey grow.
quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens,	when defined ointment is not present,
ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu;	or you take myrrh and aloes and incense, and grind them together, and powder it on the honey when it is on the fire;
et puis en glue .i. drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe,	and then wrap it in a cloth, and place it on the chest, and do not administer it again for a long time.
et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire;	and roots of celestial lily, which is also like fine wheat flour and centuary;
et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use;	and use simple or compound medicines: grind them, make powder, and put it on the honey I said, and use.
et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure,	and if the wound is prolonged, and not healed by this treatment,
adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens;	then know that the corruption is at its full extent, and makes an impression on the bone, or causes stiff limbs, or ligaments.
si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	so treat the wound of a fistula, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess of the joint
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main,	Panniculus is an abscess that arises under the joint of the thumb.
ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	or of the foot, or perhaps occurs in other joints;
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient .i. aposteme chaus,	and when it is neglected and not taken care of, then a foul abscess comes forth,
et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	and runs and bursts forth with bowels until it reaches the root of the joint, and perhaps even beyond.
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	and comes to the corrosion just to the bone, until a foul pain comes forth, and is the joint of the toe wide open, and is the color flux.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie,	When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help at all,
si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle,	so it is necessary that you remove all the superfluous matter that remains in the joint,
puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	The cautery is a great help if the bone is sound and the joint is healthy;
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece,	and if the joint begins to rot the flesh, and pierces, and bleeds,
si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char,	so it is necessary that you put a spit under the joint that is piercing the flesh,
et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement,	and seal it above, and remove that subtle and delicate flesh.
et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	and put on the remaining flesh burning and corrosive medicines to remove all;
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat it with ointments until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	And if the corruption is in the bone, then remove it, and treat it further, for as long as the corrupted bone remains, it cannot heal.
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en .i. des nous si com il est devant dit,	and if you see the toe corrupting, then remove it in one of those ways as is said before,
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat it until it is healed.
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	and if it is fierce, and swells, and it feels great pain, then it is necessary that you heal it first.
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus,	then cut the joint of the spatula in a diagonal direction above.
et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	and take care that the cut does not come to the flesh which is beneath the joint, for the patient would feel too great pain.
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	and if it happens, then put something on top that soothes.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain of the deafness in the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus,	The toes that are born in some people's hands by chance are all flesh.
et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle,	and perhaps there is a place where it has bones, and sometimes there is no joint.
et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	and some of them are born at the root of the joint, or their birth is in certain joints of the toes.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet,	Those who are born in any other part of the toe do not move.
et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	and those who are born at the joint of the toe, by chance, do move.
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	the shape of that which is fleshly is light, in such a way:
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	cut it at its root with a broad spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	That which is born at the root of the joint is grievous to cure: if it takes hold, don't bother trying to cut it.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os,	In that which is born or attached to the back part of the toe, it is necessary that you cut the flesh all around just up to the bone.
puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then bind the bone with a suitable thread to it, then care for it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The kind of wound that comes together by birth, or by the healing of a wound, or by burning with fire, or by similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	If it is necessary that you bind that wound, so that it be repaired according to its natural forms;
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	then put between two tents or moist cloths soaked in rose oil, so that they do not stick together.
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	or you put between two thin pieces of linen, until the flesh is sewn, as it is necessary.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If a wound comes to any of its joints with the palm, then bind that wound as it is necessary.
Des vils	Of wounds
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	Wounds are great and swollen, full of mournful superfluities, that come to many members of the body;
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	and they occur more often in the legs of those who walk and work and carry things, than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	It is necessary then that you minister to him sometimes purging of gall, and then salve from the basilica.
Li cure de fer si est selonc .ij. manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	The cure of iron is according to two manners: one is when you bind and drag away the black blood;
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	and the other manner is that you open the vein and drain it completely.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez,	The cutting is according to this manner: first rise the leg with hot water very strongly, until the thick blood is thinned.
puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	then strain the patient's leg above the knee up to the part below the groin;
puis cope la voinne en .i. leu, ou en .ij. ou en .iij., d’une taille large,	then cut the vein in one place, or two places, or three places, with a broad incision,
puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	then lift and drain away the black blood at your hand, from one end to the other, until as much blood flows out as the patient's virtue can endure.
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	and then bind it, and command that he keep eating flesh purging black gall;
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	and recommence the evacuation and salve when the veins are full, and harm comes to the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil,	The healing of it is according to this manner: rise the patient's leg, if there are many hairs.
puis le met ou bain, et li. arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	then put it in a bath, and rise the leg with hot water until it becomes red, and the veins are swollen;
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	and if you don't have a bath, heat it by the fire, and then bind it in place at the vein of the long part above the knee, or in the part below at the ankle;
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	then apply oil to the skin, and scrape the vein from each side, until it appears when one feels it;
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	and one sees it red and black, and when it enters the skin it seems just like a white cord.
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier,	then push the point down below, until it is raised from the skin, and then pat it with oil lightly.
puis le cope en .i. autre leu ensus iij. dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere,	then bind it in one place above two joints, and then scrape the skin over the vein until it appears.
puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	then lift it up by the point, just as you did, and pat it with another oil, just as you did first.
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet,	then cut another incision, or more if you need them, then lift it and bind at the joint of the foot.
puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	then drain and lift up to the second incision; then draw out from incision to incision until it flows completely, then bind.
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil fort double,	and if you can't drain and lift it, then insert an awl into each strong thread doubled.
et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz .i. rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	and bind and drain it, and push down below one point, and turn your hand from side to side until it flows out;
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	and be careful that it doesn't bind, for if it binds, then one cannot drain or lift it, and harm comes to the patient.
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and when you have drained it all, then put a moist cloth made of wool, wine, and rose oil on the wound, and care for it until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit,	And if the flesh is constricted and twisted and swollen together, and it is not straight, as we have said,
si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	then it is necessary that you cut it twistedly, but do not bind it; and drain it as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The shape of the iron with which you cut the flesh is curved, and does not cut through, so that it cuts the vein.
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	and is of great curvature, for if it were thin, it would cut the vein, but let it be thick as we have said, and this is the shape:
De la voinne civile	Of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein is located in legs, in hot parts where there are no herbs or trees, and in earth where there is no moisture;
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir,	and by chance it may be found elsewhere besides legs, and this happens due to the putrefaction that comes from below the skin;
si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	as if a serpent or worm were to come forth inside the body, and to be located between the skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation,	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are that a great inflammation comes to the leg,
puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	then the swelling changes and the vein begins to emerge, just like the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a .ij. З., et la noe,	When the swelling opens, it is necessary that you wrap around a piece of linen from one and a half to two and a half inches, and tie it off.
et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	and leave the linen on the leg, and whenever it becomes undone at the back, wrap it around the linen and tie it off.
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	and if it is too long, cut off a part and wrap the remaining part around it, and do not bind it at its root until it has fully emerged.
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	for if you cut it, it will retreat back into the flesh and cause an abscess and putrefaction in that place, and a bad disease.
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	therefore it is necessary to treat it slowly and gradually up to the end, and leave none of it in the body.
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de .v. paumes de lonc, ou de .x.,	and sometimes this vein is as long as five or ten palms.
et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de .x. paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute .i. rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons,	and one man came to me, whose it was as long as ten palms, and when you cut it, he pushed one point or perforation, and it pierced down to the bottom.
si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	so that everything flows out; and be empty the matter which is inside, and administer to the place medicines purging putrefaction some day, then care for it as one would for abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet,	And sometimes this vein has many branches, and indeed when it opens at the joint of the foot or in the foot.
et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	and then it comes forth with pus, and from which it springs forth; treat it thus as we have said before.
Des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	Of the veins that are born between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués,	This disease is called in our land "beef illness", because it often befalls oxen,
et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant,	and it is a small worm that is born between skin and flesh, and ascends and descends all over the body.
et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	and it can be felt as it moves from member to member, until it reaches the skin where it is going and bursts forth;
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	and is caused by an imbalance of certain humors, such as those that come from worms and serpents and lice and ascarids or the belly;
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil,	and one doubts of its wickedness, for when it goes through the body and ascends to the head, and comes to the eye;
par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	by chance it returns, and destroys the eye; and this often happens.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see it being cured and pulled out, one cannot flee except when it is going:
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement,	so then it is necessary that you bind the place above and below with a strong cord tightly.
puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves,	then pull up and pull it out, and if the worm is deeply embedded in the flesh, and you do not find it,
si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	then cauterize it with fire above, until it dies;
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	and the greatest harm that it does is that it corrupts the eye, as we have said;
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	and if you see it coming or near the eye on the forehead, then bind tightly below it, and then pull up and pull it out;
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries,	and it is necessary to use the patient in a cleansing of the body with soluble medicines to purge the bad humors.
et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	and be wary of meats that cause an imbalance of humors.
De la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	Of the pain that comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres,	This disease is called in our land "vacirir", and is a pain that comes in some members,
et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	and then moves from member to member; and I saw what I am telling you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to a sick woman, and she showed me her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm;
et .i. poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule,	and shortly after, I saw it rising also like a worm on the shoulder,
plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	faster than anything else, just like quicksilver when it flows from one place to another;
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule,	the pain departed from that place and settled in the shoulder,
et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	and then shortly after it coursed through all the body, until it reached the other arm;
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	then she told me that it was turning around the body again and again, just as I saw it.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was greatly amazed at how she moved from member to member in this way, for I had never seen this disease behave in such a manner before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre,	However, I had seen many cases where the pain had moved from place to place.
mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	but never like this, as I saw it in the woman;
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes,	and I thought that it was because the woman had a dry body and her veins were uncovered,
et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	and therefore this windiness appeared constrained;
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	and it does not appear according to this reason in those who are well-nourished, and who have moist bodies and veins that are well-covered.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit,	And when you see this disease being cured, and the patient feels that pain, if it appears as we have said,
si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	then bind above and below hastily, and then pull up until the constrained windiness issues forth from that place;
et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz,	and cauterize the place; and if you do not see it at your eyes,
si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	then treat it with medicines that counteract windiness, such as fetid pills and serpent's tooth pills, and similar others.
Des saiettes	Of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	The arrows are diverse, according to their appearances and according to the places in the body where they strike.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The diversity of their kinds is that there are some with large points, and small, and hairy, and sound;
et de celles qui ont .ij. angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	and those with two angles, and those with tongues, and those which have fragments;
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc .ij. manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit,	and that which strikes a member may strike in two ways: or it pierces the principal member,
si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	such as brain, heart, liver, spleen, kidneys, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When it strikes then in any place of these members, and the sign of death that I shall tell you later appears:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	so it is necessary to beware of the extraction of this arrow, for death comes afterwards in many dispositions;
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	and when this bad sign does not appear to you, and the arrow is not deeply embedded, then extract it and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil,	And the sign of the brain when the arrow strikes and pierces the bone, and the sacric fluid bursts forth which is above the brain,
est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	it is when there is a clouding and darkness and sleepiness and redness in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasms and commotion of understanding, and vomiting of bile;
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	and by chance it is without breath from the nostrils or ears; and by chance it affects speech and voice;
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	and bursts forth from the moist white wound resembling pustules, and also bursts forth like a boil of flesh;
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	and if this sign appears to you, then take care and extract the arrow if it is not deeply embedded.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The sign of the arrow when it strikes the heart is that it is near the left breast and feels as if it were stuck in something hard, not empty;
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	and by chance the arrow moves just like pustules, and there is dark bloody discharge, and comes with cold sweat and chilliness, and syncope:
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	know then without doubt that death is impending.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the arrow that strikes the spleen is when without any foam it bursts forth from the wound, and the throat inflates, and the patient's color changes, and sighs deeply and searches for cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow strikes in the cover of the chest, it is below the small ribs; and there is great pain and great suffering and sighing; and all the members of the shoulders are affected.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow strikes the stomach, by chance something from undigested food bursts forth from the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow strikes the belly and bursts forth through the intestine route, there is no hope for recovery or in the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrow pierces the bladder, and the urine leaps out and comes forth, and the patient feels very great pain: know that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other limb, as the face and neck and throat and shoulder and arm and back of the neck and rib cage and hip and knees and legs, and a similar limb, are safe according to many conditions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in a nerve or an artery and it's not venomous, as I will tell you what happened to me, so that you may do similarly.
Il avint a .i. home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	It happened to one person that an arrow fell into the armpit at the root of the neck:
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I tried to pull it out and pulled it from the other side beneath the fat of the ear, and he was healed without numbness.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz,	And I pulled out an arrow that had fallen into the fat of the eye below the paper-thin skin,
