et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust,	and the arrow was lodged and I couldn't pull it out except for the tip towards the wood.
et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout .i. fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	and the arrow was as big as a Turkish bow, all light iron without any ears; the joint was healed, and no bad accident came to him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And I pulled out an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and the arrow was Arabian with ears:
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I loosened the feathers and pulled it out slowly until I pulled it out, and the Christian was healed.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And I pulled out an arrow from one person who had fallen into his belly, and I thought he was dying;
et puis qu’il ot passez .xxx. jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and then after he had passed 30 days, his condition did not change;
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut into the arrow and extracted it, and he was healed, and there was no bad accident.
Et si vis .i. home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if you find one person who has an arrow stuck in his back, and the wound is sewn up above;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez,	and the arrow remains inside him, and did not change his natural disposition,
ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	nor found any harm in any of his natural works.
Et vis .i. autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And if you find another person who has an arrow stuck in his face, and the wound is sewn up;
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	and remained thus without suffering great pain; and many similar things.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz,	And I pulled out an arrow from one of the king's princes who had fallen into his neck,
et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue	and was slightly leaning to the right side; and the arrow was entirely lodged.
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue .iij. jors. Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I was summoned to the treatment after it had fallen three days. I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I searched for it with all a subtle touch, and did not feel it;
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	and he felt puncturing and pain below his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette	I thought it was from the tip of the arrow
Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I applied a plaster with an attractive and digestive property to the wound, because the flesh did not swell;
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	and I saw the tip of the arrow.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens,	I applied a plaster for many days, and the wound was healed above, and the patient remained thus for a long time,
tant qu’il sentit la saiette .i. jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	until he felt the arrow one day inside his neck; and he told me so.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte,	I applied medicine with a corrosive quality to the wound for many days, until it was fully open,
et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	and I tried to pull it out, and felt the tip of the arrow which was stuck at the root;
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	then I inserted it into the opening of the wound with that corrosive medicine, until the head of the arrow appeared visibly;
et trespassa bien li termines entor .iiij. mois,	and passed well beyond the boundaries for three months,
et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	and then I opened up the wound so that I inserted forceps on both sides, and it could not come out;
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris .i. jor as tenailles bien faites,	then I did not cease to search and extract with the use of instruments, until I grasped it one day with forceps well-made,
selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	according to what its shape will be at the end of this chapter, until I pulled it out and restored the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And the doctor judges that the nasal cartilage cannot be restored:
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I restored it then, and the wound was sewn up, and the patient was completely healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes,	Now I have told you the quality of the extraction of some arrows,
si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	so that you put your care into what I do not say, for books cannot take in everything.
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant,	but wise masters may learn from a small thing, and about what is present and lacking,
trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	find true nine works, and nine instruments, at the descent of strange things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc .ij. manieres:	I say that arrows do not emerge from members where they are stuck except according to two ways:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	or by the way they enter, or by another part;
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	and that which leaps forth from a place where it enters, is an arrow entering into fleshy parts, and sometimes jumps forth now.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it does not jump forth now, then leave it so that the flesh is cleared around, and the exit be freed.
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	and also if it is stuck in the bone and cannot come out, then leave it so for some days, and gently move it each day;
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout .i. foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	and then it jumps forth, and if it does not jump, then pierce around with a subtle instrument, until the flesh around is stretched out, and then pull it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil,	And if the arrow is stuck in the bone of the head, and goes just to one of the vents of the brain,
et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors,	and some of the accidents that I have mentioned appear to the patient: do not pull it out at all, but leave it so for a few days,
car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	for if the arrow comes just to the sacrum, that is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac,	And if the arrow is stuck only in bone and does not come just to the sacrum,
et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	and remains the patient for some days without bad accident, then extract it.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is very stuck and cannot come out at all, then administer poultices around, as I have told you; then care for the wound until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrow is lodged in the flesh of the body so that one cannot see it, then search for it with all diligence;
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	and if you feel it, then pull it out with any suitable instrument;
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette,	and if you cannot due to the narrowness of the wound and the depth of the arrow,
et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	and there is no bone nor nerve nor vein, so one waits until the wound is great;
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient,	and pull out the arrow if you can, and if it has ears on which it holds.
si oste la char qui est ens fichie de .ij. pars au mues que tu pues,	if you remove the flesh that is stuck in two parts to the wound as far as you can.
et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	and then break or bend the ears of the arrow, until you can pull it out.
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	and be subtle that you do not break the arrow, so that you may pull it out more easily.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot pull it out at once, then leave it until the skin around it is rotten, then pull it out, for the extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if the hemorrhaging of blood makes you contraindicated, then follow what we have said about treatment in its chapter.
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril,	and beware of the incision of the nerve and vein, and set your mind to how you can pull out the arrow without peril.
ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens,	or soon or late, or firmly or gently; and place the patient according to the shape he was in when the arrow hit him.
car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	for it is the greatest aid that there can be, and if you cannot do so, then place him according to what the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The arrow that comes from the other side, or it shows anything of him, or the skin is swollen in that place as one sees or feels painfully.
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	cut then above, until the forceps can take hold, and then pull it out: if it jumps forth now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if she is held in the bone, then turn your hand roundly, until she enters the bone, and enlarge the bone, then pull her out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if she cannot come out, then leave her still, and then begin the extraction again until she comes forth.
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	and if the head of the arrow is stuck, then push it all the way through.
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre .i. estrument cheveit,	and if the head falls off, and you wish to administer poulticing, then apply one instrument with a beard.
si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer,	so that the point of the arrow enters the beard of the instrument; and then push it through.
et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute .i. estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	and if the arrow is bearded, then apply one instrument with a pointed end inside, to ease the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues,	And if the arrow is stuck, then it is necessary that you cut away all the flesh around where the venom is, if you can.
puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	then treat the wound as it seems right.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the arrow hits the hip or back or belly or bladder or side, and it is near, and you can cut above, then cut.
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	and be careful not to cut the vein or nerve, and then pull it out, and then dress the wound, if necessary.
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and treat it until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the forceps with which one handles arrows are similar to the beak of a bird, and see here the shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many kinds: great, small, and little, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel,	The shape of the bearded point is also like the feather of a bird.
por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	to push against the point of the arrow, as this is its shape:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the shape of the forceps to push and to grasp if it is thus:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of common veins of the body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont .xxxi., de coi il a ou chef xvi.,	Of veins through which one heals 31, of which it has or 16 head.
c’est a savoir: .ij. batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	that is to say: two batons that are behind the ears, which are called the "herbeches".
et les .ij. arteres qui sont en .ij. temples apparans;	and the two arteries that are in the two temples appearing.
et .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers des .ij. eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	and two veins that are in the two eyes of the two lids, which are called "aspirations".
et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	and the vein that is in the forehead; and the vein that is at the crown of the head.
et les .ij. guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the two jugular veins which are in the neck.
et les .ij. voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the two veins that are on the upper lips of the mouth, and these are the veins that are called "augeherich".
et .ij. voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	and two veins that are below the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont .v. en chescun bras:	The veins through which one usually heals are five in each arm:
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	one is the cerebral vein, and it is on the left side of the chest, and they call it "the vein of the head" among the common people.
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique,	and the middle one is called "faste", and it is composed of the cerebral and basilic veins,
et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit,	and they call it "the vein of the heart" among the common people; and the basilic is on the right side.
et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile,	and they call it "the vein of the belly" among the common people, and it is above the scrotum.
et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	and it is that through which one usually heals, which appears manifestly above the pubic area.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a .ij. rains;	And the saphena vein is the one that is between the ulnar and annular veins, and it has two branches.
et en la jambe et ou piet sont .iij. voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit,	and in the leg and foot are three veins: one is below the crease of the right hip,
et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	and the second saphenous vein that is at the ankle of the left side, and the vein called "nesse" which is in the ankle of the other side.
et en l’autre jambe sont .iij. voinnes desoz celles.	and in the other leg are three veins below those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The treatment of the veins that are behind the ears helps ancient headache and migraines;
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide,	and the quality of the healer, as I tell you, is that you raise the patient's head.
et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis,	and wipe the area where the veins are with a rough cloth; then tighten the patient's neck with a screw.
tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en .ij. leus dependens dou chief:	until the two veins appear behind the ears in two places dependent on the head:
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	which then comes to your hand, and where you feel the pulse beneath your hand, so take hold.
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont,	then take the lancet, and push it through the vein just to the bone, then lift your hand all along the vein upwards.
et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien .ij. dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	and cut and open the skin and the vein well for two fingers' breadth of travel, and let out as much blood as you see fit.
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then tighten it up and bind, until it is healed.
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	and I have already said the incision and cauterization in the first book.
Li sainie des .ij. arteres que sont en .ij. temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene,	The treatment of the two arteries that are in the two temples is good for ancient headaches and migraines.
et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	and also for obtalmia, accustomed to the eyes, and at the very core of old age's tears to the eyes.
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	and the qualities of a physician are such as I say:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent apertement;	and it is that the patient stretches his neck, so that the two veins appear openly;
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	and feels the hairs below your two fingers, and then signs in consent;
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz,	then lift the key on the vein above to your two-fingered index, and push the lancet below,
et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en .ij. autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	and lift the vein above, and cut it, just as you did with the other two veins, and make a hole in the blood according to your necessity;
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	then release the patient, and place your two fingers on the vein for an hour, then place cotton on it;
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	and then bind it tightly, and let it be until it is healed; and we have spoken of their cutting and extraction, as well as the beginning of this book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The bloodletting from the frontal vein is worth as much as the cephalic bloodletting for old face diseases, and for migraine, and for fever;
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	and the quality is that the patient stretches his neck while twisting, until the vein appears;
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	then take the instrument which is called "fossor", whose form is:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	and place the point on the vein, and press down with your hand or something else, and let the blood flow out according to the quantity you see;
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	then release the patient's neck, and tie the vein until it is healed and never once make a wide incision.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, it is not necessary that the incisions be too narrow; and the vein should not cross over, for the bone is near, and by chance the incision may break when it is subtle.
Li sainie des .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The bloodletting of the two veins that are in the armpits is helpful for those with fever, and with typhoid, and with fever in the eye, and for old face diseases;
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	and the quality of their bloodletting is that the patient stretches his neck while twisting without any binding, just as before;
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	then bleed, and let the vein be about an inch long, a little bit wide, because there is no fat.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the incision is subtle, by chance it may break; then make a hole in the blood, as much as you need, and then tie on cotton, and tie it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice,	The bloodletting of the neck vein is worth as much for ague, and for sudden fever, and for old face diseases,
si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	just as migraine and fever that come to the face, and especially when it is old;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre,	and the quality of the bloodletting is that the patient stretches his neck, then strains his neck to your left hand,
et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les .ij. narines,	and take the subtle incision long, and place it inside the lip in the space between the two nostrils,
car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	because the vein does not open well there, and the blood will begin to flow now;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	and do not go too far forward, and let the blood flow according to your necessity, then tie it for a night, because it is very quickly restored;
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	and this is the form of the incision:
Li sainie des .ij. guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The bloodletting of the two inguinal veins is helpful for the constriction of the bladder, and for the beginning of menstruation, and for many diseases, and for epilepsy, and for corrosion, and for herpes, and hemorrhoids;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	and the quality of the bloodletting is that the patient stretches his neck above one and the other, just as we have said;
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus .i. siege,	and let the master be standing on the patient's head, and the patient sit on one seat,
puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	then bleed the long vein a little bit widely, then let the blood flow temperately, or as much as is needed;
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement,	then do the other side in the other vein, then release the ligature, and bind the veins moderately;
que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	so that the patient does not choke; and let it be until morning, when the wound is healed.
De la sainie des leivres	Of the bleeding of the liver
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The bloodletting of the veins above the lips is helpful for bleeding in the mouth, and for corruption of gums, and splits of lips, and around the neck.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And the quality of the bloodletting is to have the patient sit before you, and stretch his neck as I said;
puis torne la levre, et regarde as .ij. voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre,	then turn the lip, and look at the two veins, one of which is on the right lip and the other on the left;
et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	and they can be recognized by their being black, and by the fact that around them are small black veins:
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance,	cut one and the other, and if you do not recognize them, and you are in doubt,
si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des .ij. voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	then cut the largest one from each side, and do the same for the two veins that are above and below, because it is the same method.
De la sainie desoz la lengue	Of the bloodletting under the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	The bloodletting of the veins that are under the tongue is helpful after the cephalic bleeding, and it is for constriction of the throat, and for diseases of the uvula, and for diseases of the mouth;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	and the quality of the bloodletting is that the patient sits between your hands in front of the sun, and lifts his tongue, and looks down on each side to a black vein;
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	then bleed one and the other, and do not go too far forward, because underneath are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc .ij. manieres:	The veins of the neck that are commonly bled are bled in two manners:
ou em poignant a tout .i. flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	or by piercing with one sharp and wide incision, or by making a subtle cut like a trencher cutting, and is called "anesil";
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	and are wide and subtle according to the width and constriction of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the mirtin incision is very renowned, and is wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	And it is necessary to open the veins that are thick and full of gross blood, and contain much blood and turmoil;
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	and this is the form of the olive incision:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is more subtly pointed, and is for bleeding the subtle veins, where there is subtle yellowish blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The bleeding of the basilic vein, which is one of these veins, is helpful for diseases that are below the throat, and on the neck, and on the chest, and on the belly;
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	and it is necessary for the physician to bleed slowly, and beware of the artery that is underneath.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	And if he cuts the artery, and bleeding comes from it, then it is necessary to staunch it, as I said.
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	and should not be pricking at the flame, but cutting like a scythe.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	And if the basilica does not open manifestly, then it is necessary that you extract it and change to another one;
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement;	or you want some air from it, or you open the vein instead of it in the arm: it opens manifestly;
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	and cut into the flame like a scythe, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you want to know the place of the pulse, then it is necessary also that you grasp the arm so that you touch the place until you feel the pulse;
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	then mark the place of the incision and then bind the arm, and cut into the vein like a scythe;
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	and be careful not to hit the artery when you see the place swollen, for it is of the artery: then avoid it.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see it flow up high like the urine of a child, and the blood is red and fine, know that it is blood from the artery:
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	hurry then, and put your finger on top for a long time, then take away your finger if the bleeding stops, which often happens;
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	and bind the arm, and leave it so, and do not move the patient; and be on guard, and do not move him until he is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the blood is not stopped, and he complains, and the medicine is not present to you, then cut into the artery if it opens, for the head of it recedes; and stop the bleeding.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	And take a strip of flax, and cut it, and take one half and bind it well up to the other day;
se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	if the bleeding stops, that's good; if not, then treat him as we have said, with powders that stop blood;
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	and the stopping of bleeding is not hindered in many dispositions for the small size of the wound and the strength of the arm ligament.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz,	The pulse of the vein in the middle helps as much as it treats blood from above the head and below the belly.
por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	because it is composed of the basilica and the cephalic, as we have said;
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf,	and it is necessary for the surgeon to be wary about the nerve that is below, and if he cuts too deeply in front, and he finds the nerve,
et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	and it swells up and the wound is hindered, and by chance cannot heal;
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	and this nerve opens many times, and if it does not open in some men because of its subtlety, then it is necessary that you cut into the wound with an iron like a scythe; and avoid the nerve as best you can.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if he has a vein between the two nerves, then cut it long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The pulse of the cephalic helps, which treats blood from the head and aids the eyes;
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	and it is necessary to treat in puncturing the olive vein or the myrtle vein, for it is the most safe of all veins, because there are no nerves or arteries below.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	However, it is necessary to seek the lighter place and do not trouble anything if one does not take hold at first time, and one begins again;
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	and by chance the places swell up in some men, when one does not take hold at first time, but it does not trouble anything.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the pulse is according to your thinking.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit,	The first thing you should know about healing, is that healing is not most important except for preserving health,
et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	and to avoid diseases from coming;
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des .iij. voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	and let the healing be done in one of the three veins that are opened: namely, the cephalic, the facial, and the basilic;
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	and one should heal at the beginning of prayer time in spring, and after eating in autumn and winter, when the sign of repletion appears;
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés .ij. houres ou .iij. dou jor.	and one should heal on the first or third day, after two or three hours of the day.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The healing that is administered for diseases has no fixed hour or time, but only when need arises by day or night, at all hours and in every moment.
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a .xiiij. ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	and it is not necessary to heal children until they are 14 years old, nor a woman who is pregnant except until the seventh month.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	And one should not heal those who have passed 60 years of age.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier,	And when anyone wants to be healed, however it may be, then it is necessary that he purge the intestines with a light clyster.
s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	if he has a great many foul humors retained, so that the veins do not draw off the superfluities from the intestines, which are hurtful to the principal members;
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	nor does one heal who is too fat from eating meat, or drunk, until they are free of it, nor those with dropsy.
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	and beware when healing after colic passion, and vomiting, and purging of the belly, and frequenting with women, and traveling, watching, and fasting, and all that comes from the whole virtue, or from some part of the arm or body;
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	then subtlely separate the humors, if the blood is thick, through foods and drinks and medicines, if you have the power.
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc,	then enter or take a bath, if nothing hinders it, to subtlety the blood,
et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	and heal from the vein of the kidneys around the third time, as we have said;
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	and guard that day from labor, and toil, and lust, and similar things;
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras .ij. fois ou .iij.,	and be pleased and joyful, and let the healer be more high than he who is being healed, and wipe the arm two or three times.
puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	then stretch the ligament above moderately, for when it is too tight or loose, the blood cannot flow.
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	and then wipe the place with hands, until the veins swell, and one can feel it;
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier,	then moisten the healer's hand with a small amount of old oil, then place his left thumb on that vein below the place where he wants to heal.
que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	so that the vein does not fall and fail when struck.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit,	For there are veins that flow like cords to the healer, and some that are full of windiness.
si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	so that when one puts the oil on it, it draws back the oil, and cannot open up the vein, and thus is one of those.
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	and if it is to open the vein, then the wound is too narrow, therefore it is necessary that the surgeons be aware of these things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein works at the first time, that's good; if not, then it recommences a little below or above quickly, unless the lump is swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse .i. jor ou .ij., et ne liier mie le bras:	And if the lump is swollen and the patient is alarmed, then let it last one or two days and do not bind the arm yet:
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	in case an abscess forms; do not put him in the bath, then recommence the treatment if it pleases him;
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	and if the wound is small, or the blood flows subtly and you doubt that it won't bleed as much as you see, then trust in that very same wound to bleed freely altogether;
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	and work a little quickly, as long as the lump is swollen; for this often happens when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the lump swollen, then do not recommence the treatment, and put a little bit of olive oil on top; for it lightens the body's blood, and is good in this swelling that the oil lies.
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	and thus administer the oil in each treatment that you treat veins, to stop the flow of blood;
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	and this same thing makes a triangle and a bow from the eyes, when it is put on the lump; thus subtlety of blood and separation occurs when it is too large.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite,	And if a big abscess comes, which often happens, especially when it is not treated except at that time or the opening of the vein is small,
si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	so hasten, and put on the lump a damp sponge in water and a little warm oil, and hold it for an hour;
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	and it is necessary that you do this after the blood has flowed from the vein, and if it remains at the lump after some days with any blackness or greenish color, then it does not harm him;
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	and if you see, put on some thing of aloe or myrrh mixed with vinegar, poultice, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And many times an abscess and appearance of the treatment of the basilica occur: put then your hand on it, and if you find the lump soft to the compression of the hand, that is that bad appearance.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore do not put on anything of what we have said, for by chance it may cut off the flow of blood from the artery; but make a dry plaster to harden the lump, then treat it with another treatment until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each blood according to its quantity and virtue, and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the blood is black, let it flow until it turns red; and if you see it thick, let it become thinner; and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And it is necessary for one who is full and strong, and has need of bloodletting by extraction, to make the wound wider and have wide bleeding.
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	and for one who is weak, do the opposite, and let it heal little by little and often, and it should be treated by cutting across, not piercing.
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	and this manner of treatment is safe from the decoration of blood and the cutting of nerves, and is worth more than the treatment of the long or the wide.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc .iij. fois ou .iiij.	And for one whose body needs the treatment, it is necessary to give him moist bread in apple juice; if he is overheated, then treat the blood three or four times.
Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And if he is of cold complexion, then mix before the treatment moist bread in a mixture of musk syrup or aromatic honey with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and cloves, and a well-scented syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil,	And if he vomits after the treatment, after the flow of much blood, then it is necessary that he drinks broth of beef and a subtle, scented syrup.
et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	and use the other things that we have said in the division or chapter of swooning, for the evacuation of blood.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to flex his arm and be healed another time, then it is necessary, when he is weakened by great bloodletting, that he heals little by little, according to the quantity of his continued virtue.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And if he wants to flex his arm after the first treatment, and he has a strong body, then he heals in about 7 hours after the first treatment, or around the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And if he wants to be healed from another part, then he should be treated again on the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	For he has much blood inside the body that is already overheated and causes fever; therefore it is necessary to draw out a great quantity, and enlarge the opening so that it reaches the palate.
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson,	then you will fulfill all the conditions of treatment, and put your hand on the pulse when he is healing, so that death does not come instead of healing.
et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	and this happens many times, when the surgeon is negligent;
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	and it is not necessary when you see the arm separated, and blood flowing out a second time, and the opening is closed, that you press strongly on top;
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	nor if it is crooked, should he stretch his arm quickly, for this would be bad.
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer,	but let him heal the second time; or you will put at the tip of the flow, until the blood that has been congealed at the opening of the vein issues forth,
et met sus .i. poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	and put on one little bit of oil mixed with water, and press on lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, then let it be and do not constrict it, until the abscess is appeased.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if necessity requires drawing blood a second time, then let him bleed in the same place, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein within the arm is treated at the location of the vein of the head because it is composed.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And the manner of treatment is that the patient dips his hand in hot water until the abscess becomes red.
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	then it is tied gently, so that the vein appears well, then he is treated across, not lengthwise or widthwise.
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	and be the opening wide, and be treated well near the joint of the hand, and if blood cannot flow out, then put the hand in hot water, and let the blood flow into the water until you have enough.
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	and if it's in summer, then do not put the hand back in hot water, because one puts more in winter than in summer;
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	and the wound of this vein is more safe than all other veins, for it has no artery or nerve.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	The wound on the thumb side of the right hand is good against all liver diseases, and this is how:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	strain the hand, and soak it in hot water until the swelling subsides, so that it can be seen.
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	and if the wound is across, and you cover it entirely with a cloth, then nothing will trouble it;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char,	and don't go too far in depth, for the nerves are underneath all this denuded flesh,
et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	and then put the hand back in hot water, if the wound is frozen on the skin and cannot emerge.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have bled out as much as is necessary, then put oil and gall on the vein to speed up the healing, and do this for each one.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The wound on the left hand is good against mouse disease, and do everything in the same way as I told you for the right hand.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors,	The wound on the soles of the feet is good against all diseases that are under the body,
si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	such as diseases of the kidneys, and retention of urine, and disease of the reins, and hips, and old legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere,	And the quality of its wound is that the patient dips their foot in hot water and rubs on the vein until it bleeds.
et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	and above the joint of the foot; and the vein is at the ankle, and from there many veins go.
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	heal then the largest vein or the one at the ankle, which is most valuable.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you heal it above the foot, then beware of the nerves that are below, and cut across as when sewing; and let the scar be even.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the blood cannot come out, then put the foot in water and let it drain well from the vein.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if the wound needs to be cleansed the first time, then repeat the second time above a little bit, for the flesh is salty;
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	do not fear the nerves, as we have said, and do this with the soles of both feet equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The flesh of the sciatic vein is at the ankle of strength, and its wound is good against the pain of the backside when it is for hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville .iiij. dois en tordant,	And the quality of its wound is that the patient enters or bathes, and stretches above the ankle 4 fingers while twisting.
car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	for otherwise the vein will not open; and if it opens, then heal it in all ways that you can, and across.
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	and is more valuable than covering it, for the flesh is sound, and it is much recovered in four or five days.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you don't believe it, then heal any vein that opens at the back of the foot or towards the little toe, and beware of the nerves;
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	and let the blood run as you see fit, and then loosen the bandage, and put on a cloth and tighten it; it is now healed.
Des sainies de ventouse	(I'll start translating again)
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Leeches are made from horns, or earth, or glass; and leeching is done in two ways: either by piercing and drawing blood, or without piercing.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	And this leeching that is done without piercing is done in two ways: either it is with fire, or without fire;
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en .xiiij. leus dou cors,	and this leeching that is done by piercing and extracting blood is done in 14 places of the body,
de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col;	of which one is on the whole head and the others are in the neck;
et .ij. autres en .ij. costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	and two others in the two sides of the neck, and the leech below the chin;
et li ventouse des .ij. espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies;	and the leech on the two shoulders, and the leech above the hips;
et les ventouses emmi les .ij. bras; et les ventouses des .ij. jambes;	and the leeches in the two arms, and the leeches in the two legs;
et les ventouses des .ij. chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char,	and the leeches of the two ankles; and this leeching does not treat blood, except for small veins that are scattered in the flesh.
et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	and therefore it is not weakened by any means, just as one makes an incision into a vein;
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	and it is not necessary that it be administered, whether with fire or without fire, in any disease that comes from repletion, until the entire body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if by necessity of diseases it is necessary to bleed, or for habituations, then we should administer each hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and in between and at each time;
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	for there are those who, when they need to bleed, have a heavy head;
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	and there are those who suffer from repletion and redness in their face, and in their head, and neck, and darkness in their eyes;
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	and there are those who suffer from a drop of blood in their mouth, and have swollen the tongue, and redden with blood;
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	and there are those who dream, and see by night's blood and hurt and dead and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and especially when it is in the middle of the month, we order them to bleed after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The purging of the menses helps with the swelling of the head which comes to the eyes, and it is not necessary that this should be done after the evacuation of all the body.
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique,	and this leeching is in place of the purging of the cephalic.
et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	and it is not necessary for those who have a cold complexion to use this, or those who have catharrics, because this does them great harm;
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	and therefore it is not necessary for the elderly to use this, nor those who have cold diseases of the head.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who recover from this often become forgetful, and therefore it is necessary to place the leech a little lower by the fear of forgetfulness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis,	The leeching in the neck is in place of the purging of the head and the cephalic, and therefore it is good for the constriction of the belly.
et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	and to bursting of the channel of the womb, and to all, and to repletion;
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	and it is necessary to push it a little bit, for if it holds too tightly, it will bring forgetfulness or swelling of the stomach and heart.
Li ventosations as .ij. costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens,	The leechings on the two sides of the neck are good for headaches, and obtalmies, and migraines, and for strangulation, and for pain in the roots of the teeth.
et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	and it is in place of the purging of the cephalic; and it is necessary that you instruct the servant to put his hand on top while placing it, so that he does not touch the artery, and does not cause a flow of blood.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	The leechings below the chin are good for mouth diseases, and for corruption of gums, and similar diseases that are in the mouth; and it is in place of purgings of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The leechings on the shoulders are good for the disease that comes from heat and repletion.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des .iij. voinnes dou bras,	The leechings on the ribs are as good as those on the three veins of the arm.
car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	for it draws blood from these large veins;
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	and instruct the servant not to pierce too deeply in front, for the flesh is thin there, and there are nerves and arteries underneath.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The leech that is on the backside is good for hemorrhoids of the fundament, and for diseases below, and it is necessary that the leech be large, and made of earth, so that it can draw well; and by chance, if it were subtle, it would break through; and it could make great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The leeches on the legs clearly purge, for they draw blood from the entire body, and are good for old pains in the reins, and the kidneys, and the bladder, and remove the flowers; and they are in place of the two shins, and the two ankles, and although they weaken the body after long use, and cause numbness in many dispositions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The way to apply the leech is that you should first put it empty, and then suck in a temperate manner, and place it hastily, and move it evenly, and do not stop doing so until you see the spot red and swollen, and appear the redness of the blood; then pierce, and remove the leeches, and take note of the bodily disposition, for there are those who have thick skin, and clear pores: therefore it is necessary to prick only once, and make large wounds, and a little deep; and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the blood is thick, it is necessary to prick twice: the first time to make a fine opening for the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the blood is very thick, it is necessary to prick a third time; and when we want to draw out the blood a little at a time, we only need to do so once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement,	And if we want a lot of blood, we often restart; and if the blood is thick, we prick deep, and the end result is that the veins are pierced suddenly.
et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	and it is necessary for those who have thick skin and hard, and who have large pores, that you anoint the spots where the leeches are with oil that is appetizing and dissolving:
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	if it is in summer, with violet oil, or with sweet almond oil, or with pumpkin seed oil.
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	and if it is in winter, with oil of balm, or of lily, or of chamomile, or another similar one.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the surplus is thick and cold, take bitter oil, or balsamic oil, or oil of anise, and similar ones.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile,	And if one is being treated for tender skin and large pores, there is no need to apply oil.
mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	but it is necessary to wash afterwards with water of red vinegar, or cold water, or water of mulberry, or water of cucumber, or water of porphyry, or another similar one.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And that person who has much moisture, should rise easily with water of myrtle, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And those who have large superfluities should rise with old wine, or water of sage, or a decoction of anise or chamomile, or other similar things.
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou .ij.; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion,	and it is not necessary to apply a poultice before the bath or after the bath, but rather an hour or two hours after the bath; and do not sleep at all after the purging.
et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	and it is necessary for him to be warned when he should purge and when he is purged.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	And beware of those who are being treated are choleric, and the skin is too rough and inflamed.
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	so it is necessary for him to take cold things, such as green grapes and endive and lettuce at ease, and similar things.
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	and boiled meats, and the flesh of kid, and moist game.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And that person who has a cold complexion, should take honey syrup, and aromatic wine of middle age, which is between old and new, and boiled meats, and boiled fowl, and small game birds.
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	and the day when he will purge, he should drink more than eat;
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	and it is necessary to give some men sometimes treacle or musk at the time of purging, or afterwards, in order to comfort the main members;
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	and let it be subtle and thin, but it is not necessary that those who are hot should drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz,	The poultices that are applied without striking pain are those that are applied on the liver, and on the kidneys, and podagra, and on the belly and the navel and the reins and the hip, for these members do not tolerate being struck with blows.
et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre,	and one does this only to draw blood from member to member.
si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus lou ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	as we do on the breasts when the milk is flowing; to remove the viscosity that is in the member, as we apply poultices on the belly and navel to reduce the swelling.
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	and it removes the pain when there is an abscess or a stone, and it removes by its attractive power either the abscess or dislodges the stone from its place.
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue,	and thus it does when one applies it on the liver and kidneys when there is retained flatulence.
et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede,	and these poultices are administered empty to suck up as much as possible; and sometimes they are administered with fire, and sometimes filled with cold water.
si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	as in cases of catarrah, and in such a way that one fills the poultice with hot water or with water in which herbs suitable for this purpose have been boiled.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The shape of the poultice administered at fire is this:
Et ait .ij. dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu .i. petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille,	And it has two fingers of width and half a palm in depth, and on the border around the middle one small perforation, just as for pushing in a needle.
et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	and it is of earth, softened beforehand so that it does not hurt the patient when applied to the member.
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise,	and in the middle a bar of earth or iron, for putting a candle inside.
et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	and there are both large and small ones according to the diseases and age of those who take them;
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	for the poultices for children are different from those for old people, and for thin people than for fat ones.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And one should thus apply this poultice to the member:
empren la chandoile de cire ou .i. linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse,	take a candle of wax or a linen thread, and put it inside the poultice across the bar that is inside the poultice,
si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	so that the light may be at the bottom of the poultice and not burn the patient.
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	and then put it on the member, and have the two fingers on the perforation that we said, so that when one wants, the steam may go out, and remove the poultice.
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	and take the linen thread as before, and repeat it often if you need to.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	In the poultice then which is administered in cases of catarrah, it has no bar or perforation, and is applied only when it is full of water, and is put on the member just once.
et c’est li forme:	and that's the shape:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	Withoutuses are applied only in places where one cannot apply poultices because of their smallness, such as lips and gums, and similar areas;
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	and on bare areas of skin, such as the head or neck, and other similar ones.
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	and the quality of the user is that when you find withoutuses that are in sweet waters free from putridity, then take them.
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	and put them into fresh water, until they are familiar and have nothing in their bellies;
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	and then be cleansed with wine and poultice, then rub the member until it is red, and apply the withoutuses.
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	and when they are full and firm, if it is a place where one can apply a poultice, then do so, for this is very good afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If not, then lift the place gently with water, very well, and then stretch it;
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille .i. drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	and if the place is healing too close to the body of the withoutuses, then wet a linen cloth with cold water and apply it, until the withoutus are shrunk.
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	and if the withoutus are multiplied, then apply vitriolized oil, or gall, and similar things, until it is shrunk.
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	or you put half a handful of peeled peas on the place and leave them until they dry out at the place, which will now be shrunk.
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	and if you need more, then take other withoutuses.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse,	And if the withoutus do not want to be taken, then rub the place with fresh blood, or stick a needle in it until the withoutus come out.
et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	and then apply them and as soon as they feel the blood, they will dry up.
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	and when you see that they are falling, then powder on a little bit of alum and powdered silk, or ash, so that they will now stick.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	This begins the book of fractures.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is many times necessary in the art of medicine, and is a treatment for fracture and desiccation.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Here is the translation:
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	and therefore is estranged the art in our land, for I never found a good one;
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	and I know nothing, except by the science of ancient books, where I have studied so much that I have treated the science, and by experiment, and by the habituation of my life;
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces .ij. chapistres ci devant.	and I have described to you in this chapter what is contained, and I have abbreviated it at the end, and shown clearly the forms of instruments that are brought forth, as I have done in these two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.
